Onboarding guide

18. ADC Conference - Application & Use Cases

What this chapter covers. This is the application layer of the Conference module, the largest single application assembly in the codebase (over 180 types). It sits between the REST/gRPC edge (G20, Conference API & gRPC) and the domain aggregates (G17, Conference Domain), and it is where the conference's use cases actually live: create an event, publish it, add a room or a speaker, import the whole agenda from Sessionize.com, and run the AI-assisted analytics that help organizers decide which session proposals to accept. Everything here is engine-agnostic and framework-light, it depends on the abstractions introduced by MMCA.Common.Application (handlers, mappers, validators, query services, navigation populators) and on the Conference domain, but never on EF, ASP.NET, or a broker SDK directly. Read the primer's tour of CQRS and Vertical Slice first; this chapter shows those styles at full scale in one module.

The vertical-slice anatomy of a use case

Open any feature folder under Sessions/UseCases/, Events/UseCases/, Speakers/UseCases/, Categories/UseCases/, or Questions/UseCases/ and you will find the same cohesive slice: a command or query record, its handler, its FluentValidation validator, and (for creates) a request record plus a request mapper, all co-located. Adding a feature means adding a folder, not threading an edit through horizontal Services/, Validators/, and Repositories/ directories. This is the Vertical Slice discipline made physical. [Rubric §5, Vertical Slice] (assesses whether a feature is one navigable unit rather than scattered horizontally), and the folder layout is the evidence.

A command mutates and returns a Result; a query is side-effect-free and returns a Result<TDTO>. Both implement the Common contracts ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> and IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult>, so every handler in this assembly flows through the same decorator pipeline (Logging → Caching → Transactional → handler) without knowing it exists. Commands that change cached read data implement ICacheInvalidating; commands that must be atomic implement ITransactional. The controller injects the handler interface and calls HandleAsync; the concrete type is invisible to it. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses a clean command/query split through well-defined handler boundaries), this module is the canonical demonstration: dozens of single-responsibility handlers, each one slice wide, all dispatched uniformly.

The CRUD-shaped handlers, CreateEventHandler, CreateSessionHandler, CreateSpeakerHandler, CreateQuestionHandler, CreateConferenceCategoryHandler, and the matching Update*/Delete*/Add*/ Remove* families, share one shape: they delegate object construction to an IEntityRequestMapper (which runs the validator and the domain Create(...) factory, returning Result<TEntity>), then persist through IUnitOfWork and map the saved entity back to a DTO with an IEntityDTOMapper. The handler owns orchestration only, load, validate, persist, map, log, while the business rule ("an event's end date can't precede its start date") lives in the domain factory and the invariant classes. The richer handlers (UpdateSessionHandler, UpdateEventHandler) add optimistic-concurrency stamping (SetOriginalRowVersion), immutable-field guards that return Error.UnprocessableEntity, and cross-aggregate reads (fetching the parent Event read-only to check a room-vs-event constraint), concerns that genuinely need orchestration context, deliberately kept out of the entity.

Manual mapping, validation rule fragments, and authorization specifications

Three sibling families recur across every aggregate. DTO mappers (SessionDTOMapper, EventDTOMapper, SpeakerDTOMapper, RoomDTOMapper, CategoryItemDTOMapper, and the question-answer/category-item link mappers) implement the Common mapper contract and assign each field by hand, the deliberate choice of ADR-001 (manual/Mapperly mapping over reflection-based AutoMapper) so a renamed property is a compile error, not a silent null. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses explicit, traceable contracts), the mapping is code you can read and test, not convention magic.

Validation is composed, not inherited. Small generic rule fragments, EventDateRangeRules<T>, EventNameRules<T>, RoomCapacityRules<T>, SessionTitleRules<T>, SpeakerFirstNameRules<T>, CategoryItemNameRules<T>, and a dozen siblings, each encapsulate one validated concern as an AbstractValidator<T> taking a property selector, and the per-use-case validators (EventUpdateRequestValidator, SessionCreateRequestValidator, …) pull them together with FluentValidation's Include(...). The pattern mirrors MMCA.Common.Application's CommonValidationRules approach; EventDateRangeRules<T> is the richest, compiling the StartDate selector into a delegate and reading it inside a cross-property Must on EndDate. [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] and [Rubric §1, SOLID] (fragments compose without an inheritance chain; a new constraint is a new fragment, touching no existing validator).

Authorization specifications: PublishedEventSpecification, OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification, OwnSessionQuestionAnswerSpecification, are ISpecification<TEntity, TIdentifierType> implementations passed into the query services to scope what a caller may read (e.g. an anonymous visitor sees only published events; a speaker sees only their own answers). This keeps the authorization predicate as a reusable, testable expression rather than an if buried in a controller. [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses authorization that is data-scoped, not just endpoint-gated). The public-session visibility rule, which once lived in a PublicSessionSpecification, is now produced by the GetPublicSessionFilterHandler use case via the cross-source CrossSourceSpecification helper, because Session may live in a different data source from Event (ADR-018) and the published-event check can no longer be a navigation join.

Query services, navigation populators, and the composition root

Read paths do not get bespoke handlers for the common cases, they go through the framework's generic IEntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>, which supplies filtering, sorting, paging, and field projection. The one local specialization is SpeakerEntityQueryService, a thin subclass that adds a property map so API consumers can sort/filter on the computed FullName while the pipeline translates it to (FirstName + " " + LastName) in SQL. Eager-loading of child graphs is delegated to per-aggregate INavigationPopulator<in TEntity> implementations, EventNavigationPopulator, SessionNavigationPopulator, SpeakerNavigationPopulator, ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator, which encapsulate which navigations to include and how to batch-load cross-source relationships (ADR-002); child entities use the framework's NullNavigationPopulator<TEntity> because they are never the root of a full graph load.

All of this is wired by DependencyInjection, the module's composition root. It explicitly binds the closed generics Scrutor can't infer (each aggregate's query service, navigation populator, and delete handler) and then calls ScanModuleApplicationServices<ClassReference>() to discover the "many small things" (every handler, mapper, validator, and event handler) by convention. AssemblyReference and ClassReference are the marker types that anchor that scan. [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (assesses clean, explicit module boundaries), every internal concrete type is reachable only through an interface registered here, which is exactly what lets the Conference module boot as its own service host. [Rubric §33, Developer Experience], one file is the single place a new aggregate gets registered.

Event-driven reactions: domain and integration handlers

The application layer is also where the module reacts to events. Domain event handlers, SessionCreatedHandler, SpeakerDeletedHandler, RoomChangedHandler, implement IDomainEventHandler<in TDomainEvent> and run in-process after the aggregate's SaveChangesAsync, handling intra-module side effects (e.g. cascading cleanup when a speaker is removed). The integration event handler UserRegisteredHandler implements IIntegrationEventHandler<in TIntegrationEvent> and is the cross-module seam: when Identity publishes UserRegistered over the broker, Conference auto-links a speaker to that user (BR-207), trying an email match first and then a unique-name fallback for Sessionize-imported speakers whose Email is null (the public Sessionize feed omits PII), and publishing SpeakerLinkedToUser back to Identity on a hit (MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Users/IntegrationEventHandlers/UserRegisteredHandler.cs:59-107). The handler is deliberately best-effort: a broker redelivery is deduped by the consumer inbox (ADR-021), it runs in its own DI scope because the handler is a singleton, and any failure is swallowed so the already-committed registration never rolls back (UserRegisteredHandler.cs:109-114). The reciprocal direction, Conference telling Identity about speaker links, flows through the IMessageBus abstraction and the outbox (ADR-003), so the application code never references MassTransit. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness], the module collaborates through events and interfaces, never direct cross-module type references. SessionBookmarkValidationService and EventLiveValidationService are the in-process implementations of the Engagement-facing contracts (ISessionBookmarkValidationService and IEventLiveValidationService), which Engagement calls via gRPC when the modules run as separate services (ADR-007): the former gates session bookmarking (BR-49/BR-91), the latter computes an event or session live window in UTC (plus the assigned speakers and the question-moderation default) for the conference-day live layer. SpeakerEntityQueryService and GetSessionBookmarkCountQuery/GetSessionFeedbackQuery round out the speaker-facing read surface.

The Sessionize import: Strategy-pattern orchestration

The single most involved use case is importing a conference agenda from Sessionize.com. Sessionize returns one JSON payload covering five interdependent entity families, categories, rooms, questions, speakers, and sessions (sessions reference rooms and speakers; speakers reference categories). The HTTP shape is captured by a set of deserialization records (SessionizeResponse, SessionizeSession, SessionizeSpeaker, SessionizeRoom, SessionizeCategory, SessionizeCategoryItem, SessionizeQuestion, SessionizeQuestionAnswer, SessionizeLink) confined entirely to this layer, an anti-corruption boundary so a Sessionize API change never touches a domain entity, which carries no [JsonPropertyName] attributes.

The import is fetched through the ISessionizeService port (implemented by the HTTP client in G19, Conference Infrastructure) and orchestrated by RefreshFromSessionizeHandler. That handler does orchestration only: load the Event with its rooms and speakers eagerly, enforce BR-6 (a Sessionize code must be configured) and the BR-63 five-minute throttle, call the external API inside a try/catch(HttpRequestException) that converts a network failure into an Error (the Result pattern absorbing the exception), then fan out to five ISessionizeSyncStrategy implementations in dependency order, CategorySyncStrategy, RoomSyncStrategy, QuestionSyncStrategy, SpeakerSyncStrategy, SessionSyncStrategy, each carrying its work via a shared SessionizeSyncContext and returning a SessionizeSyncResult count. Each strategy bulk-loads its entity family in one GetByIdsAsync (no N+1), upserts via the domain's Create/Update methods, skips soft-deleted rows (BR-136), and accumulates warnings instead of aborting on one bad record. A final RequestIdentityInsert() lets SQL Server accept Sessionize's own integer IDs before one batched SaveChangesAsync. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns] (Strategy used to solve a real Open/Closed problem, a new entity family is a new strategy, not an edit to the orchestrator), [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (bulk loads + a single save round-trip), and [Rubric §17, DevOps & Deployment] (the throttle and graceful per-entity degradation make a re-import safe to run repeatedly).

Decision support: AI scoring and content analytics

The last cluster is session-selection decision support, analytics that help organizers triage proposals. GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler is a composite query: it loads sessions, speakers, and categories once, then computes category distribution, speaker-session overlap, content similarity, and speaker locality in a single pass, returning one dashboard DTO (the underlying queries, GetCategoryDistributionQuery, GetContentSimilarityQuery, GetSpeakerSessionOverlapQuery, are also dispatchable individually). Content similarity is computed by the pure-static SessionSimilarityCalculator, a weighted Jaccard index over category tags (60%) and span-tokenized keywords (40%, with a FrozenSet stop-word filter) above a tunable threshold (default 0.3), flagging proposals that would compete for the same audience. SpeakerLocalityHelper resolves whether a speaker is local via a category item (the locality is tracked as a CategoryItem, not a Speaker field), and the two private per-handler StatusBucket enums map SessionStatuses into display groupings.

The flagship is AI scoring. ScoreEventSessionsCommand (handled by ScoreEventSessionsHandler) fans every eligible, not-yet-scored session out to IAiScoringService, a port implemented in infrastructure by AnthropicScoringService, which calls the Anthropic Messages API. The contract is deliberately never-throw: ScoreSessionAsync returns a SessionScoringResult with a Success flag and seven 1.0–10.0 sub-scores (overall, topic relevance, description quality, novelty, actionable takeaways, depth/insight, credibility) in all cases, so one bad session never aborts the scoring loop. The input shapes are SessionScoringInput and SpeakerInfo; the result is mapped to a Conference.Shared DTO for persistence. Keeping the port here and the HTTP/LLM adapter in infrastructure is textbook [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (the application layer depends on an interface, never the SDK) and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (the AI provider is swappable behind one interface).

Taken together, this assembly is the codebase's most complete picture of how a use case is built here: a slice per feature, generic framework machinery for the repetitive 80% (query, validate, map, persist, populate), and bespoke handlers reserved for the genuinely complex 20%, the Sessionize import and the decision-support analytics, each isolated behind a port or a strategy so it can evolve, be tested, and ultimately be extracted without disturbing the rest.

AssemblyReference, ClassReference

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/AssemblyReference.cs:5 · Level 0 · class (static) + class

  • What it is: the assembly-marker pair for MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application. AssemblyReference is a static class exposing the layer's Assembly and AssemblyName; ClassReference is an empty non-static class used purely as a generic type argument for assembly scanning. Neither carries behavior.
Type File:Line Notes
AssemblyReference MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/AssemblyReference.cs:5 static class; Assembly + AssemblyName fields
ClassReference MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/AssemblyReference.cs:11 empty marker class; the T in ScanModuleApplicationServices<ClassReference>()
  • Depends on: System.Reflection only (BCL). No first-party types.
  • Concept introduced, the assembly-marker pair. Every module layer ships this same two-type pair so that DI/EF scanning can reference "this assembly" without a magic string or a fragile Assembly.Load. AssemblyReference.Assembly is computed as typeof(AssemblyReference).Assembly (AssemblyReference.cs:7), the type is its own locator, so the value can never drift from the project it lives in. ClassReference exists because Scrutor's generic scan entry point (ScanModuleApplicationServices<T>()) keys off the assembly of a type parameter, and a dedicated empty class avoids accidentally pinning the scan to some real domain type whose location could move. [Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality] (assesses idiomatic, low-ceremony conventions): a one-line, copy-identical marker pair per layer is cheaper and safer than hand-passing Assembly instances around.
  • Walkthrough: Assembly is a static readonly field set once at type-init (:7); AssemblyName reads Assembly.GetName().Name ?? string.Empty (:8), null-coalescing because AssemblyName.Name is technically nullable. ClassReference is public class ClassReference { } (:11), no members.
  • Why it's built this way: see "Concept introduced". The pair is duplicated in every MMCA.ADC.*.Application/.Infrastructure/.Domain layer rather than shared, because each must resolve to its own assembly; a shared base type would resolve to the wrong assembly.
  • Where it's used: ClassReference is the type argument to ScanModuleApplicationServices<ClassReference>() inside DependencyInjection (DependencyInjection.cs:97), telling Scrutor which assembly to scan for handlers, mappers, and validators. Sibling pairs exist in Conference.Domain and Conference.Infrastructure.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the prior tier section described this as feeding "MediatR handler discovery"; that is stale. This codebase uses Scrutor convention scanning, not MediatR, there is no MediatR reference anywhere in the Conference Application project.

CategoryItemSortRules<T>, CategoryItemNameRules<T>, ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T>

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.Validation · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/Validation/ConferenceCategoryValidationRules.cs:12 · Level 0 / Level 6 · classes (sealed)

  • What it is: three reusable FluentValidation rule fragments for the Conference Category aggregate. Each is a generic AbstractValidator<T> parameterized on the owning request/command type, takes a property-selector expression in its constructor, and encapsulates exactly one validated concern (title text, category-item name, sort order). They are composed into full Create/Update validators via Include(...) rather than re-stating the rules per command.
Type File:Line Level Selector What it validates
CategoryItemSortRules<T> ConferenceCategoryValidationRules.cs:39 0 Expression<Func<T,int>> sort order >= 0
CategoryItemNameRules<T> ConferenceCategoryValidationRules.cs:26 6 Expression<Func<T,string>> non-empty; <= CategoryItemNameMaxLength
ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T> ConferenceCategoryValidationRules.cs:12 6 Expression<Func<T,string>> non-empty; <= TitleMaxLength

The level split is real: CategoryItemSortRules<T> validates a bare int with no first-party dependency (Level 0), while the other two read max-length constants from CategoryInvariants in the Conference Domain layer (Level 5), which lifts them to Level 6. They share one file and one shape, so they are taught together here.

  • Depends on: FluentValidation.AbstractValidator<T>, System.Linq.Expressions.Expression<> (externals). CategoryItemNameRules<T> and ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T> additionally depend on CategoryInvariants for TitleMaxLength / CategoryItemNameMaxLength.
  • Concept introduced, composable validation rule fragments. [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (assesses server-side validation that mirrors the domain's constraints) and [Rubric §1, SOLID] (DRY/OCP, a rule defined once is reused, and adding a constraint never edits an existing validator). Instead of each command validator hand-writing "title not empty, title length ≤ N", the constraint lives in one generic fragment; a parent validator pulls it in with Include(new ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<UpdateCategoryCommand>(x => x.Title)). The selector is an Expression<Func<T, …>> so the same fragment applies to whichever command/request property holds the title. Crucially, the max-length values come from the domain (CategoryInvariants), so the request-layer message ("…cannot be longer than N characters") can never disagree with the entity-level invariant, one source of truth for the limit. Cross-reference the framework-level rule-fragment pattern in CommonValidationRules (MMCA.Common.Application).
  • Walkthrough: each is a sealed class … : AbstractValidator<T> whose constructor is an expression body that calls RuleFor(selector) and chains rules:
    • ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T> (:12-19): .NotEmpty() with message "You must enter a Category Title", then .MaximumLength(CategoryInvariants.TitleMaxLength) with an interpolated message naming the limit.
    • CategoryItemNameRules<T> (:26-33): identical shape against CategoryInvariants.CategoryItemNameMaxLength.
    • CategoryItemSortRules<T> (:39-45): .GreaterThanOrEqualTo(0), the simplest fragment, no domain constant needed.
  • Why it's built this way: rule fragments compose without an inheritance hierarchy: an update-category validator can Include title + item-name + sort independently. This is the same fragment pattern used across the module (see the Event/Room/Session rule families in the broader Conference Application set).
  • Where it's used: Include-d by the Category Create/Update command validators (Conference Application), which are discovered by Scrutor via DependencyInjection; the resulting validators run inside the CQRS validation decorator pipeline (primer §2).

SessionizeCategoryItem, SessionizeLink, SessionizeQuestion, SessionizeQuestionAnswer, SessionizeRoom

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Sessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Sessionize/SessionizeModels.cs:60 · Level 0 · records (sealed)

  • What it is: five leaf deserialization records that model the simplest shapes returned by the Sessionize "View All" conference API. Each is a sealed record of primitive/string fields carrying [JsonPropertyName] mappings; they hold no first-party references, which is what keeps them at Level 0. They are the bottom of the Sessionize import model tree (the composite SessionizeResponse and its mid-level children build on them).
Type File:Line Fields
SessionizeCategoryItem SessionizeModels.cs:60 Id (int), Name, Sort
SessionizeRoom SessionizeModels.cs:73 Id (int), Name, Sort
SessionizeQuestion SessionizeModels.cs:25 Id (int), Question, QuestionType, Sort
SessionizeQuestionAnswer SessionizeModels.cs:195 QuestionId (int), AnswerValue
SessionizeLink SessionizeModels.cs:126 Title, Url, LinkType
  • Depends on: System.Text.Json.Serialization attributes only. No first-party types.
  • Concept introduced, the anti-corruption deserialization model. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] and [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (a foreign schema must not leak inward). The Sessionize JSON shape is captured in dedicated Application-layer records at the integration edge; the domain entities never carry [JsonPropertyName] and never see Sessionize field names. The import strategies translate these records into Category/Room/Question/etc. so a Sessionize API change touches only these records and their strategies, the textbook anti-corruption layer. [Rubric §32, Dependency & Supply-Chain] (defensive deserialization of an external feed) also applies: every collection-typed property defaults to [] so a partial or absent JSON node deserializes safely.
  • Walkthrough: all five are public sealed record with init-only properties; string fields default to string.Empty so a missing JSON node never yields null. Notable details:
    • SessionizeLink.Url carries [SuppressMessage("Design", "CA1056")] (:131), a URL is deliberately deserialized as a string (not Uri) to round-trip whatever Sessionize sends; the suppression is justified inline ([Rubric §15, Best Practices]: suppressions are explained, not blanket).
    • SessionizeQuestionAnswer (:195-202) is the only two-field record and appears on both sessions and speakers (it is referenced from SessionizeSpeaker and SessionizeSession).
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the wire schema in tiny leaf records at the Application edge isolates the blast radius of an upstream API change to this one file plus the sync strategies.
  • Where it's used: nested inside the larger Sessionize records (SessionizeCategory contains SessionizeCategoryItem; SessionizeSpeaker contains SessionizeLink + SessionizeQuestionAnswer) and ultimately under SessionizeResponse; consumed by the ISessionizeSyncStrategy implementations during the conference import (Conference Application UseCases, covered in the handler unit).

SessionizeCategory, SessionizeSession, SessionizeSpeaker

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Sessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Sessionize/SessionizeModels.cs:41 · Level 1 · records (sealed)

  • What it is: three mid-level Sessionize deserialization records. Each is a sealed record that, unlike the Level-0 leaves, references one or more of those leaves (which is what pulls them to Level 1). Together they carry the bulk of an imported conference's data.
Type File:Line Notable fields References (Level 0 leaves)
SessionizeCategory SessionizeModels.cs:41 Id, Title, Sort, Type?, Items SessionizeCategoryItem
SessionizeSpeaker SessionizeModels.cs:86 Id (Guid), FirstName, LastName, Bio?, TagLine?, IsTopSpeaker, Sessions (int ids), CategoryItems (int ids) SessionizeLink, SessionizeQuestionAnswer
SessionizeSession SessionizeModels.cs:140 Id, Title, Description?, StartsAt?, EndsAt?, Speakers (Guid ids), CategoryItems (int ids), RoomId?, Status?, IsInformed, IsConfirmed SessionizeQuestionAnswer
  • Depends on: System.Text.Json.Serialization; the Level-0 leaf records above. No domain types.
  • Concept introduced: these continue the anti-corruption deserialization pattern taught in the leaf-record section; here the notable mechanics are cross-referencing by ID and defensive number handling:
    • References between Sessionize entities are by ID, not object graph. SessionizeSpeaker.Sessions/CategoryItems and SessionizeSession.Speakers/CategoryItems/RoomId are lists of ids (int/Guid), mirroring how the Sessionize feed denormalizes its graph. The sync strategies resolve these ids into domain relationships during import.
    • SessionizeSession.Id is [JsonNumberHandling(JsonNumberHandling.AllowReadingFromString)] (:143), a real-world robustness detail: Sessionize occasionally serializes session ids as JSON strings, and this attribute accepts both numeric and string forms transparently. [Rubric §32, Dependency & Supply-Chain] (defensive integration with a third-party feed whose contract is not under our control).
    • SessionizeSession.LiveUrl/RecordingUrl carry the same CA1056 suppression as SessionizeLink.Url, URLs deserialized as strings on purpose (:176, :180).
  • Walkthrough: all three are public sealed record, init-only, with [JsonPropertyName("camelCase")] on every property and []/string.Empty defaults so a partial response is safe. SessionizeSpeaker.Id is a Guid (Sessionize uses GUID speaker ids) while sessions/categories/rooms use int ids, a distinction the import strategies must respect when joining.
  • Why it's built this way: modeling the feed's denormalized, id-linked shape faithfully (rather than pre-joining during deserialization) keeps the records a literal mirror of the JSON, which is what makes them easy to verify against the live API and cheap to maintain.
  • Where it's used: aggregated by SessionizeResponse; consumed by the ISessionizeSyncStrategy implementations (one per entity type) invoked from RefreshFromSessionizeHandler (handler unit).

SessionizeResponse

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Sessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Sessionize/SessionizeModels.cs:6 · Level 2 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the top-level deserialization shape for the Sessionize "View All" API response, aggregating the imported categories, rooms, speakers, sessions, and questions into one object.
  • Depends on: the Level-1 records SessionizeCategory, SessionizeSession, SessionizeSpeaker and the Level-0 SessionizeRoom/SessionizeQuestion (all in the same file), referencing the Level-1 records is what makes this aggregate Level 2.
  • Concept introduced: this is the root of the anti-corruption deserialization tree introduced in the leaf-record section. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] / [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]: the entire external Sessionize JSON schema is captured at the application edge, so the foreign schema never leaks into the domain; the sync strategies translate this object into domain entities.
  • Walkthrough: five IReadOnlyList<…> properties, Categories, Rooms, Speakers, Sessions, Questions (:8-21), each [JsonPropertyName]-mapped and defaulting to [] so a partial response deserializes without nulls.
  • Why it's built this way: isolating the whole wire schema in one root record (plus its children) means a Sessionize API change touches only this file and the sync strategies, never the aggregates.
  • Where it's used: returned by ISessionizeService.GetAllAsync and consumed by the ISessionizeSyncStrategy implementations during the conference import (handler unit).

ISessionizeService

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Sessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Sessionize/ISessionizeService.cs:6 · Level 3 · interface

  • What it is: the application-layer port for fetching a conference's full dataset from the Sessionize "View All" API. One method: Task<SessionizeResponse?> GetAllAsync(string sessionizeCode, CancellationToken).
  • Depends on: SessionizeResponse (its return type); System.Threading (CancellationToken). The concrete SessionizeService (Conference Infrastructure) implements it with the actual HttpClient call.
  • Concept introduced, the port/adapter seam (hexagonal architecture). [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (the Application layer depends on an interface, never a concrete HTTP client): defining the Sessionize dependency as a one-method interface in the Application layer, with the HTTP implementation living in Infrastructure, is the inward-pointing dependency rule made concrete, the import handler is testable with a fake, and the transport (HTTP today, anything later) is swappable without touching the use case. The string sessionizeCode parameter (e.g. "kqf8l42a") is the Sessionize event code that selects which conference to pull.
  • Walkthrough: a single declaration (ISessionizeService.cs:12): GetAllAsync takes the event code and an optional CancellationToken (the codebase convention: cancellation token is always the last parameter), and returns a nullable SessionizeResponse, null signals an empty/absent response so the handler can short-circuit rather than treating "no data" as an exception.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the external feed behind an interface lets the import use case be unit-tested without a network and lets the concrete client carry its own resilience policy (retry/timeout via the standard resilience handler, ADR-009) at the Infrastructure edge.
  • Where it's used: injected into the RefreshFromSessionizeHandler (Conference Application UseCases, handler unit); the concrete SessionizeService is registered in Conference Infrastructure DI.

DependencyInjection

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/DependencyInjection.cs:34 · Level 11 · class (static)

  • What it is: the Conference module's application-layer composition root: a static class with a single extension(IServiceCollection) method, AddModuleConferenceApplication(ApplicationSettings), that wires every Application service the module needs, explicit registrations for the closed-generic services Scrutor cannot infer, plus one convention scan for everything else.
  • Depends on: a wide swath of Conference Application/Domain/Shared types plus framework abstractions: INavigationPopulator<in TEntity>, NullNavigationPopulator<TEntity>, IEntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>, EntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>, ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>, DeleteEntityCommand<TEntity, TIdentifierType>, DeleteEntityHandler<TEntity, TIdentifierType>, Result, ApplicationSettings, ClassReference, and the module's own DeleteEventHandler, EventNavigationPopulator, SessionNavigationPopulator, SpeakerNavigationPopulator, ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator, SpeakerEntityQueryService, SessionBookmarkValidationService (built in later Conference Application units), the Domain services IEventCascadeDeletionDomainService/EventCascadeDeletionDomainService and the cross-module ISessionBookmarkValidationService. Notable externals: Microsoft.Extensions.DependencyInjection (IServiceCollection, TryAddSingleton, TryAddScoped) and Scrutor (ScanModuleApplicationServices<ClassReference>).
  • Concept introduced, the module composition root. [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (modules with clean, explicit service boundaries): the composition root is what gives the module its boundary, nothing outside Conference can reach its internal concretes, because callers resolve only the interfaces bound here. [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]: every registration binds an interface to a concrete; consumers depend on the interface. [Rubric §33, Developer Experience & Inner Loop]: a single method holding every non-convention registration means a developer adding an aggregate has exactly one file to edit. The C# extension(IServiceCollection) syntax (:36) is the codebase-wide DI idiom, see primer §4.
  • Walkthrough
    • Signature (:36-39): AddModuleConferenceApplication(ApplicationSettings applicationSettings) inside an extension(IServiceCollection services) block. The settings parameter is received then discarded, _ = applicationSettings; with comment "Reserved for future use (e.g., profiler decorators)" (:40).
    • Domain service (:43): IEventCascadeDeletionDomainService → EventCascadeDeletionDomainService, registered Singleton (stateless logic).
    • Aggregate roots with custom navigation populators (:46-60): Event, Session, Speaker, Category. Each gets three scoped registrations, a custom INavigationPopulator<T>, an IEntityQueryService<T, TDTO, TId>, and an ICommandHandler<DeleteEntityCommand<T, TId>, Result>. Event and Speaker deviate: Event's delete handler is the custom DeleteEventHandler (:48) because cascade deletion needs domain-service logic, and Speaker's query service is the custom SpeakerEntityQueryService (:55); the rest use the generic implementations.
    • Aggregate roots with no child navigations (:63-65): Question, same trio but with NullNavigationPopulator<Question> (no eager-load paths).
    • Child entities (:68-90): Room, CategoryItem, EventSpeaker, EventQuestionAnswer, SessionSpeaker, SessionCategoryItem, SessionQuestionAnswer, SpeakerCategoryItem. Each gets a NullNavigationPopulator and a generic EntityQueryService, but no delete-handler registration, because children are deleted by cascade from their aggregate root, not independently.
    • Cross-module boundary (:93): ISessionBookmarkValidationService → SessionBookmarkValidationService. This is the service the Engagement module calls (in-process in monolith mode, over gRPC when extracted, ADR-007) to validate a session/user before creating a bookmark.
    • Scrutor scan (:97): ScanModuleApplicationServices<ClassReference>() discovers by convention every ICommandHandler<,>, IQueryHandler<,>, IDomainEventHandler<>, DTO/request mapper, and validator in the assembly (including the Category validation rule fragments above), handling the "many small things" without boilerplate.
  • Why it's built this way: Scrutor convention scanning covers dozens of handlers/mappers/validators with zero per-type wiring; the explicit TryAddScoped calls handle the closed generics Scrutor cannot infer (it can't derive the three type arguments of IEntityQueryService<Event, EventDTO, EventIdentifierType> from a scan). Using TryAdd* (not Add*) means a registration already present, e.g. one substituted by an integration-test WebApplicationFactory, is not overwritten, a subtle idempotency guarantee ([Rubric §14, Testability]).
  • Where it's used: called from the Conference module's IModule.Register(), which ModuleLoader invokes in topological order at service-host startup; in integration tests the same method re-runs inside WebApplicationFactory<Program>.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the _ = applicationSettings discard (:40) marks an intentional hook point (profiler decorators), not a completed feature; the prior tier walkthrough's mention of dispatching queries "through MediatR" is stale, this codebase has no MediatR; CQRS dispatch goes through the framework's own command/query dispatcher and decorator pipeline.

SessionizeSyncResult

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/ISessionizeSyncStrategy.cs:21 · Level 0 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the tiny return value of a single Sessionize sync strategy: two counters reporting how many entities that strategy created-or-updated. It is co-located with ISessionizeSyncStrategy in the same file.
  • Depends on: nothing first-party (BCL only). It is the result half of the strategy contract; the input half is SessionizeSyncContext.
  • Walkthrough: two init properties (ISessionizeSyncStrategy.cs:24-27): PrimarySynced is the count of the strategy's main entity (categories synced, speakers synced, sessions synced…); SecondarySynced is an optional companion count (only CategorySyncStrategy populates it, with the number of category items synced alongside their categories). Both default to 0, so a strategy that has no secondary entity simply leaves it unset.
  • Why it's built this way: returning a small record rather than a bare int leaves headroom to add more per-strategy metadata (a third counter, per-strategy warnings) without breaking the five implementors or the orchestrator. The orchestrator (RefreshFromSessionizeHandler) reads these two fields positionally to assemble the composite RefreshFromSessionizeResultDTO.
  • Where it's used: returned by every ISessionizeSyncStrategy.SyncAsync implementation (the five strategies below); accumulated into a List<SessionizeSyncResult> and projected into the result DTO by the handler.

RefreshFromSessionizeCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/RefreshFromSessionizeCommand.cs:18 · Level 6 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the CQRS command (UC-6) that triggers pulling the latest conference data from the Sessionize API for one event and upserting its categories, rooms, questions, speakers, and sessions. It is a one-field record: RefreshFromSessionizeCommand(EventIdentifierType EventId).
  • Depends on: first-party: ICacheInvalidating, ITransactional, IFeatureGated (all Level 0 decorator opt-in markers), ConferenceFeatures (the feature-name constants), and the Event aggregate (referenced only for typeof(Event).FullName to build the cache prefix). Externals: none beyond the BCL.
  • Concept reinforced, opt-in decorators via marker interfaces. The CQRS decorator pipeline (Logging → Caching → Transactional → handler, taught in group 5) applies cross-cutting behavior only to commands that opt in by implementing a marker interface. This command opts into three at once:
    • [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns] (assesses whether caching, transactions, and feature gating live in the pipeline, not hand-rolled in each handler). ICacheInvalidating makes the CachingCommandDecorator purge cached Event reads after a successful refresh; the CachePrefix property returns $"{typeof(Event).FullName}:" (RefreshFromSessionizeCommand.cs:21) so every cache entry keyed under the Event type is invalidated.
    • ITransactional makes the TransactionalCommandDecorator wrap the whole multi-entity upsert in a single DB transaction, so a failure midway through the five strategies rolls back the lot (the doc comment, RefreshFromSessionizeCommand.cs:12-16, states this is the reason for the marker).
    • IFeatureGated makes the feature-gate decorator check FeatureName before executing; FeatureName returns ConferenceFeatures.SessionizeIntegration (line 24), so if that feature flag is off the command short-circuits. This is [Rubric §10]'s feature-flag-as-runtime-switch in action.
  • Walkthrough: the record carries one positional parameter, EventId, plus two computed interface members: CachePrefix (line 21) and FeatureName (line 24). No validation logic lives here, preconditions (BR-6 code present, BR-63 throttle) are checked in the handler against live entity state, not on the command shape.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the command a thin, intent-only record and pushing all behavior into (a) pipeline decorators selected by markers and (b) the handler is the codebase's standard CQRS shape; it keeps the command serializable and free of dependencies on infrastructure.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference REST controller's POST /events/{id}/refresh-from-sessionize endpoint; handled by RefreshFromSessionizeHandler.

SessionizeSyncContext

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/SessionizeSyncContext.cs:11 · Level 8 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the shared, mutable context object threaded through every Sessionize sync strategy in one import run. It bundles the parsed API response, the target event, the unit of work the strategies use to reach repositories, and two running tallies (warnings and skipped-soft-deleted count).
  • Depends on: first-party: SessionizeResponse (the parsed Sessionize payload), the Event aggregate (group 17), and IUnitOfWork (repository access + SaveChangesAsync). Externals: List<string> (BCL).
  • Concept reinforced, the "parameter object" / shared-context pattern. [Rubric §1, SOLID] and [Rubric §16, Maintainability & Evolvability]: rather than passing four-plus arguments to every SyncAsync call (and re-threading them through each strategy's private helpers), the related state travels as one cohesive object. Adding a new piece of cross-strategy state (e.g. another tally) is a one-line change here, not a signature change on every strategy. The IUnitOfWork lives on the context so each strategy can resolve its own typed repository (context.UnitOfWork.GetRepository<Category, …>()) without the handler having to inject five repositories up front.
  • Walkthrough: four required init properties (SessionizeSyncContext.cs:13-16): Response (the SessionizeResponse), Event (the tracked aggregate, pre-loaded with Rooms/EventSpeakers), UnitOfWork, and Warnings (a mutable List<string> strategies append non-fatal messages to). One mutable int SkippedSoftDeleted { get; set; } (line 19), a running count of soft-deleted entities each strategy chose to skip (BR-136). Note the deliberate asymmetry: the four configuration inputs are init (set once, when the handler builds the context), but SkippedSoftDeleted is set because strategies increment it as a side effect during the run, and Warnings is init-but-mutated-in-place (the list reference is fixed; its contents grow).
  • Why it's built this way: making the four inputs required means the handler cannot construct an incomplete context (a compile-time guarantee that a strategy will never hit a null response or event). The mutable Warnings/SkippedSoftDeleted channel lets strategies report soft, non-fatal outcomes (a Sessionize record that couldn't be created, a deleted entity skipped) back to the handler without throwing, feeding the graceful-degradation story the import depends on.
  • Where it's used: constructed once per command in RefreshFromSessionizeHandler.HandleAsync and passed to each ISessionizeSyncStrategy.SyncAsync in turn; after the loop the handler reads Warnings and SkippedSoftDeleted into the result DTO.

ISessionizeSyncStrategy

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/ISessionizeSyncStrategy.cs:7 · Level 9 · interface

  • What it is: the Strategy contract for synchronizing one entity family from the external Sessionize API response into the Conference domain. Each implementation owns exactly one category of data (categories, rooms, questions, speakers, sessions). The same file also declares the SessionizeSyncResult record (lines 21-28) used as the return type.
  • Depends on: first-party: SessionizeSyncContext (Level 8, the input bundle) and SessionizeSyncResult (Level 0, co-located, the output). Externals: Task<T>, CancellationToken (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the Strategy pattern for a pluggable, ordered import pipeline. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns] (assesses whether a pattern solves a real structural problem rather than being "pattern theater"). The Sessionize payload covers five inter-dependent entity types; encoding each as an ISessionizeSyncStrategy lets RefreshFromSessionizeHandler hold an ordered array of them and iterate, knowing only the interface, never the per-entity merge logic. [Rubric §1, SOLID] (Open/Closed): adding a future entity family (say a Track) means adding one strategy and one array slot, with zero edits to existing strategies or the loop body. [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness]: the entire external-API integration is isolated behind this seam, so it can be mocked in tests or swapped wholesale.
  • Walkthrough: a single method: Task<SessionizeSyncResult> SyncAsync(SessionizeSyncContext context, CancellationToken cancellationToken) (ISessionizeSyncStrategy.cs:15). All state, the response, the event, the unit of work, the warnings, arrives via the context; the method returns counts via the result. There is no per-strategy configuration on the interface itself, which is what lets the orchestrator treat all five uniformly.
  • Why it's built this way: a record result (not an int) and a context input (not a long parameter list) both leave the contract evolvable: more counters or more shared state can be added without changing the method signature every implementor must honor.
  • Where it's used: implemented by the five sync strategies below; consumed by RefreshFromSessionizeHandler, which holds the implementations in a static readonly ISessionizeSyncStrategy[] in dependency order.

CategorySyncStrategy, QuestionSyncStrategy, RoomSyncStrategy, SessionSyncStrategy, SpeakerSyncStrategy

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · Level 10 · class (internal sealed)

Type File:Line Entity synced Bulk-loads existing? Noteworthy specifics
CategorySyncStrategy MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/CategorySyncStrategy.cs:11 Category + CategoryItem children Yes, one GetByIdsAsync (with CategoryItems include) Only strategy that populates SecondarySynced (item count); BR-136 skip
QuestionSyncStrategy MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/QuestionSyncStrategy.cs:11 Question Yes Reserved-ID-range guard; entity-type detection from answers; type-string mapping; BR-136 skip
RoomSyncStrategy MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/RoomSyncStrategy.cs:8 Room (child of Event) No, works over already-loaded context.Event.Rooms Synchronous (Task.FromResult); BR-136 skip
SessionSyncStrategy MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/SessionSyncStrategy.cs:12 Session + speaker/category/QA children Yes (3 includes) BR-86 (date-range warn), BR-122 (zero-duration warn); BR-136 skip
SpeakerSyncStrategy MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/SpeakerSyncStrategy.cs:12 Speaker + category/QA children Yes (2 includes) Social-link extraction; EventSpeaker link creation; BR-136 skip
  • What they are: one strategy class per Sessionize entity family, each implementing ISessionizeSyncStrategy to encapsulate the create-or-update (upsert) logic for that family against the shared SessionizeSyncContext. Together they are the Strategy implementations the orchestrating RefreshFromSessionizeHandler runs in sequence.
  • Depends on: first-party: ISessionizeSyncStrategy / SessionizeSyncContext / SessionizeSyncResult; their respective aggregates (Category, Question/QuestionInvariants, Event, Session, Speaker); the IUnitOfWork repositories obtained from the context; and the Sessionize* parsed-response records (SessionizeResponse and its children). Externals: LINQ, Dictionary/HashSet/List (BCL).
  • Concept reinforced, Strategy for a bulk-upsert pipeline (one algorithm per entity family). [Rubric §2, Design Patterns] and [Rubric §1, SOLID] (Open/Closed): each family's import differs in subtle ways, so isolating them keeps each SyncAsync small and below the cyclomatic-complexity analyzer budget and keeps the orchestrator closed for modification. [Rubric §16, Maintainability & Evolvability]: a change to room sync cannot break speaker sync because they share no code beyond the context.
  • Walkthrough, the shared four-phase shape. Every strategy (except the synchronous RoomSyncStrategy) follows the same pattern:
    1. Bulk pre-load, resolve the typed repository via context.UnitOfWork.GetRepository<TEntity, TId>(), then GetByIdsAsync(sessionizeIds, includes: […], asTracking: true, ignoreQueryFilters: true, …) in one query for the whole batch, and index the result into a Dictionary keyed by id (e.g. CategorySyncStrategy.cs:21-27, SessionSyncStrategy.cs:21-27, SpeakerSyncStrategy.cs:21-27, QuestionSyncStrategy.cs:44-49). asTracking: true so updates are change-tracked; ignoreQueryFilters: true so soft-deleted rows are visible to the skip check. RoomSyncStrategy skips this phase entirely, rooms are already on context.Event.Rooms, which the handler eagerly loaded. This is a deliberate [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] choice: N separate GetByIdAsync calls on a full re-import of hundreds of sessions would be an N+1 disaster.
    2. Iterate and discriminate, for each incoming Sessionize record:
      • found and IsDeleted == true → context.SkippedSoftDeleted++ and continue (BR-136: never resurrect a soft-deleted entity from an external import);
      • found and active → call the aggregate's Update(...) method (mutation stays inside the domain);
      • not found → call the aggregate's Create(...) factory, which returns Result<T>; on failure, append a message to context.Warnings and skip (graceful degradation, one bad record never aborts the whole import).
    3. Sync children, CategorySyncStrategy.SyncCategoryItems upserts each category's items; SessionSyncStrategy.SyncSessionChildren upserts SessionSpeakers, SessionCategoryItems, and SessionQuestionAnswers in one pass; SpeakerSyncStrategy upserts speaker category items and question answers and creates an EventSpeaker link when the speaker is not yet linked to the event (SpeakerSyncStrategy.cs:42-45). Children are always matched by their natural identity (CategoryItemId, SpeakerId, QuestionId) under an IsDeleted guard so deleted children are not re-added.
    4. Batch-add and return, newly created roots are collected in a local List<T> and flushed with one repo.AddRangeAsync(newEntities, …) call, then a SessionizeSyncResult with the PrimarySynced (and, for categories, SecondarySynced) tally is returned.
  • Strategy-specific details.
    • CategorySyncStrategy is the only one that returns a non-zero SecondarySynced, CategorySyncStrategy.cs:58 reports both categories and the category-items synced beneath them. New categories are created via Category.Create and their items added through the aggregate's AddCategoryItem (CategorySyncStrategy.cs:97-108), so item invariants are enforced inside the Category aggregate.
    • QuestionSyncStrategy (QuestionSyncStrategy.cs:11-116) carries three extra concerns. Entity-type detection (lines 19-27, 55-67): it pre-builds two HashSets of question ids, those answered by sessions and those answered by speakers, and uses them to tag each question "Session" or "Speaker" (defaulting to "Session" for questions with no answers yet), passing that string to Question.Create/Update. Reserved-ID-range guard (lines 32-39): a Sessionize question whose id falls in [QuestionInvariants.ManualIdRangeStart, QuestionInvariants.ManualIdRangeEnd] would shadow a user-created question, so it is rejected with a warning (not a hard error). This is a cross-source invariant: it spans external (Sessionize) and internal (user-created) data, which is exactly why it lives in the application layer and not on the Question entity, which can only see one record at a time. Type-string mapping (MapSessionizeQuestionType, lines 109-115): Sessionize's open-ended type strings (Short_Text, Long_Text, Url, YesNo, …) collapse to the three domain-valid values "Rating", "Email", "Text", with "Text" as the catch-all default. The method is internal static so it is unit-testable without instantiating the strategy.
    • RoomSyncStrategy (RoomSyncStrategy.cs:8-37) is the simplest: no async I/O (it returns Task.FromResult(result)), no repository, and it mutates only through context.Event.UpdateRoom / context.Event.AddRoom, delegating to Event aggregate methods so room invariants are enforced by the domain. (Its UpdateRoom call passes null for the four optional room attributes Sessionize does not supply, RoomSyncStrategy.cs:25.)
    • SessionSyncStrategy (SessionSyncStrategy.cs:12-147) adds two non-fatal validations: BR-86 warns when a session's StartsAt/EndsAt falls outside the event's date range (lines 53-62) and BR-122 warns on zero/negative duration (lines 64-68). Both append to context.Warnings and still import the session "as-is", deferring the accept/reject decision to a human reviewer.
    • SpeakerSyncStrategy (SpeakerSyncStrategy.cs:12-178) parses social links via ExtractSocialLinks (lines 124-156), mapping SessionizeLink.LinkType strings ("Twitter", "LinkedIn", "Blog"/"Company_Website", plus a URL-substring heuristic for GitHub) to typed nullable-string fields. ExtractTwitterHandle (lines 158-177) strips the common twitter.com/x.com URL prefixes (culture-invariant OrdinalIgnoreCase) to leave a bare handle and is internal static for direct unit testing. Because Speaker.Create does not accept social links, a newly created speaker is immediately Update(...)-ed to set them (SpeakerSyncStrategy.cs:88-94).
  • Why they're built this way: the internal sealed visibility is deliberate: these are implementation details of a single use case, not general-purpose services, so internal keeps them un-injectable elsewhere and signals their scope. The reliance on entity Create/Update (never direct property writes) keeps invariants in the domain; the warn-and-continue posture (never throw on a bad record) keeps a single malformed Sessionize entity from aborting the whole transactional import.
  • Where they're used: instantiated once in RefreshFromSessionizeHandler's static readonly strategy array and invoked sequentially inside the handler's unit-of-work transaction; each one's SessionizeSyncResult is accumulated and projected into RefreshFromSessionizeResultDTO.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the strategies assume their declared run order (categories before speakers/sessions, etc.) is honored by the handler; nothing in a strategy enforces that another strategy ran first. Each is unit-tested individually (see *SyncStrategyTests in group 25).

RefreshFromSessionizeHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RefreshFromSessionize · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RefreshFromSessionize/RefreshFromSessionizeHandler.cs:16 · Level 11 · class (sealed partial, command handler)

  • What it is: the command handler for RefreshFromSessionizeCommand. It loads the event, validates preconditions (BR-6 code present, BR-63 throttle), calls the Sessionize HTTP API, fans the response out to the five per-entity sync strategies in dependency order, commits everything in one transaction, and returns a per-entity-count result DTO. It is one of the most dependency-heavy handlers in the codebase.
  • Depends on: first-party: IUnitOfWork (repository access + SaveChangesAsync + RequestIdentityInsert), ICurrentUserService (stamps who ran the refresh), System.TimeProvider (the injected clock for the throttle window and refresh timestamp), ISessionizeService (the HTTP client abstraction over the Sessionize API), SessionizeResponse (the parsed payload), Result/Error, the Event aggregate (group 17), RefreshFromSessionizeCommand/RefreshFromSessionizeResultDTO, and the strategy seam ISessionizeSyncStrategy/SessionizeSyncContext/SessionizeSyncResult with its five implementations (CategorySyncStrategy et al.). It implements ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>. Notable externals: Microsoft.Extensions.Logging (ILogger<T>, source-generated [LoggerMessage]), HttpRequestException (BCL).
  • Concept reinforced, orchestration-only command handler over a Strategy pipeline. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns]: the handler owns what order and whether to run the import, but knows nothing of how any entity merges, that is delegated to the strategies (introduced at ISessionizeSyncStrategy). The order is made explicit and self-documenting in the static SyncStrategies array. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven]: a textbook command handler, discovered by Scrutor, wrapped by the decorator pipeline (Logging → Caching → Transactional → this), and reached only through the ICommandHandler<…> interface, never as a concrete type. [Rubric §17, DevOps & Deployment] / [Rubric §13, Observability]: the BR-63 throttle (lines 63-72) caps refreshes at one per five minutes per event (returning a Result.Failure without calling the external API), and the source-generated structured log on success records the event id, both serve runtime operability and external-rate-limit kindness.
  • Walkthrough
    • Static strategy array (lines 25-32): SyncStrategies is a static readonly ISessionizeSyncStrategy[] of exactly five stateless instances in dependency order, CategorySyncStrategy, RoomSyncStrategy, QuestionSyncStrategy, SpeakerSyncStrategy, SessionSyncStrategy (categories/rooms first because speakers and sessions reference them). static avoids re-allocating the array per command; the strategies are stateless because all per-run state lives in the freshly-built SessionizeSyncContext.
    • Constructor (lines 16-21): primary constructor taking IUnitOfWork, ISessionizeService, ICurrentUserService, TimeProvider (line 20), and ILogger<RefreshFromSessionizeHandler>. The sealed partial modifier pairs with the [LoggerMessage] source generator (line 150).
    • HandleAsync (lines 35-148) proceeds in six phases:
      1. Event load (lines 40-50): fetches the Event aggregate with Rooms and EventSpeakers eagerly loaded and asTracking: true. A missing event returns Error.NotFound (line 50).
      2. BR-6 precondition (lines 53-61): a null/whitespace Event.SessionizeCode returns Error.Invariant ("Event.Sessionize.NoCode"), no import without a configured Sessionize code.
      3. BR-63 throttle (lines 63-72): if Event.LastSessionizeRefreshOn is within the last five minutes, returns Error.Invariant ("Event.Sessionize.Throttled"). The "now" it compares against comes from the injected TimeProvider (timeProvider.GetUtcNow().UtcDateTime, line 65), not DateTime.UtcNow, so the throttle window is deterministically testable.
      4. External API call (lines 74-87): ISessionizeService.GetAllAsync(code, …) inside a try/catch (HttpRequestException); a network failure becomes Error.Failure ("Event.Sessionize.Unavailable"), the Result pattern absorbs the exception into a structured error rather than propagating it.
      5. Empty-response short-circuit (lines 89-105): a null response is valid (an event may have no published data yet). The handler stamps the refresh timestamp via Event.RecordSessionizeRefresh(userId, timeProvider.GetUtcNow().UtcDateTime) (line 92), saves, and returns a zero-count RefreshFromSessionizeResultDTO without running any strategy.
      6. Strategy execution (lines 107-133): builds a SessionizeSyncContext (response + tracked event + unit of work + empty warnings list) and awaits each strategy sequentially (not in parallel, categories must exist before speakers/sessions reference them), accumulating each SessionizeSyncResult into a List. A non-zero SkippedSoftDeleted is folded into Warnings. Event.RecordSessionizeRefresh(currentUserId, timeProvider.GetUtcNow().UtcDateTime) stamps who/when from the injected clock (line 128), unitOfWork.RequestIdentityInsert() (line 132) signals the unit of work to wrap the save in SET IDENTITY_INSERT ON/OFF per table (Sessionize supplies its own integer ids into IDENTITY columns), and SaveChangesAsync commits the whole batch in one round-trip. The result DTO is assembled from the accumulated counts.
    • Source-generated log (lines 150-151): [LoggerMessage(Level = Information, Message = "Event {EventId} refreshed from Sessionize")] on a static partial method, zero-allocation structured logging on the success path; partial requires the sealed partial class declaration.
  • Why it's built this way: the handler is pure orchestration (load → check → call → fan-out → commit → return); no per-entity merge logic lives here, which keeps it readable despite touching five entity types. Every failure path returns a Result rather than throwing, so the decorator pipeline and controller handle errors uniformly via Match/HandleFailure, the codebase's pervasive Result convention. RequestIdentityInsert() is the deliberate infrastructure seam that lets Sessionize's external ids land in SQL Server IDENTITY columns (which normally reject explicit values) so imported sessions/speakers keep stable, externally-known ids.
  • Where it's used: registered by Scrutor as the handler for RefreshFromSessionizeCommand; invoked by the Conference REST controller exposing POST /events/{id}/refresh-from-sessionize. The decorator pipeline wraps the call at runtime. Unit-tested by RefreshFromSessionizeHandlerTests (see group 25).
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the result projection (lines 137-144) reads results[0]…results[4] positionally, relying on SyncStrategies staying in the declared order; reordering the array without updating the index reads would silently swap reported counts. An enum-keyed result map would be safer but adds complexity the current five-strategy size does not justify.

EventDateRangeRules<T>

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Validation · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Validation/EventValidationRules.cs:55 · Level 0 · class (sealed, generic)

  • What it is: a reusable FluentValidation rule fragment that enforces three things about an event's scheduling window: a start date is present, an end date is present, and EndDate >= StartDate. Parameterized on the owning command/request type T so the same fragment composes into both create and update validators.
  • Depends on: FluentValidation.AbstractValidator<T> (NuGet); no first-party Level-0 types. Composed into the full event validators (higher level) via Include(...).
  • Concept introduced, the composable cross-property validator fragment. [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (assesses server-side validation that mirrors UI rules and produces clear messages, here each WithMessage is the literal text the form shows). [Rubric §1, SOLID] (Open/Closed: a new event constraint is a new fragment Included into the parent validator, not an edit to existing rules). The richest member of the room/event rule family because it validates across two properties: it compiles the startDateSelector expression into a delegate once (EventValidationRules.cs:68) and calls it inside the EndDate Must rule (lines 69-71) so the end-date rule can read the start date off the same instance being validated. The simpler siblings (RoomSortRules<T>, RoomCapacityRules<T>) validate a single property and so never compile a selector.
  • Walkthrough: the constructor (lines 58-72) takes two selector expressions (startDateSelector, endDateSelector). It wires NotEmpty on each (lines 62-66), then compiles the start selector (startDateFunc, line 68) and adds a second RuleFor(endDateSelector) whose Must((instance, endDate) => endDate >= startDateFunc(instance)) (line 70) reads the instance's start date for the comparison. There is no field state; all behaviour lives in the constructor-registered rules.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the cross-property rule as its own fragment means the "end on or after start" invariant lives in exactly one place and is Included wherever an event window is edited, instead of being re-typed (and risking divergence) in each command validator.
  • Where it's used: Included in the Conference module's create/update event command validators (higher level).

GetContentSimilarityQuery

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetContentSimilarity · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetContentSimilarity/GetContentSimilarityQuery.cs:6 · Level 0 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the query contract for "which pairs of sessions in this event have overlapping content?". Carries the event id plus a tunable similarity floor: (EventIdentifierType EventId, double MinimumSimilarity = 0.3).
  • Depends on: EventIdentifierType; no other first-party types.
  • Concept: same read-only query-record shape as GetCategoryDistributionQuery [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven]. The distinguishing detail is the defaulted threshold: MinimumSimilarity defaults to 0.3 (line 6), so callers that don't care can omit it while organizers can raise the bar to see only the strongest overlaps. (Note: the threshold parameter is MinimumSimilarity with a default of 0.3 in current source, an earlier edition of this guide described it as SimilarityThreshold = 0.4; the code is ground truth.)
  • Walkthrough: two positional parameters; MinimumSimilarity has a compile-time default. The pairwise scoring and filtering happen in GetContentSimilarityHandler.
  • Why it's built this way: exposing the threshold as a query parameter (rather than a hard-coded constant) lets the same handler serve both a permissive "show me anything related" view and a strict "show me near- duplicates" view without code changes.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference decision-support endpoints; resolved by GetContentSimilarityHandler.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Validation · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Validation/RoomValidationRules.cs:37 · Level 0 · class (sealed, generic)

SessionSimilarityCalculator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetContentSimilarity · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetContentSimilarity/SessionSimilarityCalculator.cs:9 · Level 0 · class (static, internal)

  • What it is: a pure, stateless calculator that scores how alike two sessions are, by combining their category-item overlap (60% weight) with their title/description keyword overlap (40% weight). Used by GetContentSimilarityHandler to surface sessions that might compete for the same audience or be near-duplicate submissions.
  • Depends on: System.Collections.Frozen.FrozenSet<string> (BCL); no first-party types.
  • Concept introduced, weighted Jaccard similarity with span-based tokenization. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (assesses efficient, allocation-conscious algorithms). The Jaccard index of two sets is |A ∩ B| / |A ∪ B|, 1.0 when identical, 0.0 when disjoint. This calculator blends two independent signals: two sessions with identical category tags but no shared keywords score 0.6; two with no shared tags but identical keywords score 0.4. [Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality]: the implementation is carefully allocation-light, stop words live in a FrozenSet<string> (O(1) lookup after a one-time build at class init), and TokenizeText scans the input with a ReadOnlySpan<char> instead of allocating per-character substrings.
  • Walkthrough,
    • Constants: CategoryWeight = 0.6, KeywordWeight = 0.4 (lines 11-12).
    • StopWords (lines 14-34): a FrozenSet<string> (built with StringComparer.Ordinal) of common English function words plus conference-generic noise ("SESSION", "TALK", "WORKSHOP", "DEEP", "DIVE", …) that would otherwise inflate false similarity across unrelated talks.
    • TokenizeText(string? text) (lines 41-71): returns [] for null/whitespace; otherwise walks the text as a span, treating any non-letter-or-digit as a separator, and emits each word of length >= 3 uppercased (ToUpperInvariant, per CA1308) into an ordinal HashSet<string> unless it is a stop word.
    • CalculateJaccardIndex<T>(HashSet<T> setA, HashSet<T> setB) (lines 80-92): returns 0.0 when both sets are empty; otherwise counts the intersection by probing the larger set with the smaller set's elements (a small optimization) and divides by the union count.
    • CalculateSimilarity(...) (lines 97-106): CategoryWeight * Jaccard(categoryItems) + KeywordWeight * Jaccard(keywords).
    • GetIntersection<T>(...) (lines 115-121): returns the shared elements as a List<T> (used to populate SharedCategoryItems/SharedKeywords on the result DTO).
  • Why it's built this way: a weighted composite captures both topical alignment (categories) and descriptive overlap (keywords); pure category-Jaccard alone would flag every talk that happens to sit in the same broad track, so the keyword component raises the bar. Keeping it a pure static class makes it trivially testable and free of DI/lifetime concerns.
  • Where it's used: GetContentSimilarityHandler calls TokenizeText once per session, then CalculateSimilarity for every session pair, filters by the query threshold, and maps the survivors (via GetIntersection) onto SimilarSessionPair DTOs.

StatusBucket

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetCategoryDistribution · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetCategoryDistribution/GetCategoryDistributionHandler.cs:94 · Level 0 · enum (private, nested)

  • What it is: a tiny private enum nested inside GetCategoryDistributionHandler with three members, Accepted, AcceptQueue, Pending, used to fold the open-ended session-status strings into the three columns the distribution chart reports. It is an implementation detail of that one handler and is never exposed to callers.
  • Depends on: conceptually on SessionStatuses, whose string constants the handler maps into these buckets; structurally it depends on nothing.
  • Concept introduced, the handler-private classification enum. [Rubric §16, Maintainability & Evolvability] (assesses keeping incidental detail local so it can change without ripple). Session status is a free-form string from Sessionize; rather than scatter string comparisons through the aggregation code, the handler classifies each session once into a StatusBucket and then counts by bucket. (An identically named but separate private StatusBucket exists in the session-selection-dashboard handler; the two are deliberately not shared, coupling two orthogonal use cases through one enum would buy nothing.)
  • Walkthrough: declared at GetCategoryDistributionHandler.cs:94-99 with members Accepted, AcceptQueue, Pending. The handler's ClassifyStatus(Session) (lines 101-112) maps a null status or SessionStatuses.Accepted → Accepted, SessionStatuses.AcceptQueue → AcceptQueue, and everything else → Pending. Note the bucketing runs only on sessions that survive the IsDeclined filter (lines 45, 114-115), so declined sessions never reach a bucket, which is why there is no Declined member.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the enum private to the handler means the distribution bucketing can evolve (add a bucket, re-map a status) without touching any other use case or any public contract.
  • Where it's used: inside GetCategoryDistributionHandler only.

EventNameRules<T>

Each *Rules<T> class inherits from RequiredStringRules<T> (or AbstractValidator<T>) and takes a property-selector Expression<Func<T, string>>. Because T is the command/request type, the same rule class is Included in a create-event validator and an update-event validator with no duplication. The constructor base(selector, "Event Name", EventInvariants.NameMaxLength) (EventValidationRules.cs:16-17) delegates all the NotEmpty/MaximumLength wiring to the base, so the invariant value lives once in EventInvariants and the rule class just names the field. [Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design] (ubiquitous language in code: it is literally EventNameRules, not NameValidator).
  • Walkthrough: one constructor, one base call (EventValidationRules.cs:16-17); no body logic, all behaviour is in RequiredStringRules<T>.
  • Why it's built this way: the EventInvariants.NameMaxLength constant that drives this rule is the same constant the EF configuration uses for the column's HasMaxLength, so the database constraint and the validation message can never drift apart, one source of truth.
