GetCategoryDistributionHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetCategoryDistribution · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetCategoryDistribution/GetCategoryDistributionHandler.cs:14 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the query handler that answers GetCategoryDistributionQuery: for one event it returns, per category item, how many submitted sessions are accepted, in the accept-queue, pending, and the total, the data behind the organizer's "where are submissions clustering?" view.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (to get repositories), IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult> (the CQRS contract it implements), Session + SessionCategoryItem + Category + CategoryItem (the domain entities it reads), SessionStatuses (status string constants), Result, and the CategoryDistributionDTO/CategoryGroupDistribution/CategoryItemDistribution output shapes. Uses the nested StatusBucket enum.
  • Concept introduced, the read-side aggregation handler. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (a query handler is side-effect-free: it loads, projects, and returns, no mutation, no SaveChanges). [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: every load uses asTracking: false (lines 27, 32) because nothing is written back, so EF skips change-tracking overhead, and the two reads (includes-eager-loading children) are batched rather than lazily walked. [Rubric §1, SOLID]: the handler decomposes into small static helpers (CountSessionsPerCategoryItem, BuildCategoryGroups, ClassifyStatus, IsDeclined), each with a single responsibility.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (lines 17-39):
    1. Resolve two repositories from the unit of work, sessions and categories (lines 21-22).
    2. Load all of the event's non-service sessions with their SessionCategoryItems eager-loaded (where: s => s.EventId == query.EventId && !s.IsServiceSession, no tracking, lines 24-28), and all categories with their CategoryItems (lines 30-33).
    3. CountSessionsPerCategoryItem (lines 41-64): drop declined sessions, flatten each remaining session into one (categoryItemId, bucket) pair per non-deleted SessionCategoryItem, then tally a per-item (Total, Accepted, AcceptQueue, Pending) tuple, incrementing the right slot by classifying the session via ClassifyStatus (lines 101-112) into a StatusBucket.
    4. BuildCategoryGroups (lines 66-92): keep only categories that have at least one counted item, order by Sort, and project each into a CategoryGroupDistribution whose Items are the non-deleted category items (ordered by Sort) carrying their counts.
    5. Wrap the result in Result.Success(new CategoryDistributionDTO { ... }) (line 38).
  • Why it's built this way: building the distribution from two no-tracking batch reads plus pure in-memory folding keeps the operation cheap and side-effect-free; classifying status once into the private StatusBucket keeps the bucket logic in one place instead of repeating string comparisons across the count and the projection.
  • Where it's used: registered by Scrutor as the handler for GetCategoryDistributionQuery; invoked through the CQRS dispatcher from the Conference SessionsController decision-support endpoints and aggregated by the session-selection dashboard.

GetContentSimilarityHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetContentSimilarity · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetContentSimilarity/GetContentSimilarityHandler.cs:14 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the query handler that answers GetContentSimilarityQuery: it scores every pair of an event's sessions for content overlap and returns the top matches above the caller's threshold, so organizers can spot near-duplicate or competing submissions.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult>, Session / Category and their children, SessionStatuses, SessionSimilarityCalculator (the scoring engine), Result, and the ContentSimilarityDTO/SimilarSessionPair output shapes.
  • Concept introduced, the O(n²) in-memory pairwise scan with a result cap. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (assesses awareness of algorithmic cost on large inputs). Comparing every pair of sessions is quadratic, so the handler is deliberately scoped: it pre-tokenizes each session once before the loop, runs the upper-triangular comparison (j = i + 1), and caps the output at MaxPairs = 50 (line 17) so a large event can't return a huge response. This is fine because per-event session counts are in the dozens-to-low-hundreds; a much larger corpus would want a precomputed index instead. The handler is otherwise a textbook read-side query [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven], no-tracking reads, no mutation.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (lines 19-114):
    1. Load all non-service, non-declined sessions for the event with SessionCategoryItems eager-loaded, no tracking (lines 27-33); load all categories with items (lines 36-39) to build a categoryItemId → name lookup (lines 41-48) for labelling shared items later.
    2. Pre-compute per session a HashSet of its non-deleted category-item ids plus a keyword set from Title + " " + Description via SessionSimilarityCalculator.TokenizeText (lines 51-59), done once so the inner loop never re-tokenizes.
    3. Double loop (i, then j = i + 1, lines 64-79): call SessionSimilarityCalculator.CalculateSimilarity on each pair and keep (i, j, score) tuples whose score >= query.MinimumSimilarity.
    4. Sort the kept pairs by score descending and truncate to MaxPairs (lines 82-86).
    5. Project each surviving pair into a SimilarSessionPair: round the score to 3 places (banker's rounding, line 105), resolve SharedCategoryItems to names via the lookup, and take up to 10 SharedKeywords (lines 89-111).
    6. Return Result.Success(new ContentSimilarityDTO { Pairs = result }) (line 113).
  • Why it's built this way: pre-tokenizing outside the loop turns the expensive text work into O(n) rather than O(n²); the MaxPairs cap bounds both compute and payload size; delegating all scoring to the pure SessionSimilarityCalculator keeps the handler focused on data loading and shaping, and keeps the algorithm independently unit-testable.
  • Where it's used: registered by Scrutor as the handler for GetContentSimilarityQuery; reached through the CQRS dispatcher from the Conference decision-support endpoints.

GetPublicSessionFilterQuery

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.GetPublicSessionFilter · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/GetPublicSessionFilter/GetPublicSessionFilterQuery.cs:9 · Level 0 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: A parameterless CQRS query whose handler returns a specification (not data): the filter that scopes the public session list to sessions the public may see, non-declined, non-cancelled sessions whose parent event is published (BR-132 / BR-49).
  • Depends on: nothing. public sealed record GetPublicSessionFilterQuery; (:9) carries no state, the whole event set is implied. The behavior lives entirely in GetPublicSessionFilterHandler.
  • Concept introduced, a query that yields a query-shape. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (§6 assesses clean read/write separation; this is a side-effect-free read that computes an authorization filter). Unlike the dashboard queries that return a finished DTO, this query hands back a reusable Specification that the caller then applies to its own read. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture]: the reason it exists as a dedicated query is that Session and Event can live in different data sources (ADR-018 polyglot persistence). When they do, a plain EF navigation join across Session.Event is not translatable, so the published-event check must be resolved as a two-step cross-source lookup rather than a single SQL join. The query record itself is the trivial part, its value is naming that slice.
  • Walkthrough: A single empty positional-less sealed record (:9). No members. Its XML docs (:3-8) spell out the intent: because Session may sit in Cosmos and Event in SQL Server, the handler delegates to the framework's cross-source specification helper.
  • Why it's built this way: Encapsulating "what is publicly visible" as one query keeps the rule (BR-49) in one place: the same predicate as SessionStatuses IsPubliclyVisible (its Declined/"Cancelled" exclusion), plus the published-event gate, computed once and reused by every public session endpoint.
  • Where it's used: Dispatched by GetPublicSessionFilterHandler; the Conference SessionsController calls it from BuildPublicSessionSpecificationAsync for non-organizer callers (organizers get null and see everything).

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · see per-member table · Level 0 · records (sealed)

  • What it is: Three CQRS request messages for the decision-support analytics slices. Two are queries (side-effect-free reads that drive the organizer's session-selection analytics); the third is a command (it mutates, it deletes and recreates the AI score rows). Each is a tiny immutable record that carries only the identifier its handler needs.
Type File:Line Kind Carries Handler return
GetSessionSelectionDashboardQuery MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetSessionSelectionDashboard/GetSessionSelectionDashboardQuery.cs:5 query EventId Result<SessionSelectionDashboardDTO>
GetSpeakerSessionOverlapQuery MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetSpeakerSessionOverlap/GetSpeakerSessionOverlapQuery.cs:5 query EventId Result<SpeakerSessionOverlapDTO>
ScoreEventSessionsCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/ScoreEventSessions/ScoreEventSessionsCommand.cs:5 command EventId Result<ScoreEventSessionsResultDTO>
  • Depends on: only the strongly-typed identifier alias EventIdentifierType (see the primer on identifier-type aliases). All three are event-scoped, so each carries a single EventId positional member.
  • Concept introduced, request records as the CQRS contract. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (§6 assesses whether reads and writes are cleanly separated and each handler owns one cohesive operation; here two queries return DTOs without mutating, and the one command is explicitly typed ICommandHandler because it writes). [Rubric §5, Vertical Slice] (§5 assesses whether a feature is a self-contained slice rather than scattered across horizontal layers; each of these records lives in its own UseCases/DecisionSupport/{Operation}/ folder beside its handler and, where present, its result DTO). A request record is the only public surface of a slice: a caller constructs it, the decorator pipeline (Logging then Caching then Transactional then handler) routes it, and the handler answers with a Result. Keeping the request a bare record with positional members means an invalid request is hard to construct and trivial to serialize/log.
  • Walkthrough: Each is a single-line positional sealed record taking just EventId (the analysis is event-scoped): GetSessionSelectionDashboardQuery(EventIdentifierType EventId) (:5), GetSpeakerSessionOverlapQuery(EventIdentifierType EventId) (:5), and ScoreEventSessionsCommand(EventIdentifierType EventId) (:5).
  • Why it's built this way: Records give value equality and immutability for free, which is what you want for a message that is dispatched, possibly cached by key, and logged. The split between two queries and one command makes the read/write intent unmistakable to the pipeline (only the command is eligible for transactional wrapping).
  • Where it's used: Constructed by the Conference REST endpoints (SessionsController decision-support actions) and dispatched to the matching handlers below (GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler, GetSpeakerSessionOverlapHandler, ScoreEventSessionsHandler).

SessionEventIdRules<T>

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.Validation · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/Validation/SessionValidationRules.cs:24 · Level 0 · class (sealed, generic)

  • What it is: A reusable FluentValidation rule set that enforces "a session must be tied to an event": it asserts the selected EventIdentifierType property is non-empty.
  • Depends on: FluentValidation.AbstractValidator<T> (the base it derives from, :25); System.Linq.Expressions.Expression<Func<T, EventIdentifierType>> (the property selector). No first-party base, unlike its sibling SessionTitleRules<T>, it derives directly from AbstractValidator<T> rather than the Common RequiredStringRules<T>, because the target is an id, not a string.
  • Concept introduced, composable, field-scoped validator fragments. [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (§24 assesses whether validation is consistent and reused rather than re-typed per form; these XRules<T> classes let many session request validators share one rule definition). A generic XRules<T> takes a property selector so the same rule can be applied to any request type that exposes an event id, the create-session validator, the update-session validator, and the import path all Include(new SessionEventIdRules<TRequest>(x => x.EventId)) instead of copy-pasting the NotEmpty() chain.
  • Walkthrough: The expression-bodied constructor takes Expression<Func<T, EventIdentifierType>> selector (:27) and registers a single rule: RuleFor(selector).NotEmpty().WithMessage("You must specify an Event for the Session").WithErrorCode("Session.EventId.Required") (:28-29). Because EventIdentifierType is int, NotEmpty() rejects the default 0; the explicit WithErrorCode gives clients a stable machine-readable code alongside the human message.
  • Why it's built this way: Pulling the rule into a named generic class makes the intent (every session needs an event) a first-class, testable unit and keeps the per-request validators declarative.
  • Where it's used: Composed into the session create/update request validators (higher-level AbstractValidator subclasses in the same Validation folder).

SessionScoringResult

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.ScoreEventSessions · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/ScoreEventSessions/IAiScoringService.cs:40 · Level 0 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: The internal result of scoring one session via IAiScoringService. It carries seven numeric sub-scores (1.0-10.0 decimal), free-text Reasoning, and a Success flag. It is never thrown, a failed AI call returns this record with Success = false.
  • Depends on: SessionIdentifierType for SessionId. No other first-party types; every property is required init-only.
  • Concept introduced, never-throw service results. [Rubric §29, Resilience] (§29 assesses how the system degrades under failure of a dependency; the AI call is an unreliable network hop, so its port reports failure in band rather than by exception) and [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven]. Rather than propagating exceptions out of the scoring call, ScoreSessionAsync returns a SessionScoringResult in all cases; the handler inspects Success and decides whether to persist the score or just log a warning, so one bad session never aborts the scoring loop. This is the Result philosophy (taught in Result) applied to a third-party integration.
  • Walkthrough: required init-only properties: SessionId (:43), then the seven sub-scores, OverallScore, TopicRelevanceScore, DescriptionQualityScore, NoveltyScore, ActionableTakeawaysScore, DepthOrInsightQualityScore, CredibilityExperienceScore (:46-64), plus Reasoning (:67) and Success (:70). The external-facing API shape is SessionAiScoreDTO in Conference.Shared; this record is Application-layer only.
  • Why it's built this way: Separating the internal scoring result from the external DTO lets the scoring implementation evolve its sub-scores without immediately breaking the API contract, and the Success flag avoids exception-as-control-flow across the per-session loop.
  • Where it's used: Returned by AnthropicScoringService.ScoreSessionAsync; consumed by ScoreEventSessionsHandler, which maps it onto the SessionAiScore aggregate for persistence.

SpeakerInfo

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.ScoreEventSessions · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/ScoreEventSessions/IAiScoringService.cs:23 · Level 0 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: The minimal speaker projection handed to the AI model when scoring a session: FullName, optional TagLine, optional Bio. (Distinct from the same-named UI record in Conference UI, this one is the AI-scoring input shape.)
  • Depends on: nothing first-party; three positional string/string? parameters.
  • Concept introduced, deliberate data minimization for an external model. [Rubric §11, Security] and [Rubric §30, Compliance/Privacy/Data Governance] (§30 assesses whether only the data truly needed leaves a boundary; here only the three fields the prompt uses are sent to a third-party AI API, no ids, no email, no internal status). Passing a purpose-built record instead of the full Speaker aggregate keeps PII and irrelevant internal state out of the outbound request.
  • Walkthrough: Positional record SpeakerInfo(string FullName, string? TagLine, string? Bio) (:23-26). The XML docs note the soft caps the model expects (tagline max 500, bio max 4000 chars).
  • Why it's built this way: Narrowing the speaker to "what the prompt needs" both protects privacy and makes the scoring input cheap to build and serialize.

StatusBucket

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetSessionSelectionDashboard · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetSessionSelectionDashboard/GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler.cs:308 · Level 0 · enum (private)

  • What it is: A private enum nested inside GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler that collapses the free string SessionStatuses constants into three display buckets, Accepted, AcceptQueue, Pending, for the category-distribution counts.
  • Depends on: conceptually on SessionStatuses; the string-to-bucket mapping is the handler's ClassifyStatus method (:315-326).
  • Concept introduced, normalizing an open string status for aggregation. Session.Status is a nullable string (it mirrors Sessionize's status vocabulary), so analytics code can't switch on it directly. ClassifyStatus treats null or "Accepted" as Accepted, "Accept_Queue" as AcceptQueue, and everything else (except "Declined", which is filtered out upstream) as Pending, giving the chart three stable columns regardless of how many raw status strings exist.
  • Walkthrough: Three members Accepted, AcceptQueue, Pending (:310-312). ClassifyStatus (:315) returns one; CountCategoryItems (:127) tallies a per-category-item tuple keyed by bucket; IsDeclined (:328) excludes declined sessions before bucketing.
  • Why it's built this way: Keeping the enum private to the handler is deliberate: a near-identical StatusBucket enum exists in GetCategoryDistributionHandler (GetCategoryDistribution/GetCategoryDistributionHandler.cs:94), and they are not shared. The two decision-support slices are orthogonal use-cases that must not couple, so each owns its own bucketing and can diverge freely. [Rubric §5, Vertical Slice] (slice independence over premature de-duplication).
  • Where it's used: Inside GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler only; never exposed to callers (they receive the aggregated CategoryItemDistribution counts).

IAiScoringService

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.ScoreEventSessions · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/ScoreEventSessions/IAiScoringService.cs:6 · Level 2 · interface

  • What it is: The application-layer port for scoring a single conference session with an AI model. Its contract guarantees it never throws, failure is reported in the returned result.
  • Depends on: SessionScoringInput (Level 1) and SessionScoringResult (the co-located Level-0 result record in the same file, :40). External: BCL only (Task, CancellationToken).
  • Concept introduced, port/adapter for an external AI capability. [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (§3 assesses whether the application depends on abstractions while framework/SDK detail stays in the outer layers; the application declares this port and the Anthropic HTTP/JSON details live in Infrastructure's AnthropicScoringService) and [Rubric §1, SOLID] (DIP, the handler depends on this interface, not the concrete API client). The "never throws, failure in the result" contract (:9) is the Result philosophy applied to an unreliable network dependency [Rubric §29, Resilience].
  • Walkthrough: Task<SessionScoringResult> ScoreSessionAsync(SessionScoringInput, CancellationToken = default) (:11-13) returns a result whose Success flag (not an exception) signals failure; string ModelId { get; } (:16) exposes which model produced a score, so the persisted SessionAiScore.ModelUsed is auditable.
  • Why it's built this way: Defining the port in Application lets the scoring use-case be unit-tested with a fake scorer and lets the AI vendor be swapped without touching the handler (ADR-007's port/adapter spirit applied to an outbound integration).

GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetSessionSelectionDashboard · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetSessionSelectionDashboard/GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler.cs:16 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: The composite analytics handler for the organizer's session-selection dashboard. In one query it loads every non-service session for an event (plus speakers, categories, and AI scores) and computes summary counts, category distribution, speaker overlap, speaker-locality rollups, and an AI-score leaderboard.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult>, the Event, Session, Speaker, Category, and SessionAiScore aggregates; SpeakerLocalityHelper for the locality tiers; the private StatusBucket enum; SessionStatuses; and the result shape SessionSelectionDashboardDTO with its nested CategoryDistributionDTO / CategoryGroupDistribution / CategoryItemDistribution, SpeakerSessionOverlapDTO / MultiSessionSpeaker / SpeakerSessionSummary, SpeakerLocalitySummary, and SessionAiScoreDTO.
  • Concept introduced, the composite read (load-once, compute-many). [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (§12 assesses query efficiency and N+1 avoidance; this handler does a small, fixed number of set-based loads, sessions, categories, then a batched speaker fetch by id, then scores, and computes four analytics in memory from that single working set, rather than re-querying per metric). [Rubric §8, Data Architecture]: all reads are asTracking: false (read-only projections, no change-tracker overhead). The four constituent metrics each also exist as their own decision-support query (GetCategoryDistribution, GetSpeakerSessionOverlap, and so on); this handler exists so the dashboard page makes one round trip instead of four.
  • Walkthrough: primary-constructor injection of IUnitOfWork (:16). HandleAsync (:19): validate the event exists then Error.NotFound if not (:29-31); load sessions (with SessionSpeakers + SessionCategoryItems, excluding IsServiceSession) and categories (with CategoryItems), then batch-load the distinct speakers by id via GetByIdsAsync and build a dictionary lookup (:34-57), this is the deliberate N+1 avoidance. It then builds the category-item-name and locality lookups (:60-70, the latter via SpeakerLocalityHelper), computes summary counts treating null/"Accepted" as accepted (:72-80), and delegates to private helpers: ComputeCategoryDistribution (:118, which uses CountCategoryItems/ClassifyStatus/StatusBucket), ComputeSpeakerOverlap (:180, sorted by session-count then accepted then name), ComputeSpeakerLocality (:249, rolled up per tier), and finally BuildAiScoreDtos (:331, which splits each session's category items into a "Level" item vs. ordinary categories and orders by overall score). The assembled SessionSelectionDashboardDTO is returned in Result.Success (:102-115).
  • Why it's built this way: A single composite query keeps the dashboard snappy and consistent (all metrics reflect the same snapshot). The comment at :33 notes loads are sequential by design, one EF DbContext is not thread-safe, so concurrent awaits on the same context are avoided.
  • Where it's used: Dispatched from the organizer dashboard endpoint (GetSessionSelectionDashboardQuery); the DTO feeds the Conference UI dashboard page.

GetSpeakerSessionOverlapHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.GetSpeakerSessionOverlap · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/GetSpeakerSessionOverlap/GetSpeakerSessionOverlapHandler.cs:18 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: An analytics handler that returns every speaker who submitted at least one session for an event, each annotated with their locality tier and their sessions' categories/statuses, and sorts the list so multi-session speakers surface first (session-count descending, then accepted presence, then name). The name "overlap" reflects that sort intent, not a filter: single-session speakers are still returned (the UI shows a session-count column for all). It is the standalone version of the overlap metric also embedded in the composite dashboard.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult>, the Session / Speaker / Category aggregates, SpeakerLocalityHelper, SessionStatuses, and the result shape SpeakerSessionOverlapDTO / MultiSessionSpeaker / SpeakerSessionSummary.
  • Concept: Same load-once/compute pattern and [Rubric §12] N+1 avoidance as GetSessionSelectionDashboardHandler, at smaller scope: it groups sessions by speaker first, then fetches only the speakers that actually appear and short-circuits to an empty DTO when none do (:38-39). Speaker locality comes from a category, not a Speaker field, see SpeakerLocalityHelper and the "Where are you traveling from" category note.
  • Walkthrough: primary-constructor injection of IUnitOfWork (:18). HandleAsync (:21): load non-service sessions with SessionSpeakers + SessionCategoryItems (:29-33); GroupSessionsBySpeaker (:61) builds a speakerId to List<Session> map (called at :35); if empty, return an empty SpeakerSessionOverlapDTO (:38-39); otherwise GetByIdsAsync the speakers (:41-45) and GetAllAsync the categories (:47-50), build the locality + category-name lookups (:52-54), and BuildMultiSessionSpeakers (:99) assembles one MultiSessionSpeaker per speaker, each session list sorted by title (:121-123), then sorts the whole list by session-count, then accepted-flag, then name (:127-137).
  • Why it's built this way: Standalone slice for the cases where the UI wants only the overlap table; it deliberately mirrors the composite handler's algorithm so both views agree.

ScoreEventSessionsHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport.ScoreEventSessions · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/ScoreEventSessions/ScoreEventSessionsHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class (sealed, partial)

  • What it is: The command handler that (re)scores every session in an event with the AI model. It wipes prior scores, then scores sessions one at a time, persisting each score immediately so the dashboard shows live progress, and reports how many succeeded vs. failed.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IAiScoringService, ILogger<T>, ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>, the Session / Speaker aggregates and the SessionAiScore aggregate (its Create factory), the input/result records SessionScoringInput / SpeakerInfo / SessionScoringResult, and the result DTO ScoreEventSessionsResultDTO.
  • Concept introduced, incremental persistence for live progress + source-generated logging. [Rubric §13, Observability & Operability] (§13 assesses structured, low-allocation telemetry; this is a partial class using [LoggerMessage] source-generated log methods, LogScoresDeleted, LogScoringStarted, LogSessionScored, LogSessionFailed, LogSessionSaveFailed, LogScoringCompleted, :127-143, so each scoring step is a compile-time-generated, allocation-free structured log line). [Rubric §29, Resilience]: a single failed session (AI failure, factory failure, or save failure) increments failed and continues instead of aborting the batch; only if every session failed does the handler return an Error.Failure("AiScoring.AllFailed", ...) (:116-122). Unlike the read handlers, this one calls SaveChangesAsync per session (not once at the end) so the dashboard's progress bar advances as scores land.
  • Walkthrough: primary-constructor injection of IUnitOfWork + IAiScoringService + ILogger (:15-18). HandleAsync (:20): load non-service sessions with speakers (:27-31); return 0/0 if none (:33-34); ExecuteDeleteAsync all existing scores for those sessions so the dashboard resets to zero (:37-45); batch-load the distinct speakers by id (:48-59). Then the per-session loop (:66-112): project each session's speakers to SpeakerInfo, build a SessionScoringInput (:68-76), call aiScoringService.ScoreSessionAsync (:77); on !Success log + count a failure and continue (:79-84); otherwise SessionAiScore.Create(...) with the seven sub-scores, reasoning, and aiScoringService.ModelId (:86-90), and if the factory fails, count a failure (:92-97); finally AddAsync + SaveChangesAsync inside a try/catch that turns a persistence exception into a counted failure (:99-111). The handler ends by logging the totals and returning ScoreEventSessionsResultDTO { SessionsScored, SessionsFailed } (:114-124).
  • Why it's built this way: Per-session save trades a few extra round trips for a responsive UI; the delete-then-rescore approach makes the run idempotent (re-running yields a clean, complete set rather than duplicates). Routing scores through the SessionAiScore.Create factory keeps the 1.0-10.0 invariants enforced by the domain rather than trusting the model's numbers blindly.
  • Where it's used: Dispatched from the organizer "Score sessions" action (ScoreEventSessionsCommand); the IAiScoringService port is satisfied by AnthropicScoringService.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: The command is not declared ITransactional; each session is its own save, so a mid-run cancellation leaves the scores written so far in place (intentional, for the live-progress UX), but that means the batch is not atomic. Not determinable from this file: whether the command is decorated as ICacheInvalidating to flush the dashboard's output-cache (that wiring lives in the controller/feature registration, not the handler).

GetPublicSessionFilterHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.GetPublicSessionFilter · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/GetPublicSessionFilter/GetPublicSessionFilterHandler.cs:17 · Level 9 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: The query handler behind GetPublicSessionFilterQuery. It builds the "publicly visible sessions" filter (BR-132 / BR-49) as a Specification<Session, SessionIdentifierType> that other reads apply, rather than returning any session data itself.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IQueryHandler<in TQuery, TResult>, Result, the framework helper CrossSourceSpecification and the Specification it produces, the Session and Event aggregates, and SessionStatuses. Its Level 9 comes from depending on the Level-8 CrossSourceSpecification.
  • Concept introduced, the cross-source specification (a filter that spans two data stores). [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (§8 assesses how persistence boundaries are respected; the published gate lives on Event, but the filter targets Session, and the two aggregates may live in different data sources under ADR-018 polyglot persistence). [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness]: a plain EF navigation join Session.Event.IsPublished would not be translatable when Session and Event are in separate stores, so the handler delegates to CrossSourceSpecification.BuildAsync, which resolves the principal (published Event) ids from the Event source and returns a Session.EventId IN (...) predicate ANDed with a local Session predicate, all translatable against the Session source alone.
  • Walkthrough: primary-constructor injection of IUnitOfWork (:17-18). HandleAsync (:22) calls CrossSourceSpecification.BuildAsync<Session, SessionIdentifierType, Event, EventIdentifierType> (:26-33) with: principalPredicate: e => e.IsPublished (which events count), dependentForeignKey: s => s.EventId (the join key), and localPredicate: s => s.Status != SessionStatuses.Declined && s.Status != "Cancelled" (:31, the same exclusion as SessionStatuses.IsPubliclyVisible; note "Cancelled" is a bare string literal since SessionStatuses has no such constant). It then returns Result.Success(specification) (:35), the handler never fails.
  • Why it's built this way: Expressing "publicly visible" as a specification (rather than filtering in the handler) lets the caller compose it into whatever read it is doing, list, paged, or field projection, so the visibility rule is enforced identically across all three without duplicating the predicate. Building it cross-source keeps the rule correct even when the two aggregates are stored in different engines.
  • Where it's used: Injected into the Conference SessionsController as IQueryHandler<GetPublicSessionFilterQuery, Result<Specification<Session, SessionIdentifierType>>>; its BuildPublicSessionSpecificationAsync returns the specification for non-organizer callers (and null for organizers, who see everything), then passes it as the specification: argument to the entity-query-service GetAll / paged / field-projection reads.

This record is the immutable input contract; the matching IQueryHandler implementation lives beside it in the same GetSessionBookmarkCount/ folder. GetSpeakersByEventFilterQuery

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.GetSpeakersByEventFilter · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/GetSpeakersByEventFilter/GetSpeakersByEventFilterQuery.cs:12 · Level 0 · record

  • What it is: a single-field query (EventId) whose handler returns a specification selecting every speaker that belongs to a given event. It exists because a Speaker has no EventId column; membership is a computed union of two independently-populated join paths.
  • Depends on: nothing first-party in its body; the parameter is the EventIdentifierType alias. Handled by GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler, which returns a Specification.
  • Concept, a query that returns a predicate, not data. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (assesses that cross-aggregate relationships are resolved without cross-table object-graph joins) and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (assesses that aggregates reference each other by id, preserving an extractable boundary). The doc comment (GetSpeakersByEventFilterQuery.cs:3-10) is the important teaching: a speaker is linked to an event two ways, directly through the EventSpeaker join (written by the Sessionize sync) or transitively through any SessionSpeaker of that event's sessions (written by organizer session management). Because the two link paths are filled by different flows, the handler unions them and emits an Id IN (...) filter, which stays engine-portable (no navigation join to translate).
  • Walkthrough: public sealed record GetSpeakersByEventFilterQuery(EventIdentifierType EventId) (GetSpeakersByEventFilterQuery.cs:12). The record is a marker for "resolve the speakers of this event"; all the work is in the handler.
  • Why it's built this way: returning a reusable specification (rather than a materialized list) lets the caller compose the event filter with paging, sorting, and field projection at the query-service layer instead of loading all speakers up front.
  • Where it's used: dispatched to GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler; the resulting specification feeds the paged/filtered speaker list endpoints (the organizer "Filter by Event" picker).

ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Update/ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest.cs:6 · Level 1 · record

  • What it is: the request-body DTO a client sends to update an existing conference Category: a Title, a Sort order, an optional Type, and the optimistic-concurrency token.
  • Depends on: IConcurrencyAware (the RowVersion contract). Wrapped by UpdateConferenceCategoryCommand; validated by ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequestValidator.
  • Concept, the client-supplied concurrency token. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (assesses optimistic concurrency so a late write cannot silently clobber a newer one) and [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (assesses that a stale edit surfaces as a conflict, not a silent overwrite). Implementing IConcurrencyAware means the request round-trips the EF RowVersion byte array the client last read (ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest.cs:10). The handler stamps it as the row's original value so a concurrent edit surfaces as a DbUpdateConcurrencyException, mapped to HTTP 409, rather than last-write-wins.
  • Walkthrough: a record class : IConcurrencyAware (ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest.cs:6) with four init members: RowVersion (byte[]?, line 10), Title (required string, line 13), Sort (int, line 16), Type (string?, line 19). The [SuppressMessage(... "CA1819" ...)] on RowVersion (line 9) is a scoped, justified suppression: EF's rowversion token genuinely is a byte[], so the "properties should not return arrays" analyzer is a false positive here.
  • Why it's built this way: required on Title makes an update that forgets the title a binding error; keeping RowVersion nullable lets a client that opts out of concurrency send null (the handler then just skips the check).
  • Where it's used: the payload of UpdateConferenceCategoryCommand; mapped onto the entity by UpdateConferenceCategoryHandler.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Update/EventUpdateRequest.cs:7 · Level 1 · record

  • Concept: same IConcurrencyAware optimistic-concurrency shape taught in ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest; this record just carries more fields. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design]: the request is a flat, explicit contract with required on the fields the event cannot exist without.
  • Walkthrough: a record class : IConcurrencyAware (EventUpdateRequest.cs:7). RowVersion (byte[]?, line 11) with the same CA1819 suppression (line 10); required on Name (14), StartDate/EndDate (DateOnly, 20/23) and TimeZone (the IANA identifier, 26); optional Description (17), SessionizeCode (29), VenueAddress (32), VenueMapUrl (36, with a justified CA1056 "URI-like property is a string" suppression on line 35 because it arrives as a string from the Sessionize import), and WiFiInfo (39). The last member, QuestionModerationDefault (42), threads the BR-233 default for whether live-layer session questions start moderated.
  • Why it's built this way: TimeZone is required (an IANA id, not an offset) because session times are stored and rendered relative to it; changing it is the input that trips the BR-131 warning path in UpdateEventHandler.
  • Where it's used: the payload of UpdateEventCommand; mapped onto the entity by UpdateEventHandler.

UpdateEventResult

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Update/UpdateEventCommand.cs:24 · Level 3 · record

  • What it is: a thin two-field result wrapper returned by the event-update handler: the updated EventDTO plus a boolean HasTimeZoneWarning (BR-131).
  • Depends on: EventDTO. Produced by UpdateEventHandler; it is declared in the same file as UpdateEventCommand.
  • Concept, a command that returns state plus an advisory flag. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses that a write can hand back both the new state and a non-fatal signal in one round-trip). Most update handlers return only the refreshed DTO; this one also needs to tell the caller "you changed the time zone while sessions already exist, the session start times may now be off," a warning that must not fail the update. Packaging both into UpdateEventResult lets the API surface the DTO and raise the warning without a second query.
  • Walkthrough: public sealed record UpdateEventResult(EventDTO Event, bool HasTimeZoneWarning) (UpdateEventCommand.cs:24). HasTimeZoneWarning is false unless the handler detected a time-zone change against a session-bearing event.
  • Why it's built this way: separating the advisory (HasTimeZoneWarning) from the success/failure axis keeps BR-131 as a soft warning: the write still succeeds and returns the new EventDTO; the UI decides whether to prompt the organizer to review session times.
  • Where it's used: the payload of the Result<UpdateEventResult> returned by UpdateEventHandler; unwrapped by the Events controller.

GetSessionBookmarkCountHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.GetSessionBookmarkCount · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/GetSessionBookmarkCount/GetSessionBookmarkCountHandler.cs:14 · Level 8 · class

  • What it is: the query handler that authorizes a speaker against a session and then asks the Engagement module for that session's bookmark count (BR-210).
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IBookmarkCountService, Session, Result/Error, and its query GetSessionBookmarkCountQuery. Implements IQueryHandler.
  • Concept, cross-module read through a service seam. [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (assesses that one module reaches another only through an interface, so the two can run in separate processes) and [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses an ownership/authorization check before returning data). The handler enforces its own bounded context (loads the Session, checks the speaker is assigned) and then delegates the count itself to the Engagement bounded context via IBookmarkCountService, a Conference-local interface that resolves to a real gRPC call when Engagement is a remote service, or a disabled stub when it is not present (ADR-007).
  • Walkthrough: a sealed class(IUnitOfWork unitOfWork, IBookmarkCountService bookmarkCountService) (GetSessionBookmarkCountHandler.cs:14, primary-constructor DI). HandleAsync (line 19): loads the session with its SessionSpeakers included, asTracking: false for a read (lines 23-28); returns Error.NotFound if absent (line 30); then verifies the speaker is assigned via session.SessionSpeakers.Any(ss => ss.SpeakerId == query.SpeakerId && !ss.IsDeleted) and returns Error.Forbidden("Speaker.NotAssigned", ...) if not (lines 33-40). Only after authorization does it call bookmarkCountService.GetBookmarkCountForSessionAsync(query.SessionId, ...) (line 43) and return Result.Success(count) (line 45).
  • Why it's built this way: the assignment check runs against Conference's own data (the SessionSpeakers it owns), so authorization does not depend on Engagement being reachable; the count, which is Engagement's data, is the only cross-module hop. That split keeps the security decision local and the boundary clean.
  • Where it's used: invoked through the CQRS pipeline from the Speakers controller / gRPC edge; the count feeds a speaker's session dashboard.

GetSessionFeedbackHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.GetSessionFeedback · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/GetSessionFeedback/GetSessionFeedbackHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class

  • What it is: the query handler that aggregates a session's answered feedback into average ratings and grouped free-text responses, after authorizing the requesting speaker (BR-210).
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, Session (and its SessionQuestionAnswer children), Question, the read models SessionFeedbackDTO / RatingQuestionSummary / TextQuestionResponses, and Result/Error. Implements IQueryHandler.
  • Concept, in-handler read-model projection. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (a query composes a purpose-built read model, decoupled from the write model) and [Rubric §27, Internationalization & Localization] (culture-invariant parsing where locale would introduce bugs). Feedback answers are stored as strings; the handler parses "Rating" answers as integers using CultureInfo.InvariantCulture (GetSessionFeedbackHandler.cs:76) so a comma-decimal locale can never mis-read a rating, the same deliberate culture-invariance the primer flags for identifier parsing (primer §6).
  • Walkthrough: a sealed class(IUnitOfWork unitOfWork) (GetSessionFeedbackHandler.cs:15). HandleAsync (line 19): loads the session with both SessionSpeakers and SessionQuestionAnswers included, untracked (lines 23-28); Error.NotFound if absent (line 30); the same speaker-assignment Error.Forbidden gate as the bookmark handler (lines 33-40). If there are no answers it returns an empty SessionFeedbackDTO early (lines 44-53). Otherwise it collects the distinct answered QuestionIds and loads just those Questions (lines 56-63), then groups answers by question (line 68): a "Rating" question parses its integer answers, computes Average() and ResponseCount, and emits a RatingQuestionSummary (lines 73-90); any other question type emits a TextQuestionResponses carrying the raw answer strings (lines 92-100). It returns the populated DTO (lines 103-109).
  • Why it's built this way: loading only the questions that actually have answers (a Contains over a HashSet of ids, lines 56-60) avoids pulling the whole question bank; relying on EF's soft-delete global query filter (noted at line 42) means deleted answers never reach the aggregation. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: untracked reads plus a scoped question load keep the query cheap.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the rating-vs-text split keys off the magic string "Rating" (line 73); any other QuestionType is treated as free text, and non-integer rating answers are silently dropped from the average rather than erroring.
  • Where it's used: invoked through the CQRS pipeline from the Speakers surface to render a speaker's session-feedback view.

GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.GetSpeakersByEventFilter · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/GetSpeakersByEventFilter/GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler.cs:19 · Level 8 · class

  • What it is: the handler that resolves the two speaker-link paths of an event, unions them, and returns an Id IN (...) Specification selecting exactly those Speakers.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, EventSpeaker, Session, SessionSpeaker, Speaker, Specification / InlineSpecification, and Result. Implements IQueryHandler returning Result<Specification<Speaker, SpeakerIdentifierType>>.
  • Concept, ID-list unions instead of cross-aggregate joins. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness]. A Speaker references Event/Session only by id, so the handler resolves membership as three projected id lists rather than a navigation join. The doc comment (GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler.cs:11-18) states the design: the shape mirrors the framework's CrossSourceSpecification helper (BR-132 precedent), so the resulting Speaker.Id IN (...) predicate stays translatable on any engine and the Speaker aggregate keeps its by-id boundary to the Event/Session aggregates.
  • Walkthrough: a sealed class(IUnitOfWork unitOfWork) (GetSpeakersByEventFilterHandler.cs:19). HandleAsync (line 24) runs three read-repository projections via GetReadRepository<...>().GetProjectedAsync(...): (1) the directly-linked speaker ids from EventSpeaker where EventId == query.EventId (lines 28-31); (2) the event's session ids from Session (lines 33-36); (3) only if sessions exist, the transitively-linked speaker ids from SessionSpeaker whose SessionId is in a materialized session-id list (lines 39-47, the comment on line 41 notes the list is materialized once so EF embeds a stable IN collection). It concatenates and de-duplicates the two speaker-id sets (Concat(...).Distinct(), line 50) and returns Result.Success of an InlineSpecification whose criterion is s => speakerIds.Contains(s.Id) (lines 52-53).
  • Why it's built this way: projecting ids (not entities) and unioning them keeps the final predicate a single IN filter the query service can compose with paging/sorting; guarding the third query on sessionIds.Count > 0 skips a needless round-trip for an event with no sessions.
  • Where it's used: the returned specification is applied by the paged speaker list endpoints (the organizer "Filter by Event" picker and the event-scoped speaker lists).

UpdateConferenceCategoryHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Update/UpdateConferenceCategoryHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class

  • What it is: the command handler that loads a Category, applies the optimistic-concurrency token, delegates to the entity's Update method, persists, and returns the mapped DTO.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, Category, ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper, ConferenceCategoryDTO, Result/Error, and ILogger (BCL). Implements ICommandHandler for UpdateConferenceCategoryCommand.

[Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design] (mutation happens through the aggregate's own Update method, which returns a Result so invariants are enforced inside the boundary), [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (a stale write becomes a 409, not a silent overwrite), and [Rubric §13, Observability & Operability] (structured, allocation-free logging). This is the canonical "load, stamp concurrency, delegate to domain, save, map" shape; the concurrency stamp is the concrete counterpart to ConferenceCategoryUpdateRequest's RowVersion.

The [LoggerMessage] partial method (lines 49-50) is why the class is partial.
  • Why it's built this way: mutation lives on the domain entity, so the handler only orchestrates load/stamp/save/map, keeping the write path thin; cache eviction is handled outside the handler by the pipeline because UpdateConferenceCategoryCommand is ICacheInvalidating, and audit fields are stamped centrally by SaveChangesAsync.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.{Sessions,Speakers}.UseCases.Update · Level 1 · records

Two update-request DTOs that carry an edit payload from the API surface into the matching update command. Both are public record class implementing IConcurrencyAware, they round-trip the EF rowversion optimistic-concurrency token so a stale write is rejected with a 409 instead of silently clobbering a newer edit.

UpdateSessionResult

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Update/UpdateSessionCommand.cs:24 · Level 3 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: a two-field result wrapper carried back from the session-update handler: the updated SessionDTO plus a bool HasDateRangeWarning.
  • Depends on: SessionDTO (Level 2).
  • Concept introduced, the "command returns updated entity + a soft warning" shape. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design]: most update handlers return the post-update DTO so the UI can refresh without a second GET; this one adds a non-fatal advisory. HasDateRangeWarning reports BR-86 , the session's start/end fall outside the parent event's date range, without failing the request. The edit still succeeds; the flag lets the controller surface a "are you sure?" hint. Contrast a hard rule like BR-140 (changing EventId), which the handler returns as a Result failure. Separating "warning" from "error" is the design point: not every business concern should block a write.
  • Walkthrough: a positional sealed record UpdateSessionResult(SessionDTO Session, bool HasDateRangeWarning) (line 24), co-located in the same file as UpdateSessionCommand. No methods.
  • Why it's built this way: wrapping the DTO in a record (instead of returning a bare SessionDTO) leaves a typed slot for the warning flag and room for future advisory fields without breaking the command's return type.
  • Where it's used: produced by UpdateSessionHandler (Result<UpdateSessionResult>); unwrapped by the Conference SessionsController. The speaker-update path has no equivalent wrapper , UpdateSpeakerHandler returns a bare Result<SpeakerDTO> because no speaker business rule produces a soft warning.

  • Depends on: IDomainEventHandler<in TDomainEvent> (Level 1); SessionChanged (Level 3); DomainEntityState (Level 0); ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the domain-event-handler pattern. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses whether state changes are propagated by events rather than direct calls). The pattern: one aggregate raises a single SessionChanged event for every lifecycle transition (Added/Modified/Deleted), and each interested handler implements IDomainEventHandler<SessionChanged> and routes on domainEvent.State to handle only the transition it cares about. Here the guard if (domainEvent.State != DomainEntityState.Added) return Task.CompletedTask; (line 17) makes this a "session created" handler over a general "session changed" event. Handlers are auto-discovered by Scrutor as singletons and invoked by the DomainEventDispatcher after SaveChangesAsync runs. [Rubric §13, Observability]: sealed partial class + [LoggerMessage] (line 24) compiles to a static, allocation-free structured log method.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (line 15): the State guard (line 17), then LogSessionCreated with SessionId, Title, EventId (line 20). The [LoggerMessage]-decorated partial method (line
    1. supplies the message template Session created: SessionId={SessionId}, ….
  • Why it's built this way: collapsing all session lifecycle signals onto one event type (SessionChanged) keeps the aggregate simple; handlers opt in to the transitions they need by filtering on state, rather than the domain defining three separate event types.
  • Where it's used: discovered and registered as a singleton by the Conference module's application-service scan; reacts to every session creation in-process.

SpeakerDeletedHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.DomainEventHandlers · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/DomainEventHandlers/SpeakerDeletedHandler.cs:20 · Level 4 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: a domain event handler for SpeakerChanged with state Deleted (BR-70). It logs the soft-delete and, when the speaker had been linked to a user account, publishes a SpeakerUnlinkedFromUser integration event so the Identity service can clear that user's LinkedSpeakerId.
  • Depends on: IDomainEventHandler<in TDomainEvent> (Level 1); SpeakerChanged (Level 3); SpeakerUnlinkedFromUser (Level 3); IIntegrationEventPublisher (Level 2); DomainEntityState (Level 0); IServiceScopeFactory, ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, a domain event raising an integration event across the service boundary. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness]: a domain event (SpeakerChanged, internal to Conference) triggers an integration event (SpeakerUnlinkedFromUser, a cross-service contract in the .Shared layer). The doc comment (lines 13-18) records the design transition this replaced: a former direct in-process call to IUserSpeakerLinkService.ClearLinkedSpeakerAsync, a hard cross-module reference, became an eventually-consistent broker message. The Identity service now reacts on its own schedule, so Conference no longer needs Identity loaded to delete a speaker (see ADR-007/008 on the extraction seam). [Rubric §29, Resilience]: the publish goes through IIntegrationEventPublisher, which writes to the outbox in the same transaction (ADR-003), so the unlink is durable and retried even if the broker is briefly down.
  • Walkthrough
    • HandleAsync (line 25): ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(domainEvent), then the state guard if (domainEvent.State != DomainEntityState.Deleted) return; (line 29).
    • Logs via [LoggerMessage] LogSpeakerDeleted (lines 32, 48) including the PreviousLinkedUserId.
    • The singleton-vs-scoped-dependency bridge (lines 38-45): because Scrutor registers domain event handlers as singletons but IIntegrationEventPublisher is scoped, the handler can't inject the publisher directly. It takes IServiceScopeFactory and opens a fresh await using var scope = scopeFactory.CreateAsyncScope() (line 40), resolves the publisher from that scope, and publishes inside it. This is the canonical pattern for using a scoped service from a singleton.
    • The publish is conditional on PreviousLinkedUserId.HasValue (line 38): a speaker who was never linked to a user emits no unlink event.
  • Why it's built this way: moving cleanup off a direct call onto an integration event is what makes the modules independently deployable; the conditional publish and the scope bridge are the two details that keep that correct (no spurious events, no captive-dependency bug).
  • Where it's used: discovered and registered as a singleton by the Conference module's application-service scan; fires whenever a Speaker is soft-deleted. Its event is consumed by Identity's SpeakerUnlinkedFromUserHandler.

UpdateQuestionHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Questions.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Questions/UseCases/Update/UpdateQuestionHandler.cs:18 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UpdateQuestionCommand. Its distinguishing feature is BR-137: QuestionType and QuestionEntity become immutable once any answer to the question exists, a rule the handler enforces by probing two answer aggregates before delegating the mutation.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7); Error (Level 1); Result (Level 2); Question (Level 5), EventQuestionAnswer (Level 5), SessionQuestionAnswer (Level 6), QuestionDTO (Level 1), QuestionDTOMapper (this group); ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept reinforced, a handler-owned rule that needs cross-aggregate context. The base flow (load → guard concurrency → delegate to domain → save → map) is taught at UpdateSpeakerHandler. What this handler adds, with line numbers:
    • Load and not-found guard (lines 28-31): unitOfWork.GetRepository<Question, QuestionIdentifierType>().GetByIdAsync(...); a null returns Result.Failure<QuestionDTO>(Error.NotFound.WithSource(...).WithTarget(nameof(Question))) → a 404.
    • Optimistic concurrency (line 35): repository.SetOriginalRowVersion(entity, command.Request.RowVersion) stamps the client's last-seen token so a concurrent write surfaces as DbUpdateConcurrencyException → 409.
    • BR-137 immutable-after-answers (lines 37-62): the check runs only if QuestionType or QuestionEntity actually changed (lines 38-39), a short-circuit that avoids the extra queries on the common path. It probes two aggregates through read-only repositories (unitOfWork.GetReadRepository<…>(), lines 41, 48): first EventQuestionAnswer, and only if that finds none, SessionQuestionAnswer, each via ExistsAsync(a => a.QuestionId.Equals(entity.Id), …) (lines 42-44, 49-51). If either holds an answer, it returns Error.Validation("Question.ImmutableAfterAnswers", …) → 400 (lines 54-61). [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: GetReadRepository (non-tracking) for the existence probes vs. GetRepository for the tracked entity, plus the field-change guard that skips the probes entirely when the immutable fields are untouched.
    • Delegate to the domain (lines 64-69): entity.Update(QuestionText, QuestionEntity, QuestionType, Sort, IsRequired) returns a Result; a broken invariant short-circuits with those errors verbatim (lines 71-72).
    • Persist, log, map (lines 74-78): await unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(...), then LogQuestionUpdated ([LoggerMessage] lines 81-82), then dtoMapper.MapToDTO(entity).
    • [Rubric §4, DDD]: self-contained invariants stay inside entity.Update; the cross-aggregate rule (does an answer exist anywhere?) sits in the handler because the Question aggregate cannot see the answer aggregates, the same division of labor as UpdateSessionHandler's room check.
  • Why it's built this way: BR-137 protects data integrity (changing a question's type after people have answered it would orphan or misread their answers), and it can only be evaluated with knowledge of two other aggregates, so it lives in the handler, guarded by the cheap field-change check to keep the common edit path a single read.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the QuestionsController through the dispatcher (so logging/caching decorators wrap it).

UpdateSpeakerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/Update/UpdateSpeakerHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UpdateSpeakerCommand. It loads the speaker, stamps the concurrency token, delegates the mutation to the domain entity's Update method, persists, and returns the updated SpeakerDTO. It is the simpler of the two update handlers in this unit, no cross-aggregate checks.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7); Error (Level 1); Result (Level 2); Speaker, SpeakerDTOMapper (lower in this group); ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the canonical update-handler flow (load → guard concurrency → delegate to domain → save → map). [Rubric §6, CQRS] and [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]. The standard steps, with line numbers:
    • Resolve the repository through the unit of work (line 25): unitOfWork.GetRepository<Speaker, SpeakerIdentifierType>(), the handler never sees DbContext.
    • Load and not-found guard (lines 26-28): a null entity returns Result.Failure<SpeakerDTO>(Error.NotFound.WithSource(...).WithTarget(nameof(Speaker))) → a 404 at the API boundary.
    • Optimistic concurrency (line 32): repository.SetOriginalRowVersion(entity, command.Request.RowVersion) stamps the client's last-seen EF rowversion so a concurrent write surfaces as DbUpdateConcurrencyException → 409. See IConcurrencyAware.
    • Delegate the mutation to the domain entity (lines 34-46): entity.Update(firstName, lastName, …, linkedUserId) returns a Result; if it fails (a broken invariant) the handler returns those errors verbatim (lines 48-49). The entity, not the handler, owns its state-transition rules.
    • Persist and map (lines 51-55): await unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(...) (which also dispatches any domain events the Update raised), then dtoMapper.MapToDTO(entity) to project the read DTO.
    • [Rubric §13, Observability]: a [LoggerMessage] LogSpeakerUpdated (lines 53, 58).
  • Why it's built this way: the handler is a thin orchestrator: it owns persistence and concurrency plumbing while the domain entity owns business validity. That split is the recurring shape across every update handler in the codebase.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the SpeakersController through the dispatcher (so logging/caching decorators wrap it).

UpdateSessionHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Update · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Update/UpdateSessionHandler.cs:17 · Level 9 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UpdateSessionCommand, and the fullest update flow in this unit: it adds an immutable-field guard, a cross-aggregate room check, and a soft date-range warning on top of the standard load → concurrency → delegate → save → map shape.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7); Error (Level 1); Result (Level 2); Session and Event domain entities; UpdateSessionResult, SessionDTOMapper (this group); ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept reinforced, handler-owned business rules that need cross-aggregate context. The base flow is taught at UpdateSpeakerHandler. What this handler adds, and why the handler (not the entity) is the right place: each rule needs context the Session aggregate doesn't hold (the request, or the parent Event).
    • Concurrency stamp (line 34): identical to the speaker handler.
    • BR-140 immutable EventId (lines 37-44): if command.Request.EventId != entity.EventId, return Error.UnprocessableEntity("Session.EventId.Immutable", …) → 422. A session cannot be moved between events; the handler enforces it because it can compare request vs. stored state.
    • Cross-aggregate read of the parent event (lines 47-54): eventRepo.GetByIdAsync(entity.EventId, includes: [nameof(Event.Rooms)], asTracking: false, …), a non-tracking read of the parent Event with its Rooms eagerly loaded, used purely for validation. asTracking: false avoids EF tracking an entity the handler won't modify. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: deliberate non-tracking + explicit includes instead of lazy loading.
    • BR-130 room cross-event check (lines 57-68): if a RoomId is supplied, it must exist among the parent event's non-deleted rooms; otherwise Error.Validation("Session.RoomId.CrossEvent", …) → 400. This prevents assigning a session to a room belonging to a different event, a rule that is impossible to enforce inside the Session aggregate alone, which is exactly why it lives here.
    • Delegate to the domain (lines 70-87): entity.Update(...) with the full session field set; failure short-circuits with its errors.
    • BR-86 soft date-range warning (lines 90-92, 105-113): the private static IsOutsideEventDateRange compares DateOnly.FromDateTime(startsAt/endsAt) against the event's StartDate/EndDate. The result is a bool, not an error, the update still succeeds.
    • Persist, log, wrap (lines 94-98): SaveChangesAsync, then Result.Success(new UpdateSessionResult(dtoMapper.MapToDTO(entity), hasDateRangeWarning)), the DTO plus the advisory flag.
    • [Rubric §4, DDD]: hard invariants that belong to the session alone stay inside entity.Update; rules that span aggregates (room ownership, immutable parent, date-range advisory) sit in the handler with access to both the request and the parent event.
  • Why it's built this way: the update handler is intentionally heavier than the create handler because the business-rule cross-checks need adjacent-aggregate context; the handler orchestrates that while the domain entity stays concerned only with its own state transition. Separating the soft warning (BR-86) from the hard failures (BR-130/BR-140) lets the UI advise without blocking.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the SessionsController through the dispatcher; its UpdateSessionResult is unwrapped to set a warning header/flag on the response.

These two commands are the write side of the CategoryItem child collection, the values a conference organizer adds to or removes from a Category (the topic/locality taxonomies the Sessionize import populates).
