Type File:Line Carries Differs
AddCategoryItemCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/AddCategoryItem/AddCategoryItemCommand.cs:19 CategoryId, nullable CategoryItemId, Name, Sort item id is CategoryItemIdentifierType?, null ⇒ DB-generated identity, non-null ⇒ Sessionize-assigned id
RemoveCategoryItemCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/RemoveCategoryItem/RemoveCategoryItemCommand.cs:15 CategoryId, CategoryItemId no Name/Sort, delete needs only the ids
  • What they are: request DTOs for two of the three child-item mutations on the Category aggregate. They are transport, not behavior: the rules and state changes live on the aggregate (Category.AddCategoryItem/RemoveCategoryItem, Category.cs:131/192), invoked by the handlers below.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating; the identifier aliases ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType and CategoryItemIdentifierType (the module's strongly-typed id global usings, see the identifier-alias convention); and Category only for typeof(Category).FullName in the cache-prefix expression. No EF, no ASP.NET, these are pure Application-layer messages.
  • Concept introduced, ICacheInvalidating on a command, and the cache-prefix idiom. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns] (assesses whether caching is handled in one composable place rather than smeared across handlers; here it is a marker interface read by a pipeline decorator). A command that mutates cached read data implements ICacheInvalidating and exposes a CachePrefix. Both return the same prefix, $"{typeof(Category).FullName}:" (AddCategoryItemCommand.cs:26, RemoveCategoryItemCommand.cs:20), because a category item lives inside the category aggregate's cached projection, so any item change must evict every cached Category entry. The CachingCommandDecorator in the CQRS pipeline reads this prefix after the handler succeeds and purges matching keys; the handlers themselves never touch the cache. Using typeof(Category).FullName rather than a hand-typed string means a namespace/rename can't silently desynchronize the write-side prefix from the read-side key. [Rubric §6, CQRS] also applies: these are the canonical commands of CQRS, they mutate and return a Result, kept physically separate from the read/query side.
  • Walkthrough: each is a positional sealed record (a few primitive parameters, no body beyond the one expression-bodied CachePrefix). The only structural variation is the item-id parameter: AddCategoryItemCommand makes it nullable (CategoryItemId at AddCategoryItemCommand.cs:21) so the same command serves both a fresh DB-generated item and a Sessionize-assigned id, while RemoveCategoryItemCommand requires it (it names an existing row) and drops Name/Sort entirely, a delete needs no payload.
  • Why it's built this way: a record-per-use-case is the vertical slice unit ([Rubric §5, Vertical Slice]): command + validator + handler sit together in one UseCases/{Operation}/ folder, so a feature is added or read as a cohesive whole, not assembled from scattered horizontal layers. Immutability (record) means a command can't be mutated mid-pipeline by a decorator.
  • Where it's used: constructed by the Categories REST controller (G20) from the Add/RemoveCategoryItemRequest wire records and dispatched through the command pipeline to AddCategoryItemHandler and RemoveCategoryItemHandler. AddCategoryItemCommand is validated by AddCategoryItemCommandValidator before the handler runs; RemoveCategoryItemCommand has no validator (its only inputs are ids).

CategoryItemDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.DTOs · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/DTOs/CategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:12 · Level 6 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the entity→DTO mapper for a single category item: maps CategoryItem → CategoryItemDTO, implemented as a Mapperly source-generated mapper.
  • Depends on: CategoryItem, CategoryItemDTO, IEntityDTOMapper<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>, and the external Riok.Mapperly generator ([Mapper], [UseMapper]).
  • Concept introduced, compile-time DTO mapping via Mapperly (ADR-001). [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses deliberate, explicit, stable mapping contracts, no reflection "convention magic"). ADR-001 rejected AutoMapper because its name-convention matching silently mis-maps when a DTO field diverges from the entity field, and the runtime reflection is neither traceable nor allocation-free. The codebase's answer is Mapperly: the class is partial, decorated [Mapper] (CategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:11), and declares public partial CategoryItemDTO MapToDTO(CategoryItem entity) with no body (CategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:16); the source generator emits the property-by-property assignment at compile time. The result is explicit (you can read the generated code), fast (no reflection), and a rename that breaks the mapping is a compile error, not a runtime surprise.
  • Walkthrough: implements IEntityDTOMapper<CategoryItem, CategoryItemDTO, CategoryItemIdentifierType> (CategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:13). The single-item MapToDTO is generator-supplied; the collection overload MapToDTOs is hand-written (CategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:19-23): it null-guards with ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull then projects via a collection expression ([.. entityCollection.Select(MapToDTO)]). This split, generator for the element, manual Select for the collection, is the uniform shape across every …DTOMapper in the module.
  • Why it's built this way: see ADR-001. The IEntityDTOMapper interface lets the generic IEntityQueryService project any entity's query results to DTOs uniformly, while Mapperly keeps the per-field mapping explicit and zero-cost.
  • Where it's used: registered via Scrutor assembly scanning; injected into AddCategoryItemHandler (to map the newly-added item back to a DTO) and composed into ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper as a [UseMapper] child mapper; also used by the query service when returning category-item collections.

ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Create/ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest.cs:10 · Level 6 · record (class)

  • What it is: the create-request DTO for a new conference Category: Id (auto-generated if unset), Title (required), Sort, and an optional free-text Type ("session"/"speaker"). It doubles as the command, the create flow has no separate command record; the request is dispatched directly to CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.
  • Depends on: ICreateRequest, ICacheInvalidating, the ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType alias, and Category (for the cache-prefix typeof).
  • Concept introduced, the request-as-command via ICreateRequest. [Rubric §5, Vertical Slice] and [Rubric §6, CQRS]. Implementing ICreateRequest (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest.cs:10) is what lets the generic request-mapper pipeline pick this type up: the create handler doesn't construct the entity itself, it asks an IEntityRequestMapper to do so (see ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper). It also implements ICacheInvalidating with the same $"{typeof(Category).FullName}:" prefix (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest.cs:13) the item commands use, so creating a category evicts the category read cache.
  • Walkthrough: a record class (reference type, not the record struct used for tiny auth DTOs, it carries init properties and needs nominal-style required). Title is required string (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest.cs:19) so the compiler forces callers to set it; Id, Sort, and nullable Type default sensibly. Every property is get; init;, set at construction, immutable after.
  • Why it's built this way: folding the wire request and the command into one type removes a near-empty hand-written command record for the create case; the request mapper supplies the translation seam to the domain factory, keeping validation (in the domain Create) where it belongs.
  • Where it's used: bound by the Categories controller (G20), validated by ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestValidator, translated by ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper, and handled by CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.

AddCategoryItemCommandValidator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.AddCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/AddCategoryItem/AddCategoryItemCommandValidator.cs:7 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the FluentValidation validator for AddCategoryItemCommand. It Includes the two reusable category-item rule sets and adds nothing of its own (AddCategoryItemCommandValidator.cs:11-12).
  • Depends on: the external FluentValidation AbstractValidator<T>; and the module's reusable rule sets CategoryItemNameRules<T> and CategoryItemSortRules<T> (defined elsewhere in this group).
  • Concept introduced, composable validation via Include(ruleSet). [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] / [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses input validation that is consistent and not duplicated). Rather than re-declaring the "name not empty, within max length" and "sort ≥ 0" rules in every command that touches a category item, the rules are authored once as generic AbstractValidator<T> subclasses parameterized by a property selector, and this validator simply Includes them (Include(new CategoryItemNameRules<AddCategoryItemCommand>(p => p.Name)) and the matching CategoryItemSortRules, lines 11-12). The selector lambda re-targets the same rule onto whichever command property holds the value. Validation runs in the pipeline before the handler (the ValidatingCommandDecorator), so AddCategoryItemHandler can assume well-formed input and does no field-level checks of its own.
  • Why it's built this way: DRY validation: one rule set, many commands. A change to the name length limit happens in one place and propagates to add, update, and any future command that includes it. (RemoveCategoryItemCommand has no validator, its only inputs are two ids with nothing to validate, so the slice deliberately omits one; the update-item command's validator is a sibling that includes the very same rule sets.)
  • Where it's used: auto-registered via Scrutor scanning and resolved by the validation pipeline decorator when AddCategoryItemCommand is dispatched.

ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Create/ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper.cs:11 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the request→entity translator for category creation: turns a ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest into a Category by delegating to the domain factory Category.Create (Category.cs:54).
  • Depends on: IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType>, Category, Result (Result<Category>), and the ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType alias.
  • Concept introduced, the request-mapper seam (domain construction stays in the domain). [Rubric §4, DDD] (assesses whether invariants live in the domain) and [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (the Application layer orchestrates; it does not encode entity-construction rules). Implementing IEntityRequestMapper gives the generic create-handler a uniform CreateEntityAsync hook; the implementation here is a one-liner that forwards request.Id/Title/Sort/Type straight into Category.Create(...) (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper.cs:19-23), which is the only place a Category is constructed and is where its invariants (title required, etc.) run. The mapper returns the factory's Result<Category> verbatim, so a domain validation failure flows back through the handler as a failure result rather than an exception.
  • Walkthrough: CreateEntityAsync (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper.cs:15) null-guards the request, then return Task.FromResult(Category.Create(...)). It is synchronous work wrapped in a Task, the interface is async (other request mappers may do I/O, e.g. look up related aggregates), but category creation needs none, so it wraps the factory result. The CancellationToken parameter is accepted (interface contract) and unused here.
  • Why it's built this way: separating translate the wire request (this mapper) from orchestrate persistence (CreateConferenceCategoryHandler) keeps the handler pure orchestration and keeps construction logic in the domain factory, the request mapper is the thin adapter between them.
  • Where it's used: injected into CreateConferenceCategoryHandler (as the IEntityRequestMapper<Category, ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest, …> dependency); registered via Scrutor.

ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestValidator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Create/ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestValidator.cs:7 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the FluentValidation validator for ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest; a single composed rule set for the category Title.
  • Depends on: external FluentValidation AbstractValidator<T>; the reusable rule set ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T>.
  • Concept: same Include(ruleSet) composition as the category-item validator above (see AddCategoryItemCommandValidator); here the constructor is a single expression: Include(new ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<…>(p => p.Title)) (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestValidator.cs:10). The not-empty and max-length rules live in the shared ConferenceCategoryTitleRules<T> set; the validator just points them at Title.
  • Why it's built this way: reuse: the same title rule set is includable by any future category command (e.g. an update-with-request command) without copy-paste.
  • Where it's used: Scrutor-registered; run by the validation pipeline before CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.

ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.DTOs · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/DTOs/ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper.cs:13 · Level 7 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the entity→DTO mapper for the category aggregate root: Category → ConferenceCategoryDTO, including its child CategoryItem collection. A Mapperly mapper that composes the child-item mapper.
  • Depends on: Category, ConferenceCategoryDTO, CategoryItemDTOMapper (injected), IEntityDTOMapper<...>, external Riok.Mapperly.
  • Concept introduced, nested mapper composition via [UseMapper]. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (mapping a parent aggregate and its children consistently from one source-generated path). This mapper is Level 7 (one above the leaf CategoryItemDTOMapper) precisely because it depends on that child mapper: the category DTO embeds a list of item DTOs, and rather than re-emit item mapping, Mapperly is told to reuse the existing one. The child mapper is taken as a primary-constructor parameter (ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper.cs:13-14), stashed in a private readonly field tagged [UseMapper] (ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper.cs:17-18); the generator then routes any CategoryItem→CategoryItemDTO conversion inside MapToDTO through that field. This is the manual-mapping discipline (ADR-001) scaled to an aggregate: explicit, generated, and assembled from smaller explicit mappers.
  • Walkthrough: implements IEntityDTOMapper<Category, ConferenceCategoryDTO, ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType> (ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper.cs:15). MapToDTO is generator-supplied (:21); MapToDTOs is the same hand-written, null-guarded [.. Select(MapToDTO)] collection projection (:24-28) as in CategoryItemDTOMapper. The [UseMapper] field is the only difference from a leaf mapper.
  • Why it's built this way: composition over duplication: the aggregate mapper delegates child mapping instead of redefining it, so a change to CategoryItem mapping flows automatically into the category mapper. DI-injecting the child mapper (rather than new-ing it) keeps both individually testable and Scrutor-registrable.
  • Where it's used: injected into CreateConferenceCategoryHandler (to map the created category back to a DTO) and used by the query service for category read endpoints.

AddCategoryItemHandler, CreateConferenceCategoryHandler, RemoveCategoryItemHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.* · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

Three of the four command handlers of the Categories slice (the fourth, UpdateCategoryItemHandler, is a sibling covered elsewhere in this chapter). All implement ICommandHandler<TCommand, TResult> with one HandleAsync, depend on IUnitOfWork and ILogger, and are sealed partial (the partial half is the [LoggerMessage]-generated logging method). They split into two micro-patterns: create-from-request (one handler) and load-aggregate / call-domain-method / save (two handlers).

Type File:Line Pattern Domain call Returns
CreateConferenceCategoryHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/Create/CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.cs:16 create-from-request via ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestMapper → Category.Create Result<ConferenceCategoryDTO>
AddCategoryItemHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/AddCategoryItem/AddCategoryItemHandler.cs:15 load / mutate / save Category.AddCategoryItem (Category.cs:131) Result<CategoryItemDTO>
RemoveCategoryItemHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/RemoveCategoryItem/RemoveCategoryItemHandler.cs:13 load / mutate / save Category.RemoveCategoryItem (Category.cs:192) Result
  • What they are: CQRS use-case handlers for creating a category and for adding/removing its items. They are thin orchestration over the Category aggregate; all business rules (item-name uniqueness BR-138, not-found, etc.) live on the aggregate's domain methods, not here (Category.cs:136).
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, Category, Result/Error, ICommandHandler<...>, ILogger. The DTO-returning handlers also take a Mapperly mapper: CategoryItemDTOMapper (Add) or ConferenceCategoryDTOMapper + IEntityRequestMapper (Create). RemoveCategoryItemHandler takes only IUnitOfWork + ILogger (it returns a bare Result, no DTO to map).
  • Concept reinforced, the aggregate as the unit of consistency, and SaveChangesAsync as the single seam to the framework. [Rubric §4, DDD] and [Rubric §6, CQRS]. The canonical load/mutate/save body (AddCategoryItemHandler.cs:25-38): get the typed repository (unitOfWork.GetRepository<Category, ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType>()), load the aggregate, bail with Error.NotFound.WithSource(...).WithTarget(nameof(Category)) if absent, call the domain method (category.AddCategoryItem(...)), and on success await unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(...). The handler never writes to the DB directly, that one SaveChangesAsync call is what triggers audit stamping, domain-event capture, and outbox writes (G07/the outbox, ADR-003). Two mechanics worth internalizing:
    • Remove loads the child collection and tracks it. RemoveCategoryItemHandler passes includes: [nameof(Category.CategoryItems)] and asTracking: true (RemoveCategoryItemHandler.cs:30-44), because the domain method walks the items collection and EF must have it loaded and tracked. AddCategoryItemHandler skips the include, it's appending, not searching.
    • RemoveCategoryItemHandler carries a real-world workaround. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design]. Because the UI's generic delete sends only the item id (so CategoryId arrives as the default 0), the handler resolves the owning category from the item when CategoryId == default: it queries GetAllAsync with a where: c => c.CategoryItems.Any(ci => ci.Id == command.CategoryItemId) predicate (RemoveCategoryItemHandler.cs:28-44) instead of GetByIdAsync. The inline comment documents exactly this (RemoveCategoryItemHandler.cs:24-26). (This is the fix recorded in the team's categoryitem_delete_query_param_bug note, the controller's [FromQuery] parentId bound to 0 and 404'd before the handler learned to fall back.)
  • Walkthrough, the create handler differs. CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.HandleAsync (CreateConferenceCategoryHandler.cs:23-40) does not load an aggregate: it calls requestMapper.CreateEntityAsync(command) → Category.Create (returning Result<Category>), bails on failure, then repository.AddAsync + SaveChangesAsync, logs, and returns the mapped ConferenceCategoryDTO. Validation has already run in the pipeline (via ConferenceCategoryCreateRequestValidator), so the handler assumes well-formed input. Note the command type is the request type (ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest), ICommandHandler<ConferenceCategoryCreateRequest, Result<ConferenceCategoryDTO>>.
  • Why it's built this way: uniformity ([Rubric §16, Maintainability]). With validation, caching, transactions, audit, events, and outbox all handled below the handler (the decorator pipeline and SaveChangesAsync), each handler is a five-to-ten-line orchestration, and the analyzers + Result pattern keep them all the same shape. Pushing rules into the domain factory/methods keeps invariants in the domain ([Rubric §4, DDD]).
  • Where they're used: injected into the Categories REST controller (G20): the create handler into the aggregate-root create slot, the two item handlers into the child-collection add/remove slots. Each is wrapped by the command decorators, including the CachingCommandDecorator, which reads the ICacheInvalidating.CachePrefix the commands declare and evicts the category read cache after a successful mutation.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the validation pipeline decorator and caching decorator are framework (G05/MMCA.Common) types; their wiring is documented in that group, not re-derived here.

AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.AddEventQuestionAnswer · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/AddEventQuestionAnswer/AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:17 · Level 6 · record

  • What it is: the CQRS command to record one attendee's answer to a custom event question. It carries the target Event id, the answered Question id, the answer text, and an optional explicit id for the new EventQuestionAnswer row.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (the marker it implements); the identifier-alias types EventIdentifierType, EventQuestionAnswerIdentifierType?, QuestionIdentifierType (solution-wide aliases, see primer §2); Event (only for typeof(Event).FullName in the cache prefix).
  • Concept introduced, the command record + cache-invalidation marker. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses whether writes are modelled as explicit, intent-named commands separate from reads): a command is a small immutable record naming exactly one mutation. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns] (assesses whether concerns like caching are centralized rather than scattered): by implementing ICacheInvalidating, the command opts its handler into the CachingCommandDecorator, which evicts every cache entry under CachePrefix after the handler succeeds, the handler itself never mentions caching. The marker-interface family was introduced in the CQRS pipeline group; this is its concrete ADC use.
  • Walkthrough: a sealed record with four positional members (AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:17-21): EventId, the nullable EventQuestionAnswerId (null ⇒ the store assigns the id), QuestionId, and the string AnswerValue. The lone body member is the computed CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Event).FullName}:" (line 24), keying eviction by the Event type's full name so adding an answer busts the cached event reads that would otherwise show stale answer collections.
  • Why it's built this way: modelling the write as a record keeps it value-equatable and trivially testable; pushing cache eviction onto a decorator via a one-line marker keeps the handler free of cross-cutting noise (the same rationale behind the whole decorator pipeline, see ICacheInvalidating).
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference event-question-answer controller; handled by AddEventQuestionAnswerHandler; validated by AddEventQuestionAnswerCommandValidator.

EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper, EventSpeakerDTOMapper, RoomDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.DTOs · Level 6 · classes (sealed partial)

A family of three structurally-identical Mapperly mappers, one per child entity of the Event aggregate. Each implements IEntityDTOMapper<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> for its own entity/DTO pair and does nothing but the obvious property-by-property copy.

Type File:Line Maps
EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/DTOs/EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper.cs:12 EventQuestionAnswer → EventQuestionAnswerDTO
EventSpeakerDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/DTOs/EventSpeakerDTOMapper.cs:12 EventSpeaker → EventSpeakerDTO
RoomDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/DTOs/RoomDTOMapper.cs:12 Room → RoomDTO
  • What they are: entity→DTO mappers that turn tracked domain entities into the immutable DTOs the API returns.
  • Depends on: IEntityDTOMapper<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> (the contract); their source entity and target DTO; Riok.Mapperly (the source generator).
  • Concept introduced, compile-time mapping with Mapperly, per ADR-001. [Rubric §1, SOLID] (single responsibility, each mapper does one translation) and [Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality] (no runtime reflection). ADR-001 chose manual/explicit DTO mapping over reflection-based AutoMapper; Mapperly delivers that as a source generator. The [Mapper] attribute (line 11) and the partial keyword tell Mapperly to generate the body of partial EventQuestionAnswerDTO MapToDTO(entity) at compile time, so the mapping is plain, allocation-light, debuggable C# with no startup configuration and no reflection, see primer §3.
  • Walkthrough (all three identical, e.g. EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper.cs:12-24): the class is sealed partial, attributed [Mapper]. MapToDTO is left partial (line 16), Mapperly fills it in. MapToDTOs (lines 19-23) is hand-written: it null-guards with ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull and projects the collection through MapToDTO with a collection expression [.. entityCollection.Select(MapToDTO)].
  • Why it's built this way: generating the per-property copy keeps mapping explicit and fast while removing the boilerplate hand-mapping would cost (ADR-001). The collection overload is hand-written because it is trivial and lets the generated single-item map stay the one source of truth.
  • Where they're used: injected into the Add handlers in this group (AddEventQuestionAnswerHandler, AddEventSpeakerHandler, AddRoomHandler) to map the created child back to a DTO; also composed into EventDTOMapper via [UseMapper]; auto-registered by Scrutor scanning and used by the generic query service for read endpoints.

OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Specifications · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Specifications/OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification.cs:11 · Level 6 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: an authorization specification that narrows EventQuestionAnswer queries to rows the current user created (BR-8); attendees see only their own answers, while organizers bypass it by passing no specification.
  • Depends on: Specification<TEntity, TIdentifierType> (the base it extends); UserIdentifierType (the constructor argument); EventQuestionAnswer.
  • Concept reinforced, the Specification pattern as composable authorization. [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses whether authorization is implemented as testable, reusable policy rather than ad-hoc if checks scattered through controllers): an answerable "which rows may this user see" rule is captured as a Criteria expression that EF translates straight into the SQL WHERE, so the filter runs at the database, never by over-fetching then filtering in memory. The base pattern is taught in the querying/specifications group; this is one ADC instance.
  • Walkthrough: a primary-constructor class OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification(UserIdentifierType userId) (line 11) extending Specification<EventQuestionAnswer, EventQuestionAnswerIdentifierType>. The whole behavior is the single override Criteria => a => a.CreatedBy == userId (lines 15-16), comparing the audit CreatedBy field captured by the soft-delete/audit machinery (see primer §2).
  • Why it's built this way: encoding ownership as a specification makes it unit-testable in isolation and reusable across every read path for the entity, instead of duplicating the CreatedBy == check in each query handler.
  • Where it's used: passed to the generic entity query service by the event-question-answer read endpoints for non-organizer callers.

PublishedEventSpecification

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.Specifications · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/Specifications/PublishedEventSpecification.cs:11 · Level 6 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: a specification restricting Event queries to published events only (BR-108), applied on public/attendee read paths so unpublished drafts never leak.
  • Depends on: Specification<TEntity, TIdentifierType>; Event.
  • Concept reinforced: same Specification-as-authorization shape as OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification above. [Rubric §11, Security].
  • Walkthrough: a parameterless sealed class (no per-user state) whose only member is Criteria => e => e.IsPublished (line 14). Because it carries no constructor argument it can be a singleton-style filter applied to anonymous read requests.
  • Where it's used: applied by the events read endpoints for non-organizer callers (the organizer path omits it to see drafts too).

UpdateCategoryItemCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.UpdateCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/UpdateCategoryItem/UpdateCategoryItemCommand.cs:17 · Level 6 · record

  • What it is: the CQRS command to edit an existing category item (one of the topic/locality values a conference organizer manages) inside a Category. It carries the owning CategoryId, the CategoryItemId naming the row to mutate, and the new Name/Sort.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (the marker it implements); the identifier aliases ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType and CategoryItemIdentifierType (module-wide global usings, see primer §2); and Category only for typeof(Category).FullName in the cache prefix.
  • Concept reinforced: the same command + cache-marker shape as the event-child commands above (see AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand for the ICacheInvalidating mechanics); it also sits alongside its own add/remove sibling commands in the Categories slice. The one distinction is the cache key: this command evicts under the Category aggregate rather than the Event one. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven], [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns].
  • Walkthrough: a sealed record with four positional members (UpdateCategoryItemCommand.cs:17-21): CategoryId, the required CategoryItemId (unlike the add command's nullable id, an update must name an existing row), Name, and the int Sort. The lone body member is CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Category).FullName}:" (line 24), keying eviction on the Category type's full name because a category item lives inside the category aggregate's cached projection, so editing an item must bust every cached category read.
  • Why it's built this way: an immutable record keeps the command value-equatable and testable, and deriving the cache prefix from typeof(Category).FullName rather than a literal string keeps the write-side eviction key and the read-side cache key from silently drifting apart on a namespace change or rename.

AddEventQuestionAnswerCommandValidator, AddEventSpeakerCommandValidator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · Level 7 · classes (sealed)

Two single-rule FluentValidation validators guarding the simple Add commands. Each extends AbstractValidator<TCommand> and declares one RuleFor.

AddEventSpeakerCommandValidator MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/AddEventSpeaker/AddEventSpeakerCommandValidator.cs:8 SpeakerId .NotEqual(default(SpeakerIdentifierType)), "Speaker ID is required."
  • What they are: input validators that reject malformed commands before the handler runs.
  • Depends on: FluentValidation (AbstractValidator<T>); their respective command (AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand / AddEventSpeakerCommand).
  • Concept introduced, request validation as a pipeline concern. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses input validation at the boundary) and [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (server-side validation independent of the UI): validators are discovered by Scrutor and invoked by the validation step of the request pipeline, so a failing rule short-circuits to a Validation Error (→ HTTP 400) without the handler ever executing. Keeping validation in a dedicated class, not inside the handler, is why the handlers in this group can assume their inputs are shape-valid and focus on business invariants.
  • Walkthrough: each is an expression-bodied constructor wiring exactly one RuleFor (e.g. AddEventSpeakerCommandValidator.cs:10-13). Note these guard only surface shape (non-empty text, non-default id); deeper rules (does the event exist? is it published? does the question type match?) are business invariants enforced in the handler/domain, not here.
  • Where they're used: resolved and run by the validation pipeline decorator before the matching handler.

EventDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.DTOs · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/DTOs/EventDTOMapper.cs:14 · Level 7 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the aggregate-root mapper that turns an Event (with its child collections) into an EventDTO, delegating each child collection to its own mapper and applying one hand-written field conversion Mapperly can't express.
  • Depends on: IEntityDTOMapper<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>; the three child mappers RoomDTOMapper, EventSpeakerDTOMapper, EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper; Riok.Mapperly; System.Globalization.CultureInfo.
  • Concept reinforced, composed Mapperly mappers ([UseMapper]) plus a post-generation override. Builds on the single-entity Mapperly pattern (see the child-mapper family above), here showing two production refinements. [Rubric §1, SOLID] (each child mapper owns its own translation; this one only orchestrates) and [Rubric §15, Best Practices] (the one thing Mapperly can't do is done explicitly, not fudged).
  • Walkthrough
    • The class takes the three child mappers via a primary constructor (EventDTOMapper.cs:14-18) and re-exposes each as a [UseMapper] field (lines 20-27), that attribute tells Mapperly "when you need to map a Room/EventSpeaker/EventQuestionAnswer inside the Event graph, call this mapper" instead of regenerating child logic.
    • The public MapToDTO (lines 30-41) is hand-written: it null-guards, calls the generated MapToDTOGenerated(entity), then returns dto with { LastSessionizeRefreshBy = entity.LastSessionizeRefreshBy?.ToString(CultureInfo.InvariantCulture) }. The comment (line 35) explains why, converting a nullable UserIdentifierType to a nullable string is not expressible in Mapperly, so it is patched on with a record with-expression, using CultureInfo.InvariantCulture to stay locale-stable (the codebase's culture-invariant habit, primer §6).
    • MapToDTOGenerated (lines 50-51) is the partial Mapperly method, tagged [MapperIgnoreTarget(nameof(EventDTO.LastSessionizeRefreshBy))] so the generator skips the field the public method patches by hand, no double-write, no generator warning.
    • MapToDTOs (lines 44-48) is the same null-guarded collection projection as the child mappers.
  • Why it's built this way: [UseMapper] composition keeps each entity's mapping in exactly one place (the child mappers) while letting the root mapper assemble the full graph; the generate-then-override split lets the 95% Mapperly handles stay generated while the one awkward conversion is explicit and obvious (ADR-001's "explicit mapping" intent).
  • Where it's used: injected wherever a full Event graph is serialized, the events read endpoints and the Sessionize refresh flow; auto-registered by Scrutor.

UpdateCategoryItemCommandValidator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Categories.UseCases.UpdateCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/UseCases/UpdateCategoryItem/UpdateCategoryItemCommandValidator.cs:7 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the FluentValidation validator for UpdateCategoryItemCommand, built by composing the two reusable category-item field rule sets rather than re-declaring rules inline.
  • Depends on: FluentValidation (AbstractValidator<T>); the module's reusable rule sets CategoryItemNameRules<T> and CategoryItemSortRules<T> (both in this group).
  • Concept introduced, composable validation via Include(ruleSet). [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] / [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses input validation that is consistent and not duplicated). Rather than re-authoring "name not empty, within max length" and "sort in range" in every command that touches a category item, each field's rules are written once as a generic AbstractValidator<T> subclass parameterized by a property selector, and each command validator simply Includes them. The selector lambda re-targets the same rule onto whichever command property holds the value, so the add command and this update command stay in lockstep by construction. Validation runs in the pipeline before the handler, so UpdateCategoryItemHandler does no field-level checks of its own.
  • Walkthrough: the constructor (UpdateCategoryItemCommandValidator.cs:9-13) calls Include(new CategoryItemNameRules<UpdateCategoryItemCommand>(p => p.Name)) (line 11) and Include(new CategoryItemSortRules<UpdateCategoryItemCommand>(p => p.Sort)) (line 12). There is no inline RuleFor; the body is nothing but the two Includes.
  • Why it's built this way: DRY validation, one rule set, many commands. A change to the name-length limit happens in one place and propagates to the add, update, and any future category-item command that includes it.
  • Where it's used: auto-registered via Scrutor scanning and resolved by the validation pipeline decorator when an UpdateCategoryItemCommand is dispatched, ahead of UpdateCategoryItemHandler.

AddEventQuestionAnswerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.AddEventQuestionAnswer · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/AddEventQuestionAnswer/AddEventQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:17 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the richest handler in the Conference Add family: a multi-step validate-then-upsert that records an attendee's answer to an event question, creating a new EventQuestionAnswer or updating the user's existing one.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, ICurrentUserService, EventQuestionAnswerDTOMapper, ILogger; the domain types Event, Question, EventInvariants, QuestionInvariants; Result / Error; implements ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>.
  • Concept reinforced, the aggregate as the unit of consistency, with SaveChanges as the single seam to the framework. [Rubric §4, DDD] and [Rubric §6, CQRS]. The handler never touches a child entity directly; it loads the Event aggregate, calls its methods, and saves once. The one place it reaches a sibling aggregate is a read-only Question lookup for validation, references between aggregates are by id, never by tracked object graph (see primer §2).
  • Walkthrough (HandleAsync, lines 24-56)
    • Loads the Event with its answer collection included and tracked: GetByIdAsync(EventId, includes: [nameof(Event.EventQuestionAnswers)], asTracking: true) (lines 29-33), the include + tracking are required because a domain method will walk and mutate that collection. Null ⇒ Error.NotFound (line 35), source/target stamped via .WithSource/.WithTarget.
    • BR-108: EventInvariants.EnsureEventIsPublished(entity.IsPublished, …) (line 38); failure short-circuits with the invariant's errors.
    • BR-128 + BR-124: delegates to the private ValidateQuestionAsync (lines 58-77): loads the Question from its own repository, rejects it if missing or its QuestionEntity != "Event" (a Validation error, lines 65-72), then runs QuestionInvariants.EnsureAnswerValueMatchesQuestionType(question.QuestionType, command.AnswerValue, …) so the answer text matches the question's declared type.
    • BR-107 upsert: reads the current user via currentUserService.UserId!.Value (line 48) and looks for a non-deleted answer this user already gave for this question (lines 49-50). If one exists it calls UpdateExistingAnswerAsync → entity.UpdateEventQuestionAnswer(existing.Id, AnswerValue) (line 85); otherwise CreateNewAnswerAsync → entity.AddEventQuestionAnswer(EventQuestionAnswerId, QuestionId, AnswerValue) (lines 99-102). Either branch saves once with unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(...), logs via a source-generated [LoggerMessage] (lines 111-112), and returns the mapped DTO.
  • Why it's built this way: upsert (rather than create-or-409) matches the product rule that a user has at most one answer per question; doing the eligibility checks in the handler (event published, question valid) keeps "who/when may answer", an application concern, out of the domain entity, while the actual mutation stays a domain method on Event. The single SaveChangesAsync is the one place audit stamping, domain-event capture, and outbox writes fire.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference event-question-answer controller; it is the richest member of the Conference "load-aggregate / call-domain-method / save" handler family (contrast the minimal AddEventSpeakerHandler below).

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.AddRoom · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/AddRoom/AddRoomCommand.cs:20 · Level 6 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the command to add a new Room to an Event, carrying the room's descriptive fields plus an optional explicit room id.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (Level 0, the marker it implements); the alias types EventIdentifierType, RoomIdentifierType? (solution-wide global using aliases, see primer §2); Event (Level 5, only via typeof(Event).FullName for the cache prefix).
  • Concept reinforced, the command record + cache-invalidation marker. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses whether writes are modeled as explicit, intent-named commands) and [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns] (assesses whether concerns like caching are centralized): this is the same shape as the sibling Add commands (AddEventQuestionAnswerCommand, AddEventSpeakerCommand), which introduce the pattern. By implementing ICacheInvalidating the command opts its handler into the caching decorator, which evicts every entry under CachePrefix after the handler succeeds; the handler itself never mentions caching. The only difference from the other Add commands is the wider payload.
  • Walkthrough: eight positional members (AddRoomCommand.cs:20-28): EventId, the optional RoomId, the required Name and int Sort, then the nullable descriptors int? Capacity, string? Floor, string? Location, string? AccessibilityInfo. The lone body member is CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Event).FullName}:" (line 31), keying eviction by the Event type's full name. Note RoomId is nullable because room ids are app-assigned (a room's int PK is the same id space as the external Sessionize import); when null, AddRoomHandler allocates the next id in a reserved range rather than letting the database pick.
  • Why it's built this way: modeling the write as a record keeps it value-equatable and trivially testable; pushing cache eviction onto a decorator via a one-line marker keeps the handler free of cross-cutting noise (the rationale behind the whole decorator pipeline, see ICacheInvalidating).
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference rooms controller; validated by AddRoomCommandValidator; handled by AddRoomHandler.

EventCreateRequest

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Create/EventCreateRequest.cs:10 · Level 6 · record (class)

  • What it is: the wire-shaped input record for the create-an-event use case. Unusually for this codebase it doubles as the command itself: there is no separate CreateEventCommand wrapper, EventCreateRequest flows straight through the dispatcher into CreateEventHandler.
  • Depends on: ICreateRequest (Level 0, the generic create-pipeline marker); ICacheInvalidating (Level 0); Event (Level 5, only via typeof(Event).FullName for the cache prefix); the EventIdentifierType id alias (global using, see primer §2); DateOnly (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the request-as-command + the generic create pipeline. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses whether writes are modeled as explicit commands routed through a single dispatcher). Most create slices in this module reuse a generic request pipeline: a …CreateRequest implements ICreateRequest, a matching IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType> turns it into a domain entity, and the handler is ICommandHandler<TCreateRequest, Result<TDTO>>. So the request record is the command (line 10 declares : ICreateRequest, ICacheInvalidating), there is no CreateEventCommand type, which is why EventCreateRequest sits at Level 6 alongside the other commands rather than at the Level 1 request-DTO band. It also implements ICacheInvalidating so the caching decorator evicts the event cache after a successful create (CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Event).FullName}:", line 13). [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design]: the required modifier on Name, StartDate, EndDate, TimeZone (lines 19-31) makes those fields non-omittable at the contract level, while Description, SessionizeCode, VenueAddress, VenueMapUrl, and WiFiInfo are nullable optionals.
  • Walkthrough: a flat record class of init properties only, no behavior. Id (line 16) is present but documented "auto-generated if not provided", so a client may omit it and let the domain factory assign one. VenueMapUrl carries an inline [SuppressMessage("Design", "CA1056")] (line 40); a URL-shaped string normally trips the analyzer, but it is stored verbatim from the Sessionize import, and the suppression is justified inline ([Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality]: suppressions are explained, not blanket-disabled). The other properties are plain values; StartDate/EndDate are DateOnly (date-only, no time component).
  • Why it's built this way: collapsing the create request and command into one type removes a redundant wrapper for the simple "POST a body, build the entity" shape; the generic mapper pipeline (EventCreateRequestMapper) keeps domain construction out of the handler. Validation lives separately in EventCreateRequestValidator, the vertical-slice split this module uses everywhere.
  • Where it's used: built by the Conference events controller from the request body; validated by EventCreateRequestValidator, mapped by EventCreateRequestMapper, and handled by CreateEventHandler.

PublishEventCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Publish · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Publish/PublishEventCommand.cs:11 · Level 6 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the state-transition command that makes an Event visible to attendees. It carries only the target EventIdentifierType Id.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (Level 0); Event (Level 5, only via typeof(Event).FullName); the EventIdentifierType alias.
  • Concept introduced, the parameterless state-transition command. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven]. It is a one-line positional record: sealed record PublishEventCommand( EventIdentifierType Id) : ICacheInvalidating (line 11) with a single expression-bodied CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Event).FullName}:" (line 14). It carries no payload because the transition is the whole intent; the real rule (is the event in a state where it can be published?) lives on the domain entity's Publish() method, not on the command. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: ICacheInvalidating drives the caching decorator to clear the event cache namespace so read endpoints reflect the new visibility immediately. (Note the using Microsoft.Extensions.Logging on line 1 is an unused import copied from the handler template; the command itself does no logging.)
  • Walkthrough: nothing beyond the positional Id and the CachePrefix property. No methods, no validation, no request DTO, and no …Validator, because a bare id needs none.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the transition rules on the aggregate (rather than in the command or handler) is the DDD split this codebase follows: the command names the intent, the entity owns the validity of the transition. Deriving CachePrefix from typeof(Event).FullName (not a string literal) keeps the cache key correct if the type is renamed.
  • Where it's used: built by the Conference events controller from the route id; handled by PublishEventHandler. Its unpublish counterpart lives in a sibling slice.

EventCreateRequestMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Create/EventCreateRequestMapper.cs:11 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the request-to-entity mapper for the create-event slice: it turns an EventCreateRequest into a Result<Event> by delegating to the Event factory method.
  • Depends on: IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType> (Level 4); Event (Level 5); EventCreateRequest (Level 6); Result (Level 2); Task (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the request mapper as the create-pipeline's domain-construction port. [Rubric §1, SOLID] (DIP) and [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]. The generic create pipeline (introduced at EventCreateRequest) needs one place that knows how to build the entity from the request without the handler hard-coding it. That place is the IEntityRequestMapper<Event, EventCreateRequest, EventIdentifierType> implementation (line 12): the handler depends only on the interface, and DI wires this concrete mapper in. Crucially the mapper does not construct Event directly: it calls Event.Create(...) (lines 19-29), the factory that returns Result<Event>, so an invalid event cannot be produced. Construction validity stays in the domain (ADR-001 chose explicit, hand-written mapping over reflection-based AutoMapper; this is the manual mapping it prescribes). [Rubric §15, Best Practices]: ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(request) guards the input (line 17).
  • Walkthrough: one method, CreateEntityAsync (line 15). It is synchronous work wrapped in Task.FromResult (line 19) because Event.Create is a pure factory; the async-shaped signature exists only to satisfy the interface (other mappers may need real I/O). It forwards all ten request fields positionally to the factory in declaration order (lines 20-29).
  • Why it's built this way: keeping entity construction in a dedicated mapper (not the handler) means the handler stays a thin orchestrator and the construction rules stay testable in isolation; delegating to the Result-returning factory keeps the "invalid entity is unconstructable" guarantee intact.
  • Where it's used: injected into CreateEventHandler as IEntityRequestMapper<Event, EventCreateRequest, EventIdentifierType>.

  • Concept reinforced, validator-by-composition. [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (server-side validation that mirrors the domain rules). The constructor body is three Include(new …Rules<EventCreateRequest>(p => p.<Field>)) calls (lines 11-13), exactly the composition pattern AddRoomCommandValidator uses for rooms. Include merges another validator's rules into this one, so the constraints (name length, valid IANA time zone, start before end) live once in the shared rule classes and the validator only wires which property each applies to. EventDateRangeRules is included with two selectors (p => p.StartDate, p => p.EndDate, line 13), a cross-field rule. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns]: this validator is run automatically by the validation decorator in the CQRS pipeline before CreateEventHandler ever sees the request; the handler never calls it.
  • Walkthrough: only a constructor; no overridden members. It validates Name, TimeZone, and the StartDate/EndDate pair. The optional fields (Description, SessionizeCode, venue/WiFi) are unvalidated by design.
  • Why it's built this way: pulling each field constraint into a named, generic rule lets the create- and update-event validators reuse the same rule classes against their own property selectors, so there is no duplicated length constant or message between create and update.
  • Where it's used: resolved by the validation pipeline decorator when an EventCreateRequest flows through the dispatcher.

AddRoomHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.AddRoom · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/AddRoom/AddRoomHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the Add-family handler for rooms, with one extra wrinkle over the baseline: server-controlled id allocation in a reserved range when the caller supplies no Room id.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (and its read-repository accessor), RoomDTOMapper, ILogger<T> (BCL); Event, Room, EventInvariants (for the id-range constants); IReadRepository<TEntity, TIdentifierType>; Result / Error; implements ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>.
  • Concept introduced, application-enforced key allocation where the DB identity column cannot be used. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (assesses deliberate persistence and key strategy): a Room's int PK is its Sessionize id, so the application must keep organizer-created rooms in a disjoint, reserved id range to avoid colliding with imported ids.
  • Walkthrough (HandleAsync, lines 21-69): load the Event (lines 25-26); null returns Error.NotFound.WithSource(nameof(AddRoomHandler)).WithTarget(nameof(Event)) (line 28). The allocation block (lines 33-51): if command.RoomId is null (line 34), open a read repository for Room (line 36), fetch all rooms whose id falls in [EventInvariants.RoomManualIdRangeStart, RoomManualIdRangeEnd] with ignoreQueryFilters: true (lines 37-41, so soft-deleted rows still reserve their ids), take Max(id) + 1 (or the range start if none, lines 43-45), and fail with Error.Failure if the range is exhausted (lines 47-48); an explicitly supplied id is respected untouched. Then entity.AddRoom(roomId, Name, Sort, Capacity, Floor, Location, AccessibilityInfo) (lines 53-60), a domain method returning a Result; on failure return its errors (lines 61-62). On success SaveChangesAsync (line 64, with .ConfigureAwait(false)), a source-generated [LoggerMessage] LogRoomAdded (lines 66, 71), and return roomDTOMapper.MapToDTO(result.Value!) (line 68).
  • Why it's built this way: caller-provided ids are honored (so the Sessionize import can pin exact ids) but absent ids are allocated from a reserved manual range, keeping the imported and manual id spaces disjoint without a separate id-generation table; ignoreQueryFilters ensures a deleted room never lets its id be reused.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Conference rooms controller.

CreateEventHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Create/CreateEventHandler.cs:16 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for EventCreateRequest. It maps the request to an entity via the request mapper, adds it through the repository, persists, and returns the mapped EventDTO. The canonical create-handler flow in this module.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7); IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType> (Level 4, the EventCreateRequestMapper); EventDTOMapper (Level 7); Result (Level 2); Event, EventDTO; ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, the canonical create-handler flow (map, add, save, project). [Rubric §6, CQRS] and [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]. The steps, with line numbers:
    • Map the request to a domain entity (line 27): requestMapper.CreateEntityAsync(command, …) returns Result<Event>; on failure the handler returns those errors verbatim (lines 28-29). Domain construction validity (from Event.Create) short-circuits here; the handler never persists an invalid entity.
    • Resolve the repository through the unit of work (line 32): unitOfWork.GetRepository<Event, EventIdentifierType>(); the handler never touches DbContext.
    • Add and persist (lines 34-35): repository.AddAsync(entity, …) then unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(…), which also stamps audit fields and dispatches any domain events the factory raised.
    • Project the read DTO (line 39): dtoMapper.MapToDTO(entity) wrapped in Result.Success, so the controller can return the new event without a second GET.
    • [Rubric §13, Observability]: a source-generated [LoggerMessage] LogEventCreated (lines 37, 42) emits a structured, allocation-free log line.
  • Why it's built this way: the handler is a thin orchestrator: it owns persistence sequencing while the EventCreateRequestMapper owns construction and the domain factory owns validity. Note the .ConfigureAwait(false) on the persistence awaits (lines 34-35), library-layer code that avoids capturing a synchronization context. This is the recurring create shape; contrast the heavier update handlers elsewhere in the module that add concurrency and cross-aggregate checks.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the events controller through the dispatcher (so the logging/caching/validation decorators wrap it).

RemoveEventQuestionAnswerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.RemoveEventQuestionAnswer · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/RemoveEventQuestionAnswer/RemoveEventQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:14 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for RemoveEventQuestionAnswerCommand. It loads the Event with its EventQuestionAnswers, enforces a per-row ownership check (BR-52/BR-53), then delegates the removal to the aggregate.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7); ICurrentUserService (Level 0, who-am-I); RoleNames (Level 0, the Organizer constant); Error (Level 1); Result (Level 2); Event / EventQuestionAnswer; ILogger<T> (BCL).
  • Concept introduced, handler-level resource-based authorization (owner-or-admin). [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses authorization at the right granularity, not just "is logged in" but "may this user touch this row"). The flow, with line numbers:
    • Tracked, eager load with the answers (lines 25-29): GetByIdAsync(command.EventId, includes: [nameof(Event.EventQuestionAnswers)], asTracking: true, …), then a not-found guard (lines 30-31).
    • Locate the target answer, skipping soft-deleted (line 34): entity.EventQuestionAnswers.FirstOrDefault(a => a.Id == command.EventQuestionAnswerId && !a.IsDeleted).
    • BR-52/BR-53 ownership gate (lines 35-42): if the answer exists and the caller is not an Organizer (!currentUserService.IsInRole(RoleNames.Organizer)) and answer.CreatedBy != currentUserService.UserId!.Value, return Error.Forbidden(code: "EventQuestionAnswer.NotOwner", …), a 403. So an attendee may only delete their own answer; an organizer may delete any. The check reads the row's CreatedBy audit field, the soft-delete/audit machinery (see primer §2) doubles as the authorization key.
    • Delegate to the aggregate (line 44): entity.RemoveEventQuestionAnswer(command.EventQuestionAnswerId) returns a Result.
    • Persist on success + [LoggerMessage] (lines 45-49); return result verbatim (line 51).
    • [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns]: the coarse authentication (is-logged-in, has-role) is handled by middleware/attributes upstream; this fine-grained, data-dependent rule must live in the handler because only it has the loaded row's owner.
  • Why it's built this way: row-level ownership cannot be expressed as a static [Authorize] policy (it depends on runtime data), so it belongs in the handler after the load; keeping the rule next to the data it guards makes it testable and consistent. The same ownership rule is also expressible as a specification (OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification) for read scoping, but the write path enforces it directly here.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the event-question-answer controller through the dispatcher.

QuestionDTOMapper, SpeakerCategoryItemDTOMapper, SpeakerQuestionAnswerDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.{Questions,Speakers}.DTOs · Level 6 · class (sealed partial)

These three are structurally identical Mapperly-generated entity→DTO mappers; teaching one teaches all three. Each is a [Mapper]-attributed sealed partial class implementing IEntityDTOMapper<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType>, declares a partial QuestionDTO MapToDTO(...) whose body the Riok.Mapperly source generator fills in at compile time (see Mapperly in the primer), and hand-writes a tiny MapToDTOs that null-guards and projects the collection ([.. entityCollection.Select(MapToDTO)]).

Type File:Line Maps
QuestionDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Questions/DTOs/QuestionDTOMapper.cs:12 Question → QuestionDTO
SpeakerCategoryItemDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/DTOs/SpeakerCategoryItemDTOMapper.cs:12 SpeakerCategoryItem → SpeakerCategoryItemDTO
SpeakerQuestionAnswerDTOMapper MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/DTOs/SpeakerQuestionAnswerDTOMapper.cs:12 SpeakerQuestionAnswer → SpeakerQuestionAnswerDTO
  • Concept introduced, compile-time, explicit DTO mapping. [Rubric §1, SOLID] and [Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality]. ADR-001 (ADRs/001-manual-dto-mapping.md) chose explicit mapping over reflection-based AutoMapper; Mapperly is the realization of that decision, the mapping is generated as ordinary, debuggable, allocation-free code from the partial signature, so there is no runtime reflection and a property-name mismatch is a compile error, not a silent null. The [Mapper] attribute and partial method are the entire contract; the generator pairs source/target properties by name.
  • Walkthrough (uniform): MapToDTO is the generated scalar map (each *.cs:16); MapToDTOs (each *.cs:19-23) does ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(entityCollection) then [.. entityCollection.Select(MapToDTO)], a collection-expression spread that materializes a List exposed as IReadOnlyCollection<TDTO>.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping these mappers trivial and generator-backed means the only hand-written mapping logic lives where a rule genuinely differs (compare SpeakerDTOMapper, which adds PII redaction). These three have no such rule, so they stay one-liners.
  • Where it's used: injected into Conference query services and command handlers (SpeakerCategoryItemDTOMapper is also a constructor dependency of AddSpeakerCategoryItemHandler and a [UseMapper] child of SpeakerDTOMapper); auto-registered by Scrutor assembly scanning.

SpeakerLocalityHelper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.DecisionSupport · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/DecisionSupport/SpeakerLocalityHelper.cs:10 · Level 6 · class (internal static)

  • What it is: a stateless helper that resolves a speaker's locality tier (Atlanta/Suburbs, Georgia, Surrounding State, North America, Not North America) from the category system, and classifies whether a speaker counts as "local". It backs the session-selection decision-support analytics, locality is one input organizers weigh when curating the schedule.
  • Depends on: Speaker, Category (domain entities, read-only); the CategoryItemIdentifierType alias.
  • Concept introduced, locality-via-category, not via a Speaker field. There is no Speaker.Location column; a speaker's origin is modeled as a SpeakerCategoryItem pointing into the "Where are you traveling from" category (Sessionize category 121854). This helper encapsulates that indirection so callers never hard-code the lookup. [Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design] (assesses whether the model mirrors the business's own vocabulary): the conference's own Sessionize categorization is the source of truth for locality, so the code reads it rather than inventing a parallel field.
  • Walkthrough: four static methods:
    • GetLocalityTier(speaker, localityCategoryItems) (SpeakerLocalityHelper.cs:19-33) iterates the speaker's SpeakerCategoryItems, skipping soft-deleted rows (sci.IsDeleted, line 25, honoring soft-delete in-memory since these are already-loaded children), and returns the first tier name whose CategoryItemId is present in the supplied lookup, else null.
    • IsLocalSpeaker(localityTier) (lines 41-49) is a case-insensitive substring test, a tier counts as local if it contains "Atlanta", "Georgia", or "Surrounding".
    • FindLocalityCategory(categories) (lines 57-74) locates the locality Category by title substring "traveling" (case-insensitive, line 66), with a hard-coded fallback to id 121854 (line 69) if no title matches, a defensive belt-and-suspenders against the category being renamed.
    • BuildLocalityLookup(localityCategory) (lines 81-89) projects the category's non-deleted CategoryItems into an IReadOnlyDictionary<CategoryItemIdentifierType, string> of id→name, returning an empty dictionary when the category is null.
  • Why it's built this way: pulling the lookup table out once (BuildLocalityLookup) and passing it into the per-speaker GetLocalityTier keeps the analytics loop O(speakers) rather than re-scanning categories per speaker; the title-match-with-id-fallback hedges against the two ways the category could be identified.
  • Where it's used: consumed by the session-selection decision-support analytics (the DecisionSupport use-case folder) when assembling speaker-locality summaries for organizers.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the magic number 121854 is duplicated here as a literal; the comments name the tiers, but the exact tier strings come from the live category data, not from source.

QuestionCreateRequestMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Questions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Questions/UseCases/Create/QuestionCreateRequestMapper.cs:11 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the request→entity mapper that turns a validated QuestionCreateRequest into a domain Question by calling the entity's Create factory.
  • Depends on: IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType> (the contract); Result / Result<T>; Question; the QuestionIdentifierType alias.
  • Concept introduced, request mapper vs. DTO mapper. Where a *DTOMapper projects an entity out to a wire DTO, an IEntityRequestMapper goes the other direction and is allowed to fail: it returns Result<Question> because construction routes through the domain factory, which enforces invariants. [Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design]: an invalid entity is unconstructable, the only way to make a Question is Question.Create, which returns a failure Result instead of throwing or producing a half-valid object (the Result pattern).
  • Walkthrough: CreateEntityAsync (QuestionCreateRequestMapper.cs:15-27) null-guards the request, then returns Task.FromResult(Question.Create(...)) passing request.Id (already overwritten by the handler), QuestionText, and the nullable QuestionEntity!/QuestionType! (null-forgiven, validation/defaults are expected upstream), Sort, IsRequired, and a hard-coded questionSource: "User" (line 26) that tags manually-created questions distinctly from Sessionize-imported ones. The method is synchronous under the async signature (no awaits), hence Task.FromResult.
  • Why it's built this way: centralizing construction in the factory keeps the create slice from duplicating invariant checks; the "User" source literal is what lets the import path and the manual path coexist in one entity.
  • Where it's used: injected into CreateQuestionHandler (as IEntityRequestMapper<Question, QuestionCreateRequest, QuestionIdentifierType>).

QuestionCreateRequestValidator

SpeakerDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.DTOs · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/DTOs/SpeakerDTOMapper.cs:17 · Level 7 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the entity→DTO mapper for Speaker. Unlike the trivial trio above, it adds PII redaction (BR-66: speaker email is hidden from non-organizers) and composes child mappers, hence the higher level (it has real dependencies).
  • Depends on: IEntityDTOMapper<...>; the two child mappers SpeakerCategoryItemDTOMapper and SpeakerQuestionAnswerDTOMapper (constructor-injected as [UseMapper]); ICurrentUserService; RoleNames; Email value object; SpeakerDTO; Riok.Mapperly.
  • Concept introduced, role-gated PII redaction in the mapping layer, and Mapperly composition. [Rubric §11, Security] and [Rubric §30, Compliance, Privacy & Data Governance] (assess least-privilege exposure of personal data). The mapper checks the current user's role and strips email for everyone but Organizers, the contract returned to an attendee literally cannot contain the speaker's email. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns]: Mapperly's [UseMapper] lets the generated parent map delegate child-collection mapping to the injected child mappers (composition over a monolithic mapper).
  • Walkthrough
    • Two [UseMapper] private readonly child mappers (SpeakerDTOMapper.cs:23-27), the generator calls these when mapping Speaker.SpeakerCategoryItems/SpeakerQuestionAnswers.
    • MapToDTO (lines 30-37): null-guard, call the generated MapToDTOGenerated(entity), then the redaction gate, currentUserService.IsInRole(RoleNames.Organizer) ? dto : dto with { Email = null } (line 36). The with expression produces a copy with email nulled for non-organizers.
    • MapToDTOs (lines 40-44): the same null-guard + Select(MapToDTO) spread as the trivial mappers, so the redaction applies per-element.
    • private partial SpeakerDTO MapToDTOGenerated(Speaker entity) (line 46) is the Mapperly-generated core; NullableEmailToString(Email? email) (line 49) is a custom converter teaching the generator how to flatten the Email value object to a string?.
  • Why it's built this way: putting redaction in the mapper (not the controller) guarantees every path that produces a SpeakerDTO, list, by-id, nested under a session, gets the same PII rule from one place; a forgotten endpoint can't leak email.
  • Where it's used: Conference speaker query service and any handler returning a SpeakerDTO; auto-registered by Scrutor (its child-mapper and ICurrentUserService dependencies are satisfied by DI).
