CreateQuestionHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Questions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Questions/UseCases/Create/CreateQuestionHandler.cs:16 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the create handler for QuestionCreateRequest. It follows the standard create template (validate → map request to entity → persist → return DTO) but adds server-controlled id allocation in a reserved manual range, because question ids share an id space with externally-imported Sessionize questions.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork; IEntityRequestMapper<Question, QuestionCreateRequest, QuestionIdentifierType> (implemented by QuestionCreateRequestMapper); QuestionDTOMapper; ILogger<T>; ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>; Result / Error; Question and QuestionInvariants.
  • Concept introduced, application-enforced key allocation. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (assesses deliberate persistence strategy, here, key allocation). The database's identity column can't be used because the question id space is shared with an external system (Sessionize), so manually-created questions must live in a disjoint reserved band (QuestionInvariants.ManualIdRangeStart = 999_999_000 .. ManualIdRangeEnd = 999_999_999, MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Domain/Questions/QuestionInvariants.cs:37,40). The handler allocates the next free id in that band itself.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (CreateQuestionHandler.cs:23-59):
    1. Get the repository, then GetAllAsync every question already in the manual id band, with ignoreQueryFilters: true (lines 31-35) so even soft-deleted rows still reserve their id (preventing reuse after delete).
    2. Pick nextId = max(id)+1, or ManualIdRangeStart if the band is empty (lines 37-39); if nextId exceeds the band, fail with Error.Failure(..., "Manual question ID range exhausted.") (lines 41-42).
    3. Overwrite the caller's id via a record with expression, command = command with { Id = nextId } (line 45), so caller-supplied ids are ignored, matching QuestionCreateRequest's contract.
    4. requestMapper.CreateEntityAsync(command, ...) (line 47) routes through Question.Create and may fail; propagate result.Errors if so (lines 48-49).
    5. repository.AddAsync then SaveChangesAsync (lines 53-54), log via [LoggerMessage] (lines 56, 61-62), return the mapped QuestionDTO (line 58).
  • Why it's built this way: disjoint id ranges let the import path and the manual path coexist in the same table without collision; ignoreQueryFilters on the reservation scan is the subtle but essential detail that stops a deleted question's id from being silently reissued.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Questions REST controller in the Conference service.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the read-then-max-then-write id allocation is not transactionally serialized against a concurrent create at the application layer; the TransactionalCommandDecorator governs the save, but concurrent allocation races are not guarded in this method's visible code.

UnpublishEventHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Unpublish · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Unpublish/UnpublishEventHandler.cs:13 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UnpublishEventCommand. It loads the Event aggregate by id and delegates the visibility transition to the domain entity, returning a bare Result (no DTO). It is the mirror of PublishEventHandler.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (returning bare Result); IUnitOfWork; Error; Result; Event; ILogger<T>.
  • Concept introduced, the canonical state-transition handler (load → guard → delegate → save). [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] and [Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design]. This is the simplest handler shape in the unit, no request payload, no child collection, no authorization. HandleAsync (UnpublishEventHandler.cs:18-35):
    • Load by id (lines 22-23): repository.GetByIdAsync(command.Id, cancellationToken), a plain by-id load with no includes (the transition needs no children).
    • Not-found guard (lines 24-25): a null entity returns Result.Failure(Error.NotFound.WithSource(nameof(UnpublishEventHandler)).WithTarget(nameof(Event))) → a 404 at the API boundary. WithSource/WithTarget enrich the Error for diagnostics.
    • Delegate the transition to the domain (line 27): entity.Unpublish() returns a Result. The entity decides whether the transition is legal (e.g. unpublishing an event not currently published), not the handler.
    • Persist only on success (lines 28-32): if (result.IsSuccess) then SaveChangesAsync and the [LoggerMessage] log; the handler then returns result verbatim (line 34), success or the domain's failure errors. A failed transition is not persisted.
    • [Rubric §13, Observability]: LogEventUnpublished is a source-generated [LoggerMessage] partial (lines 37-38, message "Event {EventId} unpublished").
  • Why it's built this way: the handler owns persistence plumbing and the not-found check; the aggregate owns transition validity. Returning the domain Result directly (rather than re-wrapping) keeps the error provenance intact.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the EventsController through the dispatcher. Cache eviction is automatic via UnpublishEventCommand's ICacheInvalidating prefix.

UpdateEventQuestionAnswerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.UpdateEventQuestionAnswer · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/UpdateEventQuestionAnswer/UpdateEventQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:14 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UpdateEventQuestionAnswerCommand. It loads the Event with its EventQuestionAnswers, enforces a per-row ownership check (BR-52/BR-53), then delegates the edit to the aggregate. It is the update twin of RemoveEventQuestionAnswerHandler, differing only in update-vs-remove of the located answer.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (returning bare Result); IUnitOfWork; ICurrentUserService (who-am-I); RoleNames (the Organizer constant); Error; Result; Event / EventQuestionAnswer; ILogger<T>.
  • Concept introduced, handler-level resource-based authorization (owner-or-admin). [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses authorization at the right granularity, not just "is logged in" but "may this user touch this row"). HandleAsync (UpdateEventQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:20-54):
    • Tracked, eager load with the answers (lines 25-29): GetByIdAsync(command.EventId, includes: [nameof(Event.EventQuestionAnswers)], asTracking: true, ...), then a not-found guard (lines 30-31). Tracking is required because this is a write and EF must observe the child mutation.
    • Locate the target answer, skipping soft-deleted (line 34): entity.EventQuestionAnswers.FirstOrDefault(a => a.Id == command.EventQuestionAnswerId && !a.IsDeleted).
    • BR-52/BR-53 ownership gate (lines 35-42): if the answer exists and the caller is not an Organizer (!currentUserService.IsInRole(RoleNames.Organizer)) and answer.CreatedBy != currentUserService.UserId!.Value, return Error.Forbidden("EventQuestionAnswer.NotOwner", ...) → 403. So an attendee may only edit their own answer; an organizer may edit any. The check reads the row's CreatedBy audit field, the soft-delete/audit machinery (see primer §2) doubles as the authorization key.
    • Delegate to the aggregate (lines 44-46): entity.UpdateEventQuestionAnswer(command.EventQuestionAnswerId, command.AnswerValue) returns a Result.
    • Persist on success + [LoggerMessage] (lines 47-51); return result verbatim (line 53). LogEventQuestionAnswerUpdated is the source-generated logger (lines 56-57).
    • [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns]: the coarse authentication (is-logged-in, has-role) is handled by middleware/attributes upstream; this fine-grained, data-dependent rule must live in the handler because only it has the loaded row's owner.
  • Why it's built this way: row-level ownership can't be expressed as a static [Authorize] policy (it depends on runtime data), so it belongs in the handler after the load; centralizing it here (rather than the controller) keeps the rule next to the data it guards and identical across the remove and update paths.
  • Where it's used: registered by the Conference application-service scan; invoked by the EventQuestionAnswersController through the dispatcher. The ownership rule is also expressible as a specification (OwnEventQuestionAnswerSpecification) for read scoping, but the write path enforces it directly here.

UpdateRoomHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.UpdateRoom · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/UpdateRoom/UpdateRoomHandler.cs:13 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler for UpdateRoomCommand: loads the Event aggregate with its rooms, delegates to Event.UpdateRoom, and saves. Unlike the add/create handlers it returns a bare Result (no DTO).
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork; ILogger<T>; ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>; Result / Error; Event.
  • Concept introduced, child-update via the aggregate root, with a targeted include. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] and [Rubric §4, Domain-Driven Design]. Because a Room is a child of Event, the handler loads the root with the Rooms collection eagerly included and tracked (so EF observes the child mutation), then calls entity.UpdateRoom(...) rather than touching the room directly, the aggregate root remains the only mutation entry point.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (UpdateRoomHandler.cs:18-46):
    1. GetRepository<Event, EventIdentifierType>() then GetByIdAsync(command.EventId, includes: [nameof(Event.Rooms)], asTracking: true, ...) (lines 22-27), the includes array eager-loads the rooms; asTracking: true is required so EF persists the in-graph edit.
    2. If null, Result.Failure(Error.NotFound.WithSource(...).WithTarget(nameof(Event))) (lines 28-29).
    3. entity.UpdateRoom(command.RoomId, command.Name, command.Sort, command.Capacity, command.Floor, command.Location, command.AccessibilityInfo) (lines 31-38) returns a Result; the domain method finds the room by id and enforces its invariants.
    4. Only on success (result.IsSuccess, lines 39-43): SaveChangesAsync then log via [LoggerMessage] (lines 41-42, 48-49). The handler then returns result either way (line 45), propagating the domain's success/failure verbatim.
  • Why it's built this way: guarding the save behind result.IsSuccess avoids a no-op SaveChangesAsync (and a misleading "updated" log line) when the domain rejected the edit; returning the domain Result directly means the handler adds no error of its own beyond the not-found case.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Events/Rooms REST controller in the Conference service; cache eviction is automatic via UpdateRoomCommand's ICacheInvalidating prefix.

AddSpeakerCategoryItemCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.AddSpeakerCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/AddSpeakerCategoryItem/AddSpeakerCategoryItemCommand.cs:18 · Level 6 · record (sealed)

  • What it is: the write command that associates an existing Speaker with a SpeakerCategoryItem join entity (e.g. a "traveling from" or topic tag). A three-field record: the parent SpeakerId, an optional explicit SpeakerCategoryItemId for the new join row, and the CategoryItemId being attached.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (the marker it implements); the SpeakerIdentifierType/SpeakerCategoryItemIdentifierType/CategoryItemIdentifierType aliases (see identifier aliases); Speaker (only for its typeof(...).FullName in the cache prefix).
  • Concept introduced, the cache-invalidating command. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns] (assesses whether concerns like caching live in one place instead of being smeared through handlers). A command opts into cache eviction merely by implementing ICacheInvalidating and exposing a CachePrefix; the CachingCommandDecorator in the CQRS decorator pipeline sees the marker and clears the matching cache region after the handler succeeds, the handler itself contains no cache code. Here CachePrefix is $"{typeof(Speaker).FullName}:" (AddSpeakerCategoryItemCommand.cs:24), so writing a speaker's categories evicts the cached speaker reads. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] is the flip side: read endpoints are output-cached, and this is the write-side invalidation that keeps them coherent.
  • Walkthrough: the positional record params (AddSpeakerCategoryItemCommand.cs:18-21): SpeakerId identifies the aggregate to mutate; SpeakerCategoryItemId is nullable so the caller can either supply an explicit join-row id or pass null for database-generated identity (documented at line 16); CategoryItemId is the category item to attach. The only member body is the computed CachePrefix (line 24).
  • Why it's built this way: modeling the operation as an immutable record command (not a method argument bag) is what lets the dispatcher route it through the decorator pipeline and lets the validator/handler be discovered by name. The nullable id mirrors the domain's Speaker.AddSpeakerCategoryItem overload that accepts an optional id.
  • Where it's used: handled by AddSpeakerCategoryItemHandler; validated by AddSpeakerCategoryItemCommandValidator; dispatched from the Speakers REST controller in the Conference service.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.LinkUser · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/LinkUser/LinkUserToSpeakerCommand.cs:18 · Level 6 · record

  • Depends on: Speaker (for the CachePrefix and the SpeakerIdentifierType alias), UserIdentifierType (the Identity id alias, via MMCA.ADC.Identity.Shared.Users), and the two opt-in marker interfaces ICacheInvalidating and ITransactional.
  • Concept reinforced, the command record + decorator opt-ins. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (writes are explicit command messages, never anonymous service-method args). The command is a sealed record so it is immutable and value-comparable; the handler (LinkUserToSpeakerHandler) is selected by the dispatcher purely from the command type. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting Concerns]: by implementing ICacheInvalidating it opts the CachingCommandDecorator into wiping the speaker cache, and by implementing ITransactional it opts the TransactionalCommandDecorator into wrapping the handler in a DB transaction, the cross-cutting behavior is declared on the message, not coded in the handler (the decorator pipeline is taught in primer §2).
  • Walkthrough: the positional record (SpeakerIdentifierType SpeakerId, UserIdentifierType UserId) (line 18). The one body member is CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Speaker).FullName}:" (line 21), the cache key namespace the invalidation decorator clears, derived from the entity type's full name so it always matches the keys the read path writes.

Linking touches the Speaker aggregate and raises an integration event that must reach Identity; making the whole handler transactional ensures the Speaker.LinkedUserId write and the outbox row land atomically (ADR-003 outbox dual-dispatch, see IIntegrationEventPublisher). The doc comment (lines 11-14) states exactly this rationale.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by SpeakersController's link action; handled by LinkUserToSpeakerHandler.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.RemoveSpeakerCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/RemoveSpeakerCategoryItem/RemoveSpeakerCategoryItemCommand.cs:15 · Level 6 · record

Unlike the link/unlink commands it is not ITransactional, removing a category item is a single-aggregate write with no cross-context event, so the default per-SaveChangesAsync transaction suffices.

SpeakerCreateRequestMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/Create/SpeakerCreateRequestMapper.cs:11 · Level 7 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the request→entity mapper for speaker creation: it turns a SpeakerCreateRequest into a Speaker by delegating to the domain factory method, returning a Result<T> so invalid input never produces a half-built entity.
  • Depends on: IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType>, Speaker, Result/Result<T>.
  • Concept reinforced, the request mapper as the seam between the wire DTO and the domain factory. [Rubric §4, DDD] (entity construction goes through the factory, which enforces invariants and returns a Result). Unlike a DTO mapper (entity→DTO, mechanical), a request mapper goes the other way and may fail: hence its return type is Task<Result<Speaker>>, not Speaker. It is the only place that knows how request fields line up with the Speaker.Create parameters.
  • Walkthrough: CreateEntityAsync(SpeakerCreateRequest request, CancellationToken) (line 15): ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(request) then Task.FromResult(Speaker.Create(request.Id, request.FirstName, request.LastName, request.Email, request.Bio, request.TagLine, request.ProfilePicture, request.IsTopSpeaker)) (lines 19-27). The call is synchronous (the factory does no I/O) but wrapped in Task.FromResult to satisfy the async port signature. Note it forwards only a subset of the request's fields, the social/website URLs and LinkedUserId are not factory parameters and are not set here.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the request→Result<Speaker> translation in a dedicated mapper lets CreateSpeakerHandler stay pure orchestration (map → save → return DTO) and makes the field-mapping unit-testable in isolation.
  • Where it's used: injected into CreateSpeakerHandler as IEntityRequestMapper<Speaker, SpeakerCreateRequest, SpeakerIdentifierType>.

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.AddSpeakerCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/AddSpeakerCategoryItem/AddSpeakerCategoryItemHandler.cs:15 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • Concept introduced, the child-add mutation handler. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses command/query separation and thin, single-purpose handlers). The handler does five things and nothing more: fetch the aggregate, 404 if absent, delegate the actual mutation to the domain (speaker.AddSpeakerCategoryItem), persist via the unit of work, and return the mapped result. All cross-cutting work (logging, caching, transaction) is added by the decorator pipeline, not here. This is the same family as the update/add/remove handlers catalogued in the conference domain, see also UpdateRoomHandler.
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync (AddSpeakerCategoryItemHandler.cs:21-39):
    1. unitOfWork.GetRepository<Speaker, SpeakerIdentifierType>() then GetByIdAsync (lines 25-26).
    2. If null, Result.Failure<...>(Error.NotFound.WithSource(...).WithTarget(nameof(Speaker))) (lines 27-28), the Error carries source/target metadata for the Problem-Details response.
    3. speaker.AddSpeakerCategoryItem(command.SpeakerCategoryItemId, command.CategoryItemId) (line 30), the domain decides whether the add is legal and returns a Result<SpeakerCategoryItem>; on failure the handler propagates result.Errors (lines 31-32).
    4. SaveChangesAsync (line 34) persists (and stamps audit fields / dispatches domain events centrally).
    5. LogCategoryItemAdded(...) via the [LoggerMessage] source-generated logger (lines 36, 41-42), then return the mapped SpeakerCategoryItemDTO off result.Value! (line 38).
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the mutation in Speaker.AddSpeakerCategoryItem (not the handler) preserves the aggregate's invariants; the handler is pure orchestration, which is exactly why it can be so short and why the decorator pipeline can wrap it uniformly. Cache eviction is automatic because the command implements ICacheInvalidating.
  • Where it's used: dispatched by the Speakers REST controller in the Conference service when an organizer tags a speaker.

LinkUserToSpeakerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers.UseCases.LinkUser · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/UseCases/LinkUser/LinkUserToSpeakerHandler.cs:17 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the handler that mutates the Conference side of the bidirectional User↔Speaker link (Speaker.LinkedUserId) and then publishes an integration event so the Identity side updates asynchronously.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IIntegrationEventPublisher, Speaker, the SpeakerLinkedToUser integration event, Error/Result, and ICommandHandler.
  • Concept reinforced, cross-context coordination via integration events (no cross-module domain reference). [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] and [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness]. Conference and Identity own separate databases (ADR-006), so there is no FK between Speaker and User; consistency flows through events. The integration-event publish path is ADR-003 (outbox dual-dispatch, IIntegrationEventPublisher).
  • Walkthrough: HandleAsync(LinkUserToSpeakerCommand command, CancellationToken) (line 23): (1) load the speaker; null → Result.Failure(Error.NotFound…) (lines 27-30); (2) BR-208 guard, query all speakers whose LinkedUserId equals command.UserId and fail with an Error.Invariant("Speaker.UserAlreadyLinked") if any other speaker already holds that user (lines 33-44), so one user can't link to two speakers; (3) speaker.LinkUser(command.UserId), the domain method that sets LinkedUserId and enforces speaker-side invariants (line 46); (4) only on success: SaveChangesAsync, LogUserLinkedToSpeaker(...), then integrationEventPublisher.PublishAsync(new SpeakerLinkedToUser(command.UserId, command.SpeakerId), …) (lines 47-58), captured by the outbox and ultimately handled by Identity's SpeakerLinkedToUserHandler. Returns the domain result (line 60).
  • Why it's built this way: the comment at lines 53-54 records that the event replaces a previous direct IUserSpeakerLinkService call: routing the cross-context update through an event is precisely what makes Conference and Identity independently extractable (ADR-007/008), since neither references the other's Application/Domain. The whole command is ITransactional so the Speaker write and the outbox row commit atomically.
  • Where it's used: SpeakersController's link action; tested by LinkUserToSpeakerHandlerTests.

AddSessionCategoryItemCommand, AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommand, AddSessionSpeakerCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.* · Level 7 · sealed record (each implements ICacheInvalidating)

The three child-collection commands that mutate a Session aggregate by adding one of its owned children. They share an identical shape, a sealed record of identifier parameters that implements ICacheInvalidating with the same CachePrefix, so they are taught once here; the per-command differences are only in which child and which identifiers each carries.

Type File:Line Parameters Notes
AddSessionCategoryItemCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionCategoryItem/AddSessionCategoryItemCommand.cs:15 SessionId, SessionCategoryItemId?, CategoryItemId Associates a category item with the session
AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionQuestionAnswer/AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:18 SessionId, SessionQuestionAnswerId?, QuestionId, string AnswerValue Records (or upserts) an attendee's feedback answer
AddSessionSpeakerCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionSpeaker/AddSessionSpeakerCommand.cs:15 SessionId, SessionSpeakerId?, SpeakerId Associates a speaker with the session
  • What they are: CQRS command messages, immutable records that name an operation and carry the ids it needs. They hold no behavior; a matching handler (below) does the work. They are the "C" of CQRS, each represents an intent to change a session.
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (Level 0); the Session entity (only for typeof(Session).FullName in the cache prefix); strongly-typed id aliases (SessionIdentifierType, CategoryItemIdentifierType, SpeakerIdentifierType, QuestionIdentifierType, and the per-join SessionCategoryItemIdentifierType / SessionSpeakerIdentifierType / SessionQuestionAnswerIdentifierType).
  • Concept reinforced, the command as a cache-invalidation signal. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses a real read/write split with messages, not anaemic "command objects"): each is a discrete write intent dispatched through the decorator pipeline. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (assesses caching done correctly, including invalidation): every command implements ICacheInvalidating and exposes CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Session).FullName}:" (e.g. AddSessionCategoryItemCommand.cs:21). The CachingCommandDecorator (the pipeline stage introduced in the CQRS group) reads this prefix and evicts every cached session read after the write succeeds, so a category-item addition can never be served stale. The prefix is computed from the entity type's full name rather than a hand-typed string, so a namespace rename cannot silently desynchronise the cache key. First place to internalise: this is how a write tells the read-cache "you are now wrong about sessions."
  • Walkthrough
    • All three are positional sealed records, the constructor parameters are the public init-only properties, with structural equality and with-expression copying for free (the create slice's CreateSessionHandler leans on that same with-copy for id allocation).
    • The nullable explicit-id parameter (SessionCategoryItemId? line 17, SessionSpeakerId? line 17, SessionQuestionAnswerId? line 20) is the seam for identity-insert from Sessionize: a null lets the database generate the join-entity id (the organizer-create path), while a non-null value seeds a known id when importing the Sessionize export so re-imports are idempotent (BR, Sessionize sync). The doc comment on each of these parameters (e.g. AddSessionCategoryItemCommand.cs:13) documents the null-means-DB-generated contract inline.
    • AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommand is the odd one out: besides the ids it carries a string AnswerValue payload (line 22), because answering a question writes user-supplied content, not just a foreign-key link.
  • Why it's built this way: modelling each child operation as its own command keeps the vertical slice self-contained (command + validator + handler in one folder, [Rubric §5, Vertical Slice]) and lets the pipeline attach caching/logging/transaction concerns generically off the marker interfaces rather than per-handler code.
  • Where they're used: constructed by SessionCategoryItemsController / SessionSpeakersController / SessionQuestionAnswersController (Conference API), dispatched through the command pipeline to their handlers below; validated first by the matching *Validator.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: these are pure messages; whether identity-insert actually fires depends on the repository path used by the Sessionize sync, not visible in the command itself.

  • What they are: declarative input guards that run before the matching handler, rejecting a malformed command with a Validation error (→ HTTP 400) so the handler can assume well-formed input.

They are auto-discovered by Scrutor assembly scanning and invoked by the validation stage of the command pipeline ahead of the add handlers. The division of labour is deliberate: shape checks (is an id supplied? is the answer non-empty?) live here; the deeper rules that need the loaded aggregate (service-session eligibility, question-type matching, status and event-published checks) live in the handler/domain (see AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler), because a stateless validator cannot see the database.

  • Where they're used: registered per command type; run by the command pipeline immediately before the corresponding add handler.

AddSessionCategoryItemHandler, AddSessionSpeakerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.* · Level 8 · sealed partial class

The two "thin" session-child add handlers: load the Session aggregate, call one of its domain methods, save, log. They follow the canonical load-aggregate → call-domain-method → save mutation shape and so are taught together; AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler is the same family member rich enough to merit its own section.

Type File:Line Domain method · returns
AddSessionCategoryItemHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionCategoryItem/AddSessionCategoryItemHandler.cs:16 Session.AddSessionCategoryItem(...) → Result<SessionCategoryItemDTO>
AddSessionSpeakerHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionSpeaker/AddSessionSpeakerHandler.cs:16 Session.AddSessionSpeaker(...) → Result<SessionSpeakerDTO>
  • What they are: CQRS command handlers that mutate the Session aggregate through its own domain methods, then persist via the unit of work. The aggregate, not the handler, owns the invariant; the handler is orchestration.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7) and its IRepository<TEntity, TIdentifierType>; the Session entity (Level 6); Result / Error; ILogger; and the matching child DTO mapper (SessionCategoryItemDTOMapper / SessionSpeakerDTOMapper) to project the added child on success.
  • Concept reinforced, the aggregate as the unit of consistency; SaveChanges as the single framework seam; source-generated logging. [Rubric §4, DDD] and [Rubric §6, CQRS]: the canonical body is var repository = unitOfWork.GetRepository<Session, SessionIdentifierType>(); var session = await repository.GetByIdAsync(id, …); if (session is null) return Result.Failure(Error.NotFound…); var result = session.AddX(...); if (result.IsFailure) return …; await unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(...) (see AddSessionCategoryItemHandler.cs:26-39). Two mechanics worth internalising:
    • Tracking + includes for collection-walking methods. AddSessionSpeakerHandler loads with an explicit includes: array and asTracking: true (AddSessionSpeakerHandler.cs:27) because the domain method must inspect the already-loaded child collection (to reject a duplicate speaker) and EF must be tracking to persist the change. AddSessionCategoryItemHandler loads without an include (AddSessionCategoryItemHandler.cs:27), it only appends, so it never reads the existing collection.
    • SaveChangesAsync is the only touch of the database. That single call (each with .ConfigureAwait(false), line 35) stamps audit fields, captures domain events, and writes the outbox, none of which the handler codes by hand. [Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting]: the cross-cutting work lives below the handler, so the handler stays a five-line orchestration.
    • [LoggerMessage] source-gen. Each is sealed partial class with a private static partial void LogXAddedToSession(...) decorated [LoggerMessage(Level = Information, …)] (e.g. AddSessionCategoryItemHandler.cs:42-43), giving zero-allocation, compile-checked structured logs, the pattern on every handler in this codebase ([Rubric §13, Observability]). Both handlers return Result.Success(dtoMapper.MapToDTO(result.Value!)) (line 39), projecting the newly-added child through its mapper.
  • Why it's built this way: uniformity. Because validation, caching, transactions, audit, events, and outbox are all handled by the pipeline and SaveChangesAsync, a new child operation is a handful of lines, and the analyzers + Result pattern keep every handler the same shape ([Rubric §16, Maintainability]).
  • Where they're used: injected into the Conference child-collection controllers (SessionCategoryItemsController, SessionSpeakersController); dispatched to by the command pipeline after the matching *Validator.

AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.AddSessionQuestionAnswer · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/AddSessionQuestionAnswer/AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:19 · Level 8 · sealed partial class

  • What it is: the richest member of the session-child handler family, recording an attendee's answer to a session feedback question. Unlike its thin siblings above, it runs a multi-step validate-then-upsert that reaches into two sibling aggregates (Event and Question) read-only before mutating the Session.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>; IUnitOfWork; ICurrentUserService (Level 0, to read the answering user's id); SessionQuestionAnswerDTOMapper; Session, Event, Question entities and their invariant helpers SessionInvariants, EventInvariants, QuestionInvariants (Level 4); Result / Error.
  • Concept introduced, the validate-then-upsert handler that orchestrates across sibling aggregates. [Rubric §4, DDD] (cross-aggregate references are by id, and one aggregate is never reached through another's navigation): the handler loads Event and Question through their own repositories, not through Session, keeping aggregate boundaries intact. [Rubric §11, Security] / [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety]: business eligibility is enforced server-side here, not trusted from the client. The flow (HandleAsync, …cs:26-58):
    1. Load the session with its answers tracked, GetByIdAsync(SessionId, includes: [nameof(Session.SessionQuestionAnswers)], asTracking: true, …) (…cs:31-35); 404 if missing (…cs:36-37).
    2. Eligibility gate (ValidateSessionEligibilityAsync, …cs:60-81): BR-91, SessionInvariants.EnsureNotServiceSession (a lunch/break cannot be reviewed, line 65); BR-49, SessionInvariants.EnsureStatusIsEligible (only Accepted/null status, line 70); BR-108, load the parent Event by id through its own repository and EventInvariants.EnsureEventIsPublished (lines 75-80). Each is a Result short-circuit.
    3. Question gate (ValidateQuestionAsync, …cs:83-102): BR-128, the Question must exist and have QuestionEntity == "Session", else a Validation error (lines 90-97); BR-124, QuestionInvariants.EnsureAnswerValueMatchesQuestionType checks the supplied AnswerValue against the question's QuestionType (lines 100-101).
    4. Upsert (BR-107, …cs:49-57): read the current user's id from currentUserService.UserId!.Value (line 50), search the loaded answers for one with the same QuestionId and CreatedBy that is not soft-deleted (lines 51-52); if found, route to UpdateExistingAnswerAsync (calls Session.UpdateSessionQuestionAnswer), else CreateNewAnswerAsync (calls Session.AddSessionQuestionAnswer). Both save and return the mapped DTO.
  • Walkthrough
    • Primary constructor (line 19): IUnitOfWork, ICurrentUserService, SessionQuestionAnswerDTOMapper, ILogger<AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler>.
    • The two private helpers UpdateExistingAnswerAsync (…cs:104-117) and CreateNewAnswerAsync (…cs:119-131) each call the domain method, SaveChangesAsync().ConfigureAwait(false), log, and map, so the upsert branches converge on identical persistence handling.
    • [LoggerMessage] (…cs:133-134) emits "Question answer added to Session {SessionId}" from both branches.
    • The "current user already answered ⇒ update" rule means re-submitting feedback overwrites rather than duplicating, one answer per (user, question, session).
  • Why it's built this way: the deeper rules (service-session, status, event-published, question-type) can only be checked with the loaded aggregates, so they live in the handler/domain rather than the AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommandValidator (which only guards AnswerValue non-empty). "Who is the current user" is an application concern, so ICurrentUserService is read here, not in the entity. This is the one Conference handler that reads a sibling aggregate (Question) purely to validate.
  • Where it's used: injected into the SessionQuestionAnswersController; dispatched after AddSessionQuestionAnswerCommandValidator.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: QuestionEntity == "Session" and QuestionType are compared as bare strings in the handler/domain; there is no enum for these in this slice, so a typo would surface only at runtime as a validation failure.

SessionDTOMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.DTOs · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/DTOs/SessionDTOMapper.cs:14 · Level 8 · class (Mapperly, sealed partial)

  • What it is: the parent DTO mapper for the Session aggregate (Session → SessionDTO), which composes the three child mappers to project the session's nested collections.
  • Depends on: IEntityDTOMapper, Session / SessionDTO, and the three child mappers SessionSpeakerDTOMapper, SessionQuestionAnswerDTOMapper, SessionCategoryItemDTOMapper, plus Riok.Mapperly.Abstractions.
  • Concept reinforced, Mapperly [UseMapper] composition (ADR-001). [Rubric §1, SOLID] (each child collection's mapping is delegated to its own single-responsibility mapper) and [Rubric §12, Performance] (all source-generated, no reflection). Mapperly's [UseMapper] tells the generator: when you need to map a nested collection, call this injected mapper instead of generating a duplicate inline body, so the rule for, say, SessionSpeaker lives in exactly one place.
  • Walkthrough: a [Mapper] sealed partial class with a primary constructor taking the three child mappers (lines 14-17), each stored in a [UseMapper]-attributed private readonly field (lines 20-27). public partial SessionDTO MapToDTO(Session entity) (line 30) is Mapperly-generated and routes the child collections through the [UseMapper] fields; MapToDTOs (lines 33-37) is the same hand-written null-guarded collection wrapper as the child mappers. Because it takes ctor dependencies, it is DI-registered (unlike the parameterless child mappers Scrutor also registers).
  • Why it's built this way: composing one mapper per nesting level keeps each mapping rule single-sourced and testable, and lets the parent reuse the children that already exist for single-collection projections.
  • Where it's used: the session read/query path (and anywhere a full Session is returned to a client), and the create slice's CreateSessionHandler to project the created session; tested by SessionDTOMapperTests.

RemoveSessionCategoryItemCommand, RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerCommand, RemoveSessionSpeakerCommand, UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerCommand

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · …Sessions.UseCases.* · Level 7 · record (sealed)

The four session child-management commands, the remove/update half. All are positional sealed records that implement ICacheInvalidating with the same CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Session).FullName}:", so any one of them, on success, tells the CachingCommandDecorator to evict the whole session cache namespace. (Their additive siblings, the AddSession* commands, are taught with the create/add slices of this chapter.)

Type File:Line Params · what it carries
RemoveSessionCategoryItemCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionCategoryItem/RemoveSessionCategoryItemCommand.cs:12 SessionId, SessionCategoryItemId
RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionQuestionAnswer/RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:13 SessionId, SessionQuestionAnswerId
RemoveSessionSpeakerCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionSpeaker/RemoveSessionSpeakerCommand.cs:12 SessionId, SessionSpeakerId
UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerCommand MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/UpdateSessionQuestionAnswer/UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:15 SessionId, SessionQuestionAnswerId, AnswerValue
  • What they are: the immutable input records for four CQRS commands against a Session aggregate: detach a category-item association, detach a question answer, detach a speaker association, and edit an existing answer's text. Each names its target session plus the child id (and, for the update, the new AnswerValue string).
  • Depends on: ICacheInvalidating (the marker the caching decorator reads); Session only for the typeof(Session).FullName cache-prefix string; the identifier-type aliases (SessionIdentifierType, SessionCategoryItemIdentifierType, SessionQuestionAnswerIdentifierType, SessionSpeakerIdentifierType).
  • Concept reinforced, cache invalidation declared on the command, not in the handler. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses one distinct command type per operation, each carrying its own cross-cutting contract) and [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (assesses paying for cache eviction only where data actually changed). The pattern itself is taught with the AddSession* siblings and ICacheInvalidating; the key point here is that all four compute the same type-level prefix ({typeof(Session).FullName}:, e.g. RemoveSessionCategoryItemCommand.cs:17), so changing any part of a session, its category items, its speakers, its answers, evicts the session read cache uniformly. The prefix is derived from the type, never from the instance, so eviction is namespace/tag-based, not keyed to one session id.
  • Walkthrough: each is a positional sealed record with a single expression-bodied property: public string CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Session).FullName}:"; (the only body member). Note the three Remove commands carry two ids and no payload; Update adds the string AnswerValue it will write (UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerCommand.cs:18). None of them implement ITransactional, a single aggregate save is already atomic under one SaveChanges, so they don't opt into the transactional-decorator stage.
  • Why it's built this way: co-locating the cache contract with the command keeps the matching handler pure orchestration (load, mutate, save) and makes "this command touches the session cache" a compile-checked fact rather than a comment.
  • Where they're used: constructed by the Conference REST controllers (SessionCategoryItemsController, SessionQuestionAnswersController, SessionSpeakersController) and dispatched to the matching handlers below.

SessionCreateRequest

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Create/SessionCreateRequest.cs:10 · Level 7 · record class

  • What it is: the create-request DTO for a conference session. It doubles as the command for session creation: CreateSessionHandler is declared ICommandHandler<SessionCreateRequest, …>, so this request is dispatched directly through the command pipeline rather than being wrapped in a separate CreateSessionCommand.
  • Depends on: ICreateRequest (Level 0, the marker the generic create-entity pipeline keys off) and ICacheInvalidating (Level 0, so creating a session evicts the session cache); the Session entity (cache-prefix only); the id aliases SessionIdentifierType, EventIdentifierType, RoomIdentifierType.
  • Concept reinforced, the request-as-command DTO and targeted analyzer suppression. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses DTOs decoupled from the domain entity): this is the wire shape posted to the create endpoint, 16 init-only properties, flat, with no domain behavior; the domain factory Session.Create(...) is reached only via SessionCreateRequestMapper. [Rubric §15, Best Practices & Code Quality] (assesses justified, narrowly-scoped suppressions over blanket #pragma): LiveUrl? (line 47) and RecordingUrl? (line 51) each carry [SuppressMessage("Design", "CA1056:URI-like properties should not be strings", Justification = "Stored as string for Sessionize compatibility")], Sessionize exports these as opaque strings that may not parse as Uri, so the analyzer rule is suppressed on exactly those two members with an inline reason, not project-wide.
  • Walkthrough
    • record class (line 10) implementing ICreateRequest, ICacheInvalidating; CachePrefix => $"{typeof(Session).FullName}:" (line 13), same prefix as the child commands above, so all session writes share one cache namespace.
    • Id is get; init; of SessionIdentifierType (line 16) and defaults to 0 when the organizer omits it, that default is what CreateSessionHandler's manual-id allocation keys off.
    • Two required properties, Title (line 19) and EventId (line 63), are the only mandatory fields; the FluentValidation rules in SessionCreateRequestValidator enforce their content beyond mere presence.
    • The remaining properties are optional (Description, StartsAt?, EndsAt?, Status?, IsInformed, IsConfirmed, IsServiceSession, IsPlenumSession, LiveUrl?, RecordingUrl?, AccessibilityInfo?, ResourceLinks?, Duration?, RoomId?), mirroring the Sessionize-sourced fields a session can carry.
  • Why it's built this way: folding the request and the command into one type removes a near-empty wrapper record (the "request is the command" idiom you'll see across the create slices), while still implementing ICreateRequest so it could flow through the framework's generic create handler if a bespoke one weren't supplied, see ADR-001 for the manual/explicit-mapping stance that keeps the DTO and the entity separate.
  • Where it's used: posted to the Session create endpoint on SessionsController; consumed by SessionCreateRequestMapper and validated by SessionCreateRequestValidator; dispatched to CreateSessionHandler.

DeleteEventHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events.UseCases.Delete · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/UseCases/Delete/DeleteEventHandler.cs:16 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: a custom delete handler that overrides the generic delete pipeline for Event, because deleting an event must cascade the soft-delete to its Session aggregates (which the generic handler can't reach).
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, IEventCascadeDeletionDomainService (the domain service that decides the cascade), Event, Session, ILogger. Registers under ICommandHandler<DeleteEntityCommand<Event, EventIdentifierType>, Result>, i.e. it accepts the generic DeleteEntityCommand<TEntity, TIdentifierType>.
  • Concept introduced, cross-aggregate cascade orchestrated in the application layer via a domain service. [Rubric §4, DDD] (assesses aggregate boundaries and where cross-aggregate logic lives). An Event.Delete() already cascades to its owned children, rooms, event speakers, event answers, per BR-72, all inside one aggregate boundary. But a Session is a separate aggregate (its own identity and lifecycle), so the cascade to sessions (BR-127, BR-55) cannot live inside Event.Delete(). The decision that sessions should cascade is domain logic, so it lives in the IEventCascadeDeletionDomainService; the loading of two aggregates is an application concern, so it lives here.
  • Walkthrough
    • Load the event with its owned children tracked: GetByIdAsync(command.Id, includes: [Rooms, EventSpeakers, EventQuestionAnswers], asTracking: true) (lines 27-31). Null → Error.NotFound (lines 32-33).
    • BR-127: separately load all of that event's active sessions, each with their own children (SessionSpeakers, SessionQuestionAnswers, SessionCategoryItems), filtered where: s => s.EventId.Equals(entity.Id) && !s.IsDeleted and tracked (lines 36-41).
    • Hand both to the domain service: eventCascadeDeletionDomainService.CascadeDelete(entity, sessions) (line 44), which soft-deletes the sessions then the event and returns a combined Result.
    • On success, one SaveChangesAsync (line 47) commits the whole cascade atomically, then logs (line 48).
  • Why it's built this way: the split keeps the handler thin (fetch two aggregates, delegate, save) and the cascade rule expressive and unit-testable in the domain ([Rubric §14, Testability]: the service takes loaded entities, no EF). It registers under the same ICommandHandler<DeleteEntityCommand<Event,…>, Result> key the base controller's delete slot expects, transparently replacing the generic delete handler for Event only, a clean example of overriding generic behavior for one entity without forking the pipeline.
  • Where it's used: selected by the Conference module DI for Event deletes; invoked from EventsController's delete action.

EventLiveValidationService

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/EventLiveValidationService.cs:18 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: Conference's concrete implementation of IEventLiveValidationService, the contract the Engagement live layer (Happening Now, the session Live view, the presenter UI) calls to learn an event's or session's live window in UTC, its published flag, and, for a session, its assigned speakers, plenum flag, and the event's question-moderation default. It is the provider side of a cross-module dependency, the live-layer analogue of SessionBookmarkValidationService.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (typed repositories), Event, Session, SessionInvariants (the BR rules), Result / Error, and the interface it implements. It returns the two carrier records EventLiveInfo and SessionLiveInfo. Externals: BCL TimeZoneInfo, TimeOnly, DateTime.
  • Concept reinforced, the cross-module provider, plus server-side local-to-UTC live-window math. [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (assesses modules collaborating through an abstraction owned where it is needed but implemented where the data lives, so a module can be extracted). Engagement must not reference Conference's domain, so the contract IEventLiveValidationService lives in Conference's Shared layer, Engagement depends only on that interface, and Conference supplies this implementation. When the modules share a process, DI binds the interface to this class; when extracted, Engagement instead resolves the gRPC adapter over the wire (or a DisabledEventLiveValidationService stub when Conference is off), the consumer's code never changes (ADRs 007/008). The other concept worth internalising is the live-window computation (ComputeLiveWindowUtc, lines 99-115): the window is [StartDate 00:00 local, (EndDate + 1 day) 00:00 local) (an exclusive end at midnight after the last day), converted to UTC through the event's IANA time zone, the same math the home-page countdown uses to decide the Live phase, so UI and live layer agree on "is it live right now?". [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability]: every read here is untracked (asTracking: false), nothing mutates.
  • Walkthrough
    • GetEventLiveInfoAsync(eventId, ct) (lines 21-41): load the event untracked, no includes (lines 25-30); null → Error.NotFound sourced/targeted to Event (lines 32-36); compute the window and return new EventLiveInfo(conferenceEvent.IsPublished, startUtc, endUtc) (lines 38-40).
    • GetSessionLiveInfoAsync(sessionId, ct) (lines 44-97): load the session untracked with its SessionSpeakers included (lines 48-53); null → Error.NotFound (lines 55-59). Then apply the bookmark-eligibility rules so the live layer follows the same gate as bookmarking: BR-91 SessionInvariants.EnsureNotServiceSession (no lunch/break sessions, lines 63-65) and BR-49 SessionInvariants.EnsureStatusIsEligible (no declined/cancelled sessions, lines 67-69), each a Result short-circuit. Load the parent Event untracked by session.EventId (lines 71-76); null → Error.NotFound targeted to Event (lines 78-82). Compute the window, project the non-deleted speaker ids ([.. session.SessionSpeakers.Where(ss => !ss.IsDeleted).Select(ss => ss.SpeakerId)], lines 86-87), and return new SessionLiveInfo(conferenceEvent.Id, conferenceEvent.IsPublished, startUtc, endUtc, speakerIds, session.IsPlenumSession, conferenceEvent.QuestionModerationDefault) (lines 89-96), carrying the speaker rights (BR-236), plenum flag, and moderation default (BR-233) the presenter/live UI needs.
    • ComputeLiveWindowUtc(conferenceEvent) (lines 99-115): build startLocal/endLocal from StartDate/EndDate (line 101-102), then TimeZoneInfo.FindSystemTimeZoneById(conferenceEvent.TimeZone) and ConvertTimeToUtc (lines 106-107). A catch (TimeZoneNotFoundException) (lines 109-114) stays defensive for legacy rows: rather than fail the call, it treats the stored local times as UTC via DateTime.SpecifyKind(..., DateTimeKind.Utc), noting that EventInvariants.EnsureTimeZoneIsValid already guards writes.
  • Why it's built this way: this is the same extraction seam as the bookmark validator (ADR-007/008), an interface consumed by Engagement, implemented where the Event/Session data lives. Reusing SessionInvariants means the live layer and the bookmark path share one definition of "eligible session," and centralising the local-to-UTC window here keeps a single source of truth for the Live phase that both the countdown and the live layer read.
  • Where it's used: registered as IEventLiveValidationService in Conference Application DI; consumed in-process by Engagement's live layer, or exposed over gRPC by EventLiveValidationServiceGrpcAdapter when the modules run as separate services.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the TimeZoneNotFoundException fallback treats the stored local time as UTC, so a legacy row with an unrecognised time-zone id yields a window shifted by that zone's offset; the write-time EventInvariants guard prevents new rows from reaching that branch.

RemoveSessionCategoryItemHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.RemoveSessionCategoryItem · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionCategoryItem/RemoveSessionCategoryItemHandler.cs:13 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

Two mechanics worth internalising, both shared with the richer AddSessionQuestionAnswerHandler: the load uses an explicit includes: [nameof(Session.SessionCategoryItems)] with asTracking: true (lines 23-27) because the domain method walks the already-loaded child collection to find the join row to soft-delete and EF must be tracking to persist it; and the single SaveChangesAsync is the only touch of the database (line 34), stamping audit fields, capturing domain events, and writing the outbox, none of which the handler codes by hand ([Rubric §10, Cross-Cutting]). The save and the source-generated log run only inside the if (result.IsSuccess) branch (lines 32-36), so a no-op removal is neither persisted nor logged.
  • Walkthrough
    • Get the Session repository (line 22); GetByIdAsync(command.SessionId, includes: [SessionCategoryItems], asTracking: true) (lines 23-27). Null → Error.NotFound (lines 28-29).
    • entity.RemoveSessionCategoryItem(command.SessionCategoryItemId) (line 31), the aggregate does the removal and returns a Result.
    • On success, one SaveChangesAsync (line 34) and a source-generated info log via [LoggerMessage] LogCategoryItemRemovedFromSession (lines 35, 41-42); return result (line 38).
  • Why it's built this way: uniformity. Because validation, caching, transactions, audit, events, and outbox are all handled by the pipeline and SaveChangesAsync, a child-removal handler is a handful of lines, and the analyzers plus the Result pattern keep every handler the same shape ([Rubric §16, Maintainability]).
  • Where it's used: injected into SessionCategoryItemsController's delete action; selected by the CQRS pipeline for its command type.

RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerHandler, UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerHandler

RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerHandler MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionQuestionAnswer/RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:14 soft-delete a session answer (BR-52/BR-53)

  • What they are: the two "child answer handlers with ownership enforcement" for the Session aggregate: they load the session with its answers, check the caller may touch this answer, delegate to the aggregate's domain method, and save. (Their Event-side twins, RemoveEventQuestionAnswerHandler/UpdateEventQuestionAnswerHandler, share the identical shape but are outside this unit.)
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (repository + SaveChangesAsync), ICurrentUserService (who is calling, and their roles), Session and its SessionQuestionAnswer child, RoleNames, ILogger, and their respective commands above. Returns Result via ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>.
  • Concept introduced, application-layer ownership authorization (BR-52/BR-53). [Rubric §11, Security] (assesses authorization enforced at the right layer, with the current user as a first-class input). "May this user edit this row?" is not a domain invariant of Session, it depends on who is asking, so the check lives in the handler, not the aggregate. Both handlers run the same gate (RemoveSessionQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:34-42, UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerHandler.cs:34-42): find the targeted, non-deleted answer; if the caller is not an Organizer and the answer's CreatedBy is not the current UserId, return Error.Forbidden with code SessionQuestionAnswer.NotOwner (a 403). Organizers bypass the check (they may mutate any answer). This reuses the audit field CreatedBy (stamped centrally in SaveChanges) as the ownership signal, no separate "owner" column.
  • Walkthrough (both follow the canonical mutation shape; line numbers from UpdateSessionQuestionAnswerHandler.cs):
    • Resolve the typed repo and load the session with its answer collection tracked: GetByIdAsync(command.SessionId, includes: [nameof(Session.SessionQuestionAnswers)], asTracking: true, …) (lines 24-29), the include is mandatory because the domain method walks that collection and EF must be tracking it. Null session → Error.NotFound (lines 30-31).
    • Run the ownership gate (lines 34-42), as above.
    • Delegate to the aggregate: entity.RemoveSessionQuestionAnswer(id) / entity.UpdateSessionQuestionAnswer(id, command.AnswerValue) (line 44), the domain method is the one that re-validates and returns the Result.
    • On IsSuccess, the single unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(…) (line 47) commits, stamps audit fields, captures domain events, and writes the outbox; then a source-generated [LoggerMessage] records it (lines 48, 54-55). The handler never touches the DbContext directly.
  • Why it's built this way: uniformity ([Rubric §16, Maintainability]): every mutation handler is the same five-step method, so reviewers and analyzers keep them shaped alike, and the cross-cutting work (transaction, audit, events, outbox) is all below the handler. Ownership lives here rather than in the domain because "current user" is an application concern; the domain re-checks business validity (e.g. the answer exists / the value is well-formed) independently.
  • Where they're used: injected into SessionQuestionAnswersController's delete/update actions; selected by the CQRS pipeline for their command type.

RemoveSessionSpeakerHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.RemoveSessionSpeaker · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/RemoveSessionSpeaker/RemoveSessionSpeakerHandler.cs:13 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the command handler that detaches a SessionSpeaker join entity from its Session. It is the standard load-aggregate → call domain-method → save mutation, with one extra twist: it can find the owning session even when the caller didn't send the session id.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, Session (and its SessionSpeakers collection), ILogger, RemoveSessionSpeakerCommand; returns Result via ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult>. Note: unlike the answer handlers, it has no ICurrentUserService, removing a speaker is an organizer write guarded at the controller ([Authorize] role), not an ownership check.
  • Concept introduced, defensive parameter resolution for a quirky DELETE contract. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design] (assesses robust handling of optional/partial request data). The session-speaker DELETE endpoint takes the session id as an optional query parameter, but the UI's generic delete control sends only the join-entity id, so command.SessionId arrives as the default (0). The handler branches on that (RemoveSessionSpeakerHandler.cs:28): when SessionId is default, it resolves the owning session from the join id by querying repository.GetAllAsync(includes: [SessionSpeakers], where: s => s.SessionSpeakers.Any(ss => ss.Id == command.SessionSpeakerId), asTracking: true) (lines 30-35); otherwise it loads the session directly by id (lines 39-44). This is the same child-entity-delete shape that previously bit a sibling controller (a [FromQuery] parentId defaulting to 0 → 404); here it's handled defensively in the handler. Either way it then loads the SessionSpeakers collection tracked so the domain method can walk it.
  • Walkthrough
    • Get the Session repository (line 22).
    • Resolve the session: the SessionId == default query-by-join-id branch (lines 28-36) or the direct GetByIdAsync branch (lines 37-44). Null result → Error.NotFound (lines 46-47).
    • entity.RemoveSessionSpeaker(command.SessionSpeakerId) (line 49), the aggregate does the actual removal and returns a Result.
    • On success, one SaveChangesAsync (line 52) and a source-generated info log (lines 53, 59-60).
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the id-resolution in the handler (rather than forcing the UI to thread the session id everywhere) makes the generic delete control reusable and the endpoint forgiving of a missing optional query param. The aggregate still owns the what (removal + invariants); the handler only owns the fetch.
  • Where it's used: injected into SessionSpeakersController's delete action.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: when SessionId is unset the join-id lookup assumes SessionSpeakerId is globally unique (it is, a join-entity primary key); if two sessions could share a join id the FirstOrDefault (line 35) would be ambiguous, but that can't happen here.

SessionCreateRequestMapper

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Create/SessionCreateRequestMapper.cs:11 · Level 8 · sealed class

  • What it is: the seam between the SessionCreateRequest DTO and the Session domain entity. It implements IEntityRequestMapper<Session, SessionCreateRequest, SessionIdentifierType> and forwards the request's fields to the domain factory Session.Create(...).
  • Depends on: IEntityRequestMapper<TEntity, TCreateRequest, TIdentifierType> (Level 4); Session; Result.
  • Concept reinforced, explicit request→entity mapping through the domain factory (ADR-001). [Rubric §1, SOLID] / [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture]: the create handler depends on the interface IEntityRequestMapper, never on Session.Create directly, so the "how do I build an entity from a request?" logic is a swappable adapter. The single method CreateEntityAsync (…cs:15-34) does three things: ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(request); calls Session.Create(request.Id, request.Title, request.Description, request.StartsAt, request.EndsAt, request.Status, request.IsServiceSession, request.IsPlenumSession, request.LiveUrl, request.RecordingUrl, request.AccessibilityInfo, request.ResourceLinks, request.EventId, request.RoomId), which returns Result<Session> (the factory enforces the entity's invariants, so an invalid session can't be constructed); and wraps that in Task.FromResult because the mapping itself is synchronous but the port is async. Note the mapper deliberately does not forward IsInformed / IsConfirmed / Duration, Session.Create does not accept those, so they are set (if at all) by a later update, not at creation.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping the field-forwarding in a named mapper (rather than inline in the handler) is ADR-001's explicit-mapping stance: mapping is visible, compile-checked, and unit-testable, and the domain factory remains the single gate for validity. The Task.FromResult keeps the synchronous body conformant with the async interface without fabricating a thread hop.
  • Where it's used: resolved by DI as IEntityRequestMapper<Session, SessionCreateRequest, SessionIdentifierType> and injected into CreateSessionHandler.
