MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Create/SessionCreateRequestValidator.cs:7 · Level 8 · sealed class (FluentValidation)

  • What it is: the FluentValidation validator for SessionCreateRequest. It composes two reusable rule sets rather than restating field rules inline.
  • Depends on: FluentValidation's AbstractValidator<SessionCreateRequest>; the reusable rule classes SessionTitleRules<T> and SessionEventIdRules<T>.
  • Concept reinforced, composable, reusable validation via Include(...). [Rubric §24, Forms, Validation & UX Safety] (assesses validation that is present, applied before business logic, and not copy-pasted). The constructor (…cs:9-13) calls Include(new SessionTitleRules<SessionCreateRequest>(p => p.Title)) and Include(new SessionEventIdRules<SessionCreateRequest>(p => p.EventId)), each rule class is a parameterised, property-selector-driven AbstractValidator<T> that can be Include-d into any request that has a title / event-id, so the create and update validators share one definition of "a valid session title" and "a valid event id." This is the DRY counterpart to the single-rule child-command validators. The deeper, stateful checks (does the event exist? is the room cross-event?) are not here, they live in the handlers, because a stateless validator can't query.
  • Why it's built this way: extracting the per-field rules into reusable Include-able classes means a rule change (e.g. max title length) is made once and applies to every request that includes it, eliminating the classic "validators drift apart" bug.
  • Where it's used: auto-discovered by Scrutor; run by the validation stage of the command pipeline before CreateSessionHandler.

CreateSessionHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions.UseCases.Create · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/UseCases/Create/CreateSessionHandler.cs:16 · Level 9 · sealed partial class

  • What it is: the command handler for session creation. It dispatches off SessionCreateRequest directly (the request is the command), allocates an id when the caller omits one, builds the entity through the request mapper, persists it, and returns the mapped SessionDTO. It teaches how the create slice composes the framework's mapper + repository + unit-of-work, plus a domain-specific id-allocation wrinkle the simpler create handlers don't have.
  • Depends on: ICommandHandler<in TCommand, TResult> (Level 0); IUnitOfWork (Level 7) and its IRepository<TEntity, TIdentifierType>; IEntityRequestMapper<Session, SessionCreateRequest, SessionIdentifierType> (Level 4), concretely SessionCreateRequestMapper; SessionDTOMapper; Session and SessionInvariants; Result / Error; Microsoft.Extensions.Logging.
  • Concept reinforced, partial class + [LoggerMessage] source-generated logging, and app-assigned identity with a reserved range. [Rubric §13, Observability & Operability]: the sealed partial class (line 16) plus [LoggerMessage(Level = Information, Message = "Session {SessionId} created with title '{Title}'")] private static partial void LogSessionCreated(...) (lines 64-65) emit a zero-allocation, compile-checked log helper, the pattern on every handler. The genuinely interesting concept here is application-assigned PK allocation: a Session's integer primary key is its Sessionize id, so app-created sessions must claim ids that can never collide with a future Sessionize import. [Rubric §8, Data Architecture] (deliberate identity/key strategy): the handler reserves a high range [SessionInvariants.ManualIdRangeStart … SessionInvariants.ManualIdRangeEnd] for organizer-created sessions.
  • Walkthrough
    • Primary constructor (line 16): IUnitOfWork, IEntityRequestMapper<Session, SessionCreateRequest, SessionIdentifierType>, SessionDTOMapper, ILogger<CreateSessionHandler>.
    • HandleAsync (line 23):
      1. Id allocation when command.Id == default (i.e. the organizer omitted it, so it's 0, lines 32-48): query the repository for all existing sessions whose id falls in the manual range, with ignoreQueryFilters: true so soft-deleted rows still reserve their ids (lines 34-38); pick Max(id) + 1, or ManualIdRangeStart if the range is empty (lines 40-42); if that exceeds ManualIdRangeEnd return Error.Failure(... "Manual session ID range exhausted.") (lines 44-45); otherwise rewrite the command with the new id via the record with-expression: command = command with { Id = nextId } (line 47). An explicit caller-supplied id (the Sessionize path) skips this block entirely and is respected as-is.
      2. Build the entity via requestMapper.CreateEntityAsync(command, ct) → Result<Session> (line 50); early-return on failure (lines 51-52).
      3. Persist: repository.AddAsync(entity, ct) then unitOfWork.SaveChangesAsync(ct), both .ConfigureAwait(false) (lines 56-57).
      4. Log via the generated partial method (line 59) and return Result.Success(dtoMapper.MapToDTO(entity)) (line 61).
  • Why it's built this way: delegating entity construction to SessionCreateRequestMapper keeps the handler ignorant of how Session.Create(...) works; its only jobs are id allocation, persistence, and DTO projection ([Rubric §5, Vertical Slice], one self-contained slice that does not cross aggregate boundaries). The reserved high-id range is the pragmatic answer to "the PK is an external system's id": rather than switch to GUIDs or a separate key, organizer creates live in a window Sessionize will never reach, so import and manual create coexist without collision. ignoreQueryFilters: true on the range scan is essential, without it a soft-deleted session's id could be re-handed-out and then resurrected on a future import.
  • Where it's used: registered by ScanModuleApplicationServices in the Conference Application DI; injected into SessionsController (Conference API) and dispatched through the command pipeline.
  • Caveats / not-in-source: the range scan + Max + 1 is not concurrency-safe against two simultaneous organizer creates on its own; in practice the SaveChanges PK uniqueness constraint and the low volume of manual creates (organizer-only) make a collision a caught exception rather than silent corruption, but the source contains no explicit lock or transaction isolation note for this path.

EventNavigationPopulator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Events · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Events/EventNavigationPopulator.cs:11 · Level 10 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: the concrete, Event-specific navigation populator (ADR-002). It is a single primary-constructor call whose entire body is a list of three child descriptors telling the base how to bulk-load an event's Rooms, EventSpeakers, and EventQuestionAnswers, navigations EF Core cannot reach via .Include().

  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (passed through); the generic base DeclarativeNavigationPopulator<TEntity> (Level 9) and a typed array of ChildNavigationDescriptor<TEntity, TParentId, TChild, TChildId> (Level 9); each descriptor names one child entity type.

  • Concept reinforced, declarative navigation descriptors. The mechanism is taught at DeclarativeNavigationPopulator<TEntity> and ChildNavigationDescriptor; the job here is purely binding, declare that this populator manages the Event aggregate and list its three child navigations. The actual bulk-fetch-and-assign logic lives entirely in the base. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns] (Template Method via configuration: the base defines the algorithm, the subclass supplies the descriptor array rather than overriding virtual methods). [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (the Application layer imports no EF namespace, descriptors drive repository queries, never EF Include, which is exactly why the populator exists: it loads navigations EF Core can't reach via .Include(), e.g. across data-source boundaries, ADR-002).

  • Walkthrough: the whole class is the constructor plus its descriptor array (lines 11-37). Each ChildNavigationDescriptor initializer supplies four members, shown with the first one, Rooms:

    • PropertyName, the property-name string (nameof(Event.Rooms), line 17) the base uses to build NavigationMetadata and mark the property populated.
    • ParentKeySelector, e => e.Id (line 18), the parent aggregate's primary key (groups child rows by parent after the bulk fetch).
    • ChildForeignKeySelector, child => child.EventId (line 19), the child's FK column so the base can match children to their parent, all three descriptors key children on EventId.
    • AssignAction, (e, rooms) => e.SetRooms(rooms) (line 20), a delegate that hands the loaded children to the aggregate's setter, keeping assignment inside the domain model.

    The other two descriptors follow the same shape for EventSpeakers/SetEventSpeakers (lines 22-28) and EventQuestionAnswers/SetEventQuestionAnswers (lines 29-35).

  • Why it's built this way: ADR-002 mandates that the Application layer control eager-loading without taking an EF dependency. The base provides the generic machinery; this class is the per-aggregate configuration, one file beside the Event use-cases so the populator stays small.

  • Where it's used: registered via Scrutor INavigationPopulator<Event> scanning in the Conference module DI; resolved by the EntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> for Event (behind EventsController) when loading events with their child navigations.

  • Caveats / not-in-source: the AssignAction delegates call the aggregate's Set* methods; if a child collection is added or renamed on Event, the matching descriptor here must be updated to keep eager loading in sync.

SessionBookmarkValidationService

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Sessions · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/SessionBookmarkValidationService.cs:12 · Level 8 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: Conference's concrete implementation of ISessionBookmarkValidationService, the contract the Engagement module calls to ask "may this session be bookmarked?" and "what are this event's session ids?". It is the provider side of a cross-module dependency.
  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork, Session, SessionInvariants (the BR rules), Result, and the interface it implements (SessionBookmarkValidationService.cs:12).
  • Concept introduced, the cross-module provider (interface owned by the consumer, implemented by the owner). [Rubric §7, Microservices Readiness] (assesses modules collaborating through abstractions, not direct domain references, so a module can be extracted). Engagement needs to validate a session before bookmarking it, but it must not reference Conference's domain. So the contract ISessionBookmarkValidationService lives in Conference's Shared layer, Engagement depends only on that interface, and Conference supplies this implementation. When the modules run in one process, DI binds the interface to this class; when extracted, Engagement instead resolves a gRPC adapter over the wire (or a DisabledSessionBookmarkValidationService stub when Conference is off), the consumer's code never changes (ADRs 007/008).
  • Walkthrough
    • ValidateSessionForBookmarkAsync(sessionId, ct) (lines 15-39): load the session untracked (asTracking: false, includes: [], a read-only check, lines 19-24); null → Error.NotFound.WithSource(nameof(SessionBookmarkValidationService)).WithTarget(nameof(Session)) (lines 26-30). Then run two BR invariants in order: BR-91 SessionInvariants.EnsureNotServiceSession(session.IsServiceSession, ...) (service sessions can't be bookmarked, lines 33-35), and BR-49 SessionInvariants.EnsureStatusIsEligible(session.Status, ...) (only Accepted/null-status sessions, line 38). Each returns a Result, so a failure short-circuits with the right error.
    • GetSessionIdsByEventAsync(eventId, ct) (lines 42-54): untracked GetAllAsync(where: s => s.EventId == eventId) (lines 47-51), then projects to the id collection ([.. eventSessions.Select(s => s.Id)], line 53), used by Engagement to scope bookmark queries to an event.
  • Why it's built this way: keeping validation behind an interface owned where it's needed (Engagement) but implemented where the data lives (Conference) is the seam that makes the two modules independently deployable; the invariants are reused from the domain (SessionInvariants) so the bookmark check and the session lifecycle share one source of truth. Reads are untracked because nothing here mutates.
  • Where it's used: registered as ISessionBookmarkValidationService in Conference Application DI; consumed by Engagement's bookmark create flow (in-process) or exposed over gRPC by SessionBookmarksGrpcService / SessionBookmarkValidationServiceGrpcAdapter when extracted.

UserRegisteredHandler

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Users.IntegrationEventHandlers · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Users/IntegrationEventHandlers/UserRegisteredHandler.cs:39 · Level 8 · class (sealed partial)

  • What it is: the Conference-side subscriber to Identity's UserRegistered integration event; on each new registration it tries to auto-link the user to a matching Speaker (BR-207) and, on a hit, publishes SpeakerLinkedToUser back to Identity.
  • Depends on: IServiceScopeFactory (to open a per-event DI scope), IUnitOfWork, IIntegrationEventPublisher, Speaker, the Email value object, IRepository<TEntity, TIdentifierType>, ILogger, and the UserRegistered / SpeakerLinkedToUser event records. Implements IIntegrationEventHandler<in TIntegrationEvent> closed over UserRegistered (UserRegisteredHandler.cs:41).
  • Concept introduced, the integration-event consumer, scoped DI for a singleton handler, and idempotent eventual consistency. [Rubric §6, CQRS & Event-Driven] (assesses reliable, idempotent consumers that carry enough context). An IIntegrationEventHandler<T> is a singleton per framework convention (…cs:35-37 doc comment), so it cannot hold a scoped IUnitOfWork; instead it opens scopeFactory.CreateAsyncScope() per event (…cs:53) and resolves scoped services inside. The match is two-tier (…cs:117-177): first TryMatchByEmailAsync, the original BR-207 path, comparing the normalized Email value object (…cs:124-138), then a unique-name fallback for Sessionize-imported speakers whose Email is always null (the public Sessionize view/All endpoint omits PII, …cs:19-23 doc comment). The name fallback matches exact FirstName + LastName among unlinked speakers (LinkedUserId == null, …cs:157-163) and links only when exactly one candidate matches, so an ambiguous name collision is skipped rather than mis-linked (…cs:170-173).
  • Concept reinforced, crash-tolerant at-least-once handling. [Rubric §29, Resilience]. The whole body is wrapped in a best-effort try/catch (Exception ex) when (ex is not OperationCanceledException) (…cs:109-114): a failure must not propagate back through the broker, because the user-registration transaction has already committed in Identity, re-throwing would dead-letter a successful registration. At-least-once delivery (ADR-003) means this handler may re-run, so it is made idempotent: if the speaker is already linked to a different user it logs and returns (…cs:74-78); if already linked to this user it re-publishes SpeakerLinkedToUser (so Identity can resync) and returns without re-linking (…cs:82-88). The link is eventually consistent: the new user's first JWT lacks the speaker_id claim; it appears on the next token refresh after this handler completes (…cs:27-33 doc comment).
  • Walkthrough
    • ArgumentNullException.ThrowIfNull(integrationEvent) (line 49); open the async scope and resolve IUnitOfWork + IIntegrationEventPublisher (lines 53-55), then the Speaker repository (line 57).
    • Try email match, then (if null) name match, tracking which matchMode won (lines 59-65); no match → LogNoMatchingSpeaker and return (lines 67-71).
    • Idempotency gates (lines 74-88), then speaker.LinkUser(integrationEvent.UserId) (line 90), the aggregate method; failure → LogLinkFailed and return (lines 91-95).
    • SaveChangesAsync (line 100), then publish SpeakerLinkedToUser (lines 103-105) so Identity sets User.LinkedSpeakerId, and LogAutoLinked with its match mode (line 107). The comment at …cs:97-99 notes a rare unique-index race on Speaker.LinkedUserId (two concurrent matching registrations) surfaces as a DbUpdateException swallowed by the outer catch, the winning link stands. The seven [LoggerMessage] source-generated log methods live at …cs:179-198.
  • Why it's built this way: ADR-003 (outbox + at-least-once) demands idempotent, crash-tolerant consumers; the scope-per-event pattern is the standard way a singleton event handler borrows scoped EF state. The name fallback exists specifically because the public Sessionize endpoint strips PII, so email-only matching would never link imported speakers.
  • Where it's used: registered as a broker consumer in the Conference service host; fed by Identity's registration flow → outbox → broker. Its back-link event is handled by Identity's SpeakerLinkedToUserHandler.

SpeakerEntityQueryService

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application.Speakers · MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/SpeakerEntityQueryService.cs:15 · Level 9 · class (sealed)

  • What it is: a thin concrete subclass of EntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> for Speaker. Its only addition is a property map letting API consumers sort/filter on the DTO's computed FullName field.
  • Depends on: EntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> (the base, Level 8); IUnitOfWork, INavigationMetadataProvider, IEntityQueryPipeline, INavigationPopulator<in TEntity>, and the SpeakerDTOMapper, all forwarded to the base constructor (lines 15-22). Speaker/SpeakerDTO from Conference.
  • Concept introduced, DTOToEntityPropertyMap override for computed/compound sort fields. [Rubric §12, Performance & Scalability] (assesses server-side sort/filter that translates to SQL, not in-memory). The base EntityQueryService exposes a protected virtual IReadOnlyDictionary<string, string> DTOToEntityPropertyMap hook. The Speaker entity has no FullName column, it's a computed DTO property, so sorting by it through the API would fail entity-field validation. This subclass supplies a one-entry map ([nameof(SpeakerDTO.FullName)] = "(FirstName + \" \" + LastName)", lines 28-31) so the query pipeline renders FullName into the right ORDER BY/WHERE SQL fragment. [Rubric §9, API & Contract Design]: stable, DTO-named sort keys are decoupled from internal entity structure.
  • Walkthrough: the primary constructor forwards all five services to the base ctor (lines 21-22). A private static readonly PropertyMap dictionary is built once at class load (lines 28-31), and DTOToEntityPropertyMap => PropertyMap (line 34) overrides the hook. No other members.
  • Why it's built this way: static readonly computes the map once per appdomain, not per request. Making this a thin concrete subclass (rather than registering the base generic directly) is the DI seam: the container binds IEntityQueryService<Speaker, SpeakerDTO, SpeakerIdentifierType> to this type, which carries the non-default map.
  • Where it's used: registered as the Speaker query service in Conference Application DI; injected into SpeakersController.

ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator, SessionNavigationPopulator, SpeakerNavigationPopulator

MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application · Level 10 · class (sealed)

Type File:Line Children loaded
ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Categories/ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator.cs:11 CategoryItems (one collection)
SessionNavigationPopulator MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Sessions/SessionNavigationPopulator.cs:12 SessionSpeakers, SessionQuestionAnswers, SessionCategoryItems (three)
SpeakerNavigationPopulator MMCA.ADC/Source/Modules/Conference/MMCA.ADC.Conference.Application/Speakers/SpeakerNavigationPopulator.cs:11 SpeakerCategoryItems, SpeakerQuestionAnswers (two)

  • What they are: concrete, entity-specific implementations of the navigation-populator pattern (ADR-002), one per Conference aggregate root (Category, Session, Speaker). Each is a single primary-constructor call, the entire implementation is the list of child descriptors. Their fourth sibling for the Event aggregate, EventNavigationPopulator, has the identical shape and is taught elsewhere in this chapter.

  • Depends on: IUnitOfWork (passed through); the generic base DeclarativeNavigationPopulator<TEntity> (Level 9) and a typed array of ChildNavigationDescriptor<TEntity, TParentId, TChild, TChildId> (Level 9); each descriptor names a child entity, e.g. CategoryItem / SessionSpeaker / SessionQuestionAnswer.

  • Concept reinforced, declarative navigation descriptors. The mechanism is taught at DeclarativeNavigationPopulator<TEntity> and ChildNavigationDescriptor; the job here is purely binding, declare which aggregate this populator manages and list its child navigations. The actual bulk-fetch-and-assign logic lives entirely in the base. [Rubric §2, Design Patterns] (Template Method via configuration: the base defines the algorithm, the subclass supplies the descriptor array rather than overriding virtual methods). [Rubric §3, Clean Architecture] (the Application layer imports no EF namespace, descriptors drive repository queries, never EF Include, which is exactly why the populator exists: it loads navigations EF Core can't reach via .Include(), e.g. across data-source boundaries, ADR-002).

  • Walkthrough: each constructor has the same shape, shown with SessionNavigationPopulator (the richest, three children, SessionNavigationPopulator.cs:12-37):

    public sealed class SessionNavigationPopulator(IUnitOfWork unitOfWork)
              : DeclarativeNavigationPopulator<Session>(unitOfWork, [ descriptor1, descriptor2, descriptor3 ]) { }

    Each ChildNavigationDescriptor initializer supplies four members (shown for the SessionSpeakers descriptor, SessionNavigationPopulator.cs:16-22):

    • PropertyName, the property-name string (nameof(Session.SessionSpeakers), line 18) the base uses to build NavigationMetadata and mark the property populated.
    • ParentKeySelector, e => e.Id (line 19), the parent aggregate's primary key (groups child rows by parent after the bulk fetch).
    • ChildForeignKeySelector, child => child.SessionId (line 20; CategoryId /SpeakerId for the siblings), the child's FK column so the base can match children to their parent.
    • AssignAction, (e, sessionSpeakers) => e.SetSessionSpeakers(sessionSpeakers) (line 21, and siblings), a delegate that hands the loaded children to the aggregate's setter, keeping assignment inside the domain model (the aggregate decides what to do with the list, not the infrastructure layer).

    ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator is the simplest (one descriptor, CategoryItems, with the parent-id alias ConferenceCategoryIdentifierType and child => child.CategoryId, ConferenceCategoryNavigationPopulator.cs:15-21); SessionNavigationPopulator has three (SessionSpeakers, SessionQuestionAnswers, SessionCategoryItems, lines 16-36); SpeakerNavigationPopulator has two (SpeakerCategoryItems, SpeakerQuestionAnswers, SpeakerNavigationPopulator.cs:15-28).

  • Why they're built this way: ADR-002 mandates that the Application layer control eager-loading without taking an EF dependency. The base provides the generic machinery; these classes are the per-aggregate configuration, one file per aggregate root so each populator stays small and lives beside its aggregate's use-cases.

  • Where they're used: registered via Scrutor INavigationPopulator<TEntity> scanning in the Conference module DI; resolved by EntityQueryService<TEntity, TEntityDTO, TIdentifierType> (e.g. SpeakerEntityQueryService above) when loading entities with child navigations.

  • Caveats / not-in-source: the AssignAction delegates call the aggregate's Set* methods; if a child collection is added or renamed on the aggregate, the matching descriptor here must be updated to keep eager loading in sync.
